أعطاه
ولا يطلق على ما دونها. (السنبلي بدليل ما ذكر إلخ : فإن كلام الرسول لا يفسر بعضه بعضا. (القمر) وأراد بالفضل إلخ لأن الفضل لا يتصوّر بدون المماثلة، ولما كان المراد بالمماثلة المماثلة في القدر فالفضل لا يراد إلا الفضل على القدر. (القمر) الفضل على القدر إلخ : يعني لا بد لكون الفضل ربا من كون الشيء زائدا على القدر، أي نصف صاع، فإن قلّ عنه فالفضل فيه لا يضر كبيع حفنة بحفنتين، والحفنة بالضم ملء الكفين، ومنه حفنة من دقيق، وفي الحديث إنما نحن حفنة من حفنات ربّنا أي يسير بالإضافة إلى ملكه ورحمته . (السنبلي) على القدر: أي الكيل في المكيلات والوزن في الموزونات. (القمر) حتى يجوز إلخ لأن أقل القدر الشرعي نصف صاع، ولا قدر في الشرع في أقل من نصف صاع (القمر) في القدر أي الكيل في المكيلات والوزن في الموزونات.(القمر) حكم الأمر: وهو التسوية والمماثلة الواجبة (القمر) بين هذه الأموال أي الستة المذكورة في الحديث. (القمر) يقتضي أن تكون إلخ وإلا يلزم التكلف بالمحال إلا بالقدر والجنس أي بالاشتراك في القدر والاتحاد في .الجنس. (القمر) المماثلة الصورية فإنها عبارة عن التساوي في المعيار، وهو الكيل والوزن، فبالمعيار يتساوى الطول فيما له طول والعرض فيما له عرض (القمر) تقوم المماثلة المعنوية: فإن باتحاد الجنس يتشاكل المعاني. (القمر)
قوله: "مثلاً مثل"، فإن لم يوجد الجنس كالحنطة مع الشعير أو لم يوجد القدر كما في العدديات لم تشترط المساواة ولا يظهر الربا.
ويرد عليه أنا لا نسلّم أن المماثلة تثبت بالقدر والجنس فقط، بل لا بد أن تكون في الوصف أيضًا، وهو الجودة والرداءة، فأجاب بقوله : وسقطت قيمة الجودة بالنص، وهو قوله عليا: جيّدها ورديها سواء. *
هذا حكم النص، أي كون الداعي إلى وجوب التسوية هو القدر، والجنس ثابت بإشارة وحرمة الفضل النص لا بمجرد الرأي، فالمراد بهذا الحكم الثاني غير ما أريد بالحكم الأول؛ لأن الحكم الأول هو الحكم الشرعي، أعني وجوب التسوية، وهذا الحكم هو بمعنى مدلول النص شامل للحكم والعلة جميعًا.
حفنة بحفنتين من
الحنطة مثلاً،
أو لم يوجد القدر إلخ وصورة عدم وجدان القدر ووجدان الجنس كما في بيع والمراد بقوله: "العدديات ذوات القيم كما في بيع فرس جسيم بفرس حقير. (السنبلي) بل لا بد أن تكون إلخ : فإن الجودة عبارة عن كمال معنى المالية، والرداءة هو ضد الجودة فكيف يماثل الكامل الناقص، فيتوقف المماثلة على الاتحاد في الوصف أيضًا. (القمر) وهو قوله عليها جيدها: أي جيد الأشياء الستة المذكورة في الحديث ورديّها سواء، فلا بد من رعاية المماثلة في القدر في بيع الحنطة الجيدة بالحنطة الردية، ولا اعتبار للجودة والرداءة. (القمر) فالمراد إلخ: هذا جواب سؤال مقدر ، وهو أن المتبادر من ظاهر كلام المصنف له أن قوله هذا حكم النص، والداعي إليه إلخ، وقوله: هذا حكم النص مرادهما ،واحد فما الفائدة في إيراد قوله: وهذا الحكم مرتين؟ فأجاب الشارح بقوله: فالمراد إلخ (السنبلي)
ما أريد بالحكم الأول : أي في قوله السابق هذا حكم النص. (القمر)
قال الزيلعي في تخريج "الهداية": غريب، ومعناه يؤخذ من إطلاق حديث أبي سعيد رواه مسلم، قال: قال رسول الله : الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة، والبر بالبر، والشعير بالشعير، والتمر بالتمر، والملح بالملح مثلاً بمثل يدا بيد، فمن زاد أو استزاد فقد أربى الآخذ والمعطي فيه سواء. [إشراق الأبصار: ٢٩]
Chapter of Qiyas. Definition of Qiyas and its ruling. So the meaning is the obligation of sale with the condition of equality and similitude, not the obligation of the sale itself. And He meant by 'like' the quantity, meaning measurement in measured items and weight in weighed items. By evidence of what is mentioned in another hadith: 'measure for measure'. And He meant by 'excess' in His statement: 'and the excess is usury' the excess over quantity, not the excess itself, so it is permissible to sell a handful for two handfuls, and so on until it reaches half a sa'. So the ruling of the text became the obligation of equality between them in quantity, then prohibition based on the two similars being lost in the ruling of the command, meaning wherever equality is lost, prohibition is established. And this is the ruling of the text. And the motivator i.e. the obligation of equality to it i.e. the effective cause (illa) that motivates the obligation of equality is quantity and genus; because obligating equality in quantity between these assets requires that they be similar equals, and they will not be so except by quantity and genus, i.e. similar equals. Because similitude is established by form and meaning, and that is by quantity and genus. By quantity formal similitude is established, and by genus meaningful similitude is established. And genus is indicated by His statement: 'wheat for wheat', and quantity is indicated by the condition of equality. So it is as if He said: When you proceed to sell wheat for wheat, observe similitude and sell in a state of equality, not otherwise. (al-Qamar) 'quantity etc.' Know that quantity according to jurists in measured and weighed items is not absolute, but half a sa' and above; it is not applied to what is below it. (al-Sunbulī) 'by evidence of what is mentioned etc.' For the speech of the Messenger does not interpret some parts by others. (al-Qamar) 'And He meant by excess etc.' Because excess is inconceivable without similitude, and since the intended similitude is similitude in quantity, 'excess' is only meant as excess over quantity. (al-Qamar) 'excess over quantity etc.' Means that for excess to be usury, the thing must be in excess over the quantity, i.e. half a sa'. If it is less than that, then the excess therein is not harmful, like selling a handful for two handfuls. And 'handful' (hafnah) means the fill of two palms. (al-Sunbulī) 'over quantity' i.e. measurement in measured items and weight in weighed items. (al-Qamar) 'until it is permissible etc.' Because the minimum legal quantity is half a sa', and there is no legal quantity in less than half a sa'. (al-Qamar) 'in quantity' i.e. measurement in measured items and weight in weighed items. (al-Qamar) 'ruling of the command' i.e. the obligatory equality and similitude (al-Qamar) 'between these assets' i.e. the six mentioned in the hadith. (al-Qamar) 'requires that they be etc.' Otherwise it would necessitate undertaking the impossible. Only by quantity and genus i.e. by sharing in quantity and union in genus. (al-Qamar) 'formal similitude' is equality in standard measure, which is measurement and weight. By the standard, length becomes equal in things having length, and width in things having width. (al-Qamar) 'meaningful similitude is established' for by unity of genus, meanings become similar. (al-Qamar) His statement: 'like for like'. For if genus is not present, like wheat with barley, or quantity is not present, as in countable items, then equality is not required and usury does not appear. And it is objected: We do not concede that similitude is established only by quantity and genus; rather it must also be in the description, i.e. quality and defect. So he replied by saying: And the value of quality is dropped by the text, which is His statement (peace be upon him): Its good and its bad are equal. * This is the ruling of the text, i.e. that the motivator for the obligation of equality is quantity and genus established by indication, and the prohibition of excess is by the text, not by mere opinion. So what is meant by this second ruling is different from what was meant by the first ruling; because the first ruling is the legal ruling, namely the obligation of equality, and this ruling is in the sense of the indication of the text, encompassing both ruling and cause together. A handful for two handfuls of wheat, for example, or absence of quantity, etc. And the picture of absence of quantity with presence of genus is as in selling a huge horse for a small horse. (al-Sunbulī) 'Rather it must be etc.' For quality is the perfection of the meaning of monetary value, and defect is the opposite of quality, so how can the perfect be similar to the deficient? Thus similitude depends on unity in description as well. (al-Qamar) 'And it is His statement (peace be upon him): its good' i.e. the good of the six items mentioned in the hadith and its bad are equal, so similitude in quantity must be observed in selling good wheat for bad wheat, and quality and defect are not considered. (al-Qamar) 'So what is meant etc.' This is the answer to an implicit question: that what appears from the author's statement is that his saying 'this is the ruling of the text' and 'the motivator to it etc.' and his saying 'this is the ruling of the text' have the same meaning, so what is the benefit of repeating 'and this ruling' twice? The commentator answered with his statement 'so what is meant etc.' (al-Sunbulī) 'what was meant by the first ruling' i.e. in his previous statement 'this is the ruling of the text'. (al-Qamar) Al-Zayla'i said in Takhrij al-Hidayah: It is gharib (unfamiliar), and its meaning is taken from the absolute meaning of the hadith of Abu Sa'id narrated by Muslim, who said: The Messenger of Allah said: Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, hand to hand; whoever increases or asks for increase has committed usury, the taker and the giver are equal in it. [Ishraq al-Absar: 29]
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of qiyas and its application in deriving the ruling of riba (usury). The author explains that the command in the hadith for sale with equality and similitude does not obligate the sale itself but rather the condition of equality. The key elements for similitude are quantity (qadr) and genus (jins). Quantity is determined by measurement (kayl) for measured items and weight (wazn) for weighed items. The minimum quantity to trigger riba is half a sa'. The genus is indicated by the type of commodity (e.g., wheat with wheat). The passage then addresses an objection: some argue that similitude also requires consideration of quality (joudah) and defect. The Hanafi response, based on the hadith 'the good and the bad are equal,' is that quality is not a factor in riba; only quantity and genus matter. The commentator further clarifies the difference between two uses of 'ruling of the text' in the commentary, explaining that the first refers to the legal obligation of equality, while the second refers to the indication of the text that includes both the ruling and the cause. The passage concludes with a citation from al-Zayla'i's Takhrij al-Hidayah, quoting the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that lists the six ribawi commodities.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): The process of deriving a legal ruling for a new case from an original case due to shared effective cause ('illa).
القدر (al-qadr): The standard measure (kayl/wazn) for ribawi items, with a minimum of half a sa'.
الجنس (al-jins): The category of commodity (e.g., wheat, barley) that determines genus for riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what is the minimum quantity (qadr) that triggers riba in measured items?
A) Any excess, no matter how small
B) Half a sa' and above
C) One sa' exactly
D) There is no minimum; all excess is riba

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school derives that riba only pertains to excess in quantity within the same genus, based on the hadith's explicit command for similitude and the supplementary hadith that drops quality.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Definition and Ruling of Qiyas with the Example of Riba
usul_definition: defines Qiyas through the riba example and establishes its validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Qiyas, identify its conditions (jins and qadr), and apply the derivation chain from the Quranic command and hadith to new cases.

Core Idea
Qiyas extends a ruling to new cases sharing the same cause (illa); riba's prohibition depends on genus and measure, not quality.

This passage introduces Qiyas (analogical reasoning) as a method for deriving legal rulings beyond the explicit texts. Using the prohibition of riba in six commodities, it demonstrates how the cause (illa) of measure and genus is abstracted and applied to other items like rice. The text also addresses an objection regarding quality, confirming that it is irrelevant. Finally, it anchors Qiyas in the Quranic command 'fai'tabiru' (take admonition).

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling and its cause
The hadith prohibits disparity in barter of six items (gold, silver, etc.) when exchanged like for like, hand to hand. The cause is the combination of same genus (jins) and equal measure (qadr).
These conditions are essential for the prohibition of riba in the Hanafi school.
2
Recognize the objection about quality
Someone objects that similarity also requires equality in quality (jooda). The text replies using the hadith 'its good and its bad are equal,' which drops the value of quality.
This step shows that the cause is limited to measure and genus, not subjective attributes.
3
Abstract the cause for Qiyas
The passage explains that the 'ruling of the text' includes both the legal ruling (obligation of equality) and the cause (measure and genus). The second mention of 'ruling' refers to this combined implication.
This abstraction allows the ruling to be extended to new cases.
4
Apply Qiyas to new items like rice
Since rice is a measured item like wheat (same genus and measure), the same prohibition of disparity applies. The text states 'we found rice and other things to be equal examples' and thus must establish the ruling.
This is a direct application of Qiyas: from wheat (asl) to rice (far') via the cause of measure and genus.
5
Verify the Quranic basis for Qiyas
The passage concludes by linking legal Qiyas to the Quranic verse 'fai'tabiru ya uli al-absar' (So take admonition, O you with insight), showing that Qiyas is a method commanded by Allah.
This verse provides the epistemological foundation for analogical reasoning in Hanafi usul.

(القمر)
Chapter of Qiyas. Definition of Qiyas and its ruling. His statement: "like for like." If the genus is not found, as with wheat and barley, or if the measure is not found, as in countable items, equality is not required and riba does not appear. It is objected that we do not accept that similarity is established by measure and genus only; rather it must also be in the attribute, which is quality and deficiency. He answered by saying: The value of quality is dropped by the text, which is his statement (peace be upon him): "Its good and its bad are equal." This is the ruling of the text, i.e., that the reason for necessitating equality is the measure, and the genus is established by indication, and the prohibition of excess is from the text, not mere opinion. So what is meant by this second ruling is different from what is meant by the first ruling; because the first ruling is the legal ruling, i.e., the obligation of equality, and this ruling is in the sense of the implication of the text including both the ruling and the cause together. A handful for two handfuls of wheat, for example, or if the measure is not found, etc., and the picture of not finding the measure while finding the genus is as in the sale of a valuable horse for a worthless horse. (al-Sanabli) Rather it must also be, etc.: For quality is the perfection of the meaning of value, and deficiency is the opposite of quality. How can the perfect be similar to the deficient? So similarity depends on unity in the attribute as well. (al-Qamar) And his statement "its good and its bad are equal": i.e., the good of the six items mentioned in the hadith and their bad are equal, so consideration of similarity in measure must be observed in the sale of good wheat for bad wheat, and quality and deficiency are not considered. (al-Qamar) So what is meant, etc.: This is the answer to an implied question, that the apparent meaning of the author's statement is that his saying "this is the ruling of the text" and his saying "the reason for it" etc. are one and the same. So what is the benefit of repeating "and this ruling" twice? The commentator answered by saying: So what is meant, etc. (al-Sanabli) What is meant by the first ruling: i.e., in his previous statement "this is the ruling of the text." (al-Qamar) Al-Zayla'i said in Takhrij al-Hidayah: Gharib, and its meaning is taken from the absolute nature of the hadith of Abu Sa'id narrated by Muslim, who said: The Messenger of Allah said: Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, hand to hand. Whoever increases or asks for increase has committed riba, the giver and the receiver are equal in it. [Ishraq al-Absar: 29] And we found rice and other things to be equal examples, so excess over similarity in them would be excess free from [the existence of measure and genus]. i.e., items of equal measures. These equal examples are the measured items like rice and others from among the compensations in a sales contract, like the ruling of the text without any difference, so we must establish it, i.e., establish the ruling of the text, which is the obligation of equality and the prohibition of riba regarding other than the six items and weighed items, whether it is food or not food, on condition of the existence of measure and genus. Upon the method of consideration (i'tibar) commanded in His statement: "So take admonition" (al-Hashr: 2), and it is like the punishments: i.e., this legal qiyas is like the consideration of punishments that befell the disbelievers, for Allah said: "He it is Who drove out those who disbelieved from among the People of the Book from their homes at the first gathering. You did not think that they would go out, and they thought that their fortresses would protect them from Allah. But Allah came upon them from where they least expected, and cast terror into their hearts, [so that] they destroyed their houses with their own hands and the hands of the believers. So take admonition, O you with insight." (al-Hashr: 2) And what is meant by the People of the Book is the Jews of Banu Nadir, who made a covenant with the Messenger of Allah that they would not be hostile to him when he came to Medina. That we found rice, etc.: When the author finished explaining the ruling and cause of the original case, he began to explain the branch case to complete the qiyas, so he said: And we found, etc. The method of completion is that rice and other similar items are among the measured items like wheat, so equality is required in exchange for its own genus, and disparity is prohibited due to sharing in measure. This is the explanation of qiyas in legal rulings, and it is like the qiyas in the descent of vengeance and punishment due to the cause of disobedience. So the author explained it by saying: And it is like the punishments. This is the summary of what is in al-Tanwir. (al-Sanabli) and other measured and weighed items like gypsum and iron. (al-Qamar) Equal examples: i.e., things that agree in genus and are equal in measure. (al-Qamar) Like the ruling of the text: i.e., in the six items mentioned in the hadith. (al-Qamar) So we must establish it: i.e., due to sharing in the cause, i.e., measure with genus. (al-Qamar) This qiyas: i.e., the qiyas we mentioned regarding rice and others. (al-Qamar) For the first gathering: i.e., at the time of the first gathering, i.e., the first gathering of the army of Islam. Al-Baydawi said: i.e., at the first expelling them from the Arabian Peninsula, for they had not suffered such humiliation before. (al-Qamar) For the first gathering, etc. He said in al-Tanwir: This was the first gathering for the Jews; then after that they underwent a second gathering at the time of Caliph Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) when the army of Islam arrived, and the Jews left the place and settled there. (al-Sanabli) That they would not be hostile to him: i.e., that they would not be opponents to him. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on Usul al-Fiqh, specifically the chapter on Qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author begins by stating the definition and ruling of Qiyas, explaining that it is a method of extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared cause (illa). He uses the example of riba in the six commodities (gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt) mentioned in the hadith. The conditions for riba are that the two items must be of the same genus (jins) and exchanged in equal measure (qadr). If either condition is missing, riba does not apply. The text then addresses an objection: some argue that equality also requires equality in quality (jooda/rada'a), but the author replies that the hadith explicitly states 'its good and its bad are equal,' meaning quality is irrelevant. The commentator (al-Sanabli) clarifies that the 'ruling of the text' refers to the legal obligation of equality, while the second mention of 'ruling' refers to the implication of the text including both the ruling and the cause. The passage then extends the ruling to other items like rice through Qiyas: since rice is a measured item like wheat, it shares the cause (measure and genus), so the same prohibition of disparity applies. Finally, the author connects this legal Qiyas to the Quranic verse 'So take admonition, O you with insight' (al-Hashr:2), which commands believers to derive lessons from past events. This shows that Qiyas is a valid method of reasoning based on divine command.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared cause (illa).
المماثلة (al-mumathala): Equality in measure and genus, which is required for the prohibition of riba in barter transactions.
الجنس (al-jins): Genus: the category/type of commodity (e.g., wheat, gold). For riba, same genus triggers equality requirement.
القدر (al-qadr): Measure: the quantity or weight of the commodity. Equality in measure is necessary for barter of same genus.
العلة (al-illa): The cause or effective reason that triggers the ruling. Here, the illa for riba is the combination of genus and measure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the context of riba, what are the two conditions necessary for the prohibition of disparity (tafadul) in barter exchanges according to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage?
A) Genus (jins) and quality (jooda)
B) Genus (jins) and measure (qadr)
C) Measure (qadr) and quality (jooda)
D) Hand-to-hand exchange and quality (jooda)

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a valid source of law rooted in the Quranic command to take admonition and the hadith on riba; its correct application requires identifying the precise cause (illa) of the original ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Definition and Essential Conditions of Qiyas
Defining qiyas and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of qiyas and identify its two necessary conditions: existence of quantity (qadr) and genus (jins).

Core Idea
Qiyas transfers a ruling only when the new case shares both genus and measurable quantity with the original.

This passage introduces the essential definition of qiyas as analogical reasoning that establishes the ruling of a textual case in a new case. The author uses the example of rice and other measurable goods to illustrate that the analogy depends on two conditions: quantity (qadr) and genus (jins). Without these, the ruling cannot be extended.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the central definition
Find the phrase that defines what qiyas aims to achieve. It is 'إثبات حكم النص في الفرع' (establishing the ruling of the text in the branch).
This is the core of analogical reasoning.
2
2. Extract the conditions
Look for the phrase 'بشرط وجود القدر والجنس' (on condition of existence of quantity and genus). These are the two prerequisites for applying qiyas in this context.
They ensure the similarity is sufficient.
3
3. Understand the 'illah
The effective cause ('illah) that connects the original and the branch is the combination of quantity and genus. The commentary explains that excess in similarity is free from reason due to these factors.
The 'illah is what justifies the transfer.
4
4. Know the ruling transferred
The ruling from the original text is the obligation of equality (wujub al-musawat) and prohibition of disparity (hurmat al-tafadul) regarding riba. This applies to the branch case when conditions are met.
This is the legal effect (athar) of qiyas.

ووجدنا الأرز وغيره أمثالاً متساوية، فكان الفضل على المماثلة فيها فضلاً خاليًا عن لوجود القدر والجنس أي ذوات الأمثال هذه الأمثال المتساوية المكيلات الأرز وغيره من العوض في عقد البيع مثل حكم النص بلا تفاوت فلزمنا إثباته، أي إثبات حكم النص، وهو وجوب المساواة وحرمة الربا فيما عدا الأشياء الستة والموزونات، سواء كان مطعوماً أو غير مطعوم بشرط وجود القدر والجنس. على طريق الاعتبار المأمور به في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْتَبِرُوا﴾، وهو نظير المثلات أي هذا القياس الشرعي نظير اعتبار العقوبات النازلة بالكفار، فإن الله تعالى قال: ﴿هُوَ الَّذِي أَخْرَجَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا مِنْ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ مِنْ دِيَارِهِمْ لِأَوَّلِ الْحَشْرِ مَا ظَنَنتُمْ أَنْ يَخْرُجُوا وَظَنُّوا أَنَّهُمْ مَانِعَتُهُمْ حُصُونُهُمْ مِنَ اللَّهِ فَأَتَاهُمُ اللَّهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ لَمْ يَحْتَسِبُوا وَقَذَفَ فِي قُلُوبِهِمُ الرُّعْبَ يُخْرِبُونَ بُيُوتَهُمْ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ وَأَيْدِي الْمُؤْمِنِينَ فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الْأَبْصَارِ﴾ (الحشر: ٢) والمراد بأهل الكتاب يهود النضير حيث عاهدوا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن لا يكونوا مخاصمين عليه حين قدم المدينة، أن ووجدنا الأرز إلخ لما فرغ المصنف له عن بيان حكم الأصل وعلته شرع في بيان الفرع ليتم القياس ويكمل فقال: ووجدنا إلخ وطريقة الإتمام والتكميل: أن الأرز وغيره من قبيل المكيلات مثل الحنطة، فيلزم المساواة في مقابله من جنسه ويحرم التفاضل بسبب المشاركة في الكيل، هذا بيان القياس في الأحكام الشرعية، وهو مثل القياس في نزول النقمة والعذاب بعلة المعصية فبينه المصنف بقوله : وهو نظير المثلات هذا خلاصة ما في "التنوير". (السنبلي) وغيره من المكيلات والموزونات كالجص والحديد. (القمر) أمثالاً متساوية: أي أشياء متوافقة جنسًا ومتساويًا قدراً. (القمر) مثل حكم النص: أي في الأشياء الستة المنصوص عليها في الحديث. (القمر) فلزمنا إثباته أي بسبب المشاركة في العلة أي القدر مع الجنس. (القمر) هذا القياس أي القياس الذي ذكرنا في الأرز وغيره. (القمر) لأوّل الحشر : أي في وقت أول الحشر، أي أول جمع عسكر الإسلام، قال البيضاوي: أي في أول حشرهم من جزيرة العرب؛ إذ لم يصبهم هذا الذلّ قبل ذلك. والحشر إخراج جمع من مكان إلى آخر، وبنو نضير حيّ من اليهود ومن أولاد هارون عليه السلام، كذا في بعض حواشي "تفسير البيضاوي". (القمر) لأول الحشر إلخ قال في "التنوير" : هذا لليهود كان أول الحشر، ثم بعد ذلك أخذوا بالحشر الثاني في زمان أمير المؤمنين عمر رضي الله عنه وقت وصول عسكر الإسلام حيث ذهب اليهود من المكان وأقاموا فيه (السنبلي) أن لا يكونوا عليه أي أن لا يكونوا مخاصمين عليه. (القمر)
فنقضوا العهد في وقعة أحد، فأمرهم صلى الله عليه وسلم بالخروج من المدينة فاستمهلوا عشرة أيام وطلبوا الصلح، فأبى عليهم إلا الجلاء، فأخرجهم الله من المدينة لأوّل الحشر والإخراج حال كونكم يا أيها المسلمون ما ظننتم أن يخرجوا، وظنّوا أي اليهود أنهم مانعتهم حصونهم من الله، فأتاهم الله أي عذابه وحكمه بالجلاء من حيث لم يحتسبوا ذلك، وقذف أي ألقى الله في قلوبهم الرعب حالَ كونهم يُخربون بيوتهم بأيديهم وأيدي المؤمنين لحاجتهم إلى الخشب والحجارة، فحملوا أثقالهم هذه على حمال كثيرة، وخرجوا منها، واستوطنوا بخيبر، ثم أخرجهم عمر من خيبر إلى الشام، هذا تفسير الآية. فالإخراج من الديار عقوبة كالقتل حيث سوى بينهما في قوله: ﴿وَلَوْ أَنَّا كَتَبْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ أَنِ اقْتُلُوا أَنْفُسَكُمْ أَوِ اخْرُجُوا مِنْ دِيَارِكُمْ مَا فَعَلُوهُ إِلَّا قَلِيلٌ مِنْهُمْ﴾ (النساء: ٦٦) والكفر يصلح داعيًا إليه، فكلما وجد الكفر يترتب عليه الإخراج وأول الحشر يدل على تكرار هذه العقوبة، في وقعة أحد التي هزم المسلمون فيها. (القمر) فأمرهم إلخ وحاصرهم إحدى وعشرين ليلة.(القمر) ما ظننتم إلخ لشدة بأسهم ووثاقة حصولهم. (القمر) من حيث لم يحتسبوا فإنهم كانوا يحسبون أنهم يغلبون على المؤمنين. (القمر) حال كونهم يُخربون إلخ أي يخربون بواطن بيوتهم بأيديهم، والمؤمنون يُخربون ظواهر لما نقضوا العهد فوقعوا أسبابًا لتخريب المؤمنين، فكأنهم أمروا المسلمين وكلّفوهم بهذا التخريب، ولهذا قال الله تعالى: ﴿يُحْرِبُونَ بُيُوتَهُمْ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ وَأَيْدِي الْمُؤْمِنِينَ﴾ (الحشر : ٢) (القمر) بينهما : أي بين القتل والإخراج فالتسوية والتخيير بينهما دليل على أنهما بمنزلة واحدة. (القمر) ولو أنا كتبنا عليهم أي على ضعفاء الإسلام أن مفسرة ﴿اقْتُلُوا أَنْفُسَكُمْ أَوِ اخْرُجُوا مِنْ دِيَارِكُمْ﴾ (النساء: ٦٦) كما كتبنا على بني إسرائيل ﴿مَا فَعَلُوهُ﴾ (النساء: ٦٦) أي المكتوب عليهم إلا ﴿قَلِيلٌ مِنْهُمْ﴾ (النساء: ٦٦) (القمر) داعيًا إليه أي إلى الإخراج الذي هو كالقتل. (القمر) يدل إلخ إذ الأول لا بد له من ثانٍ، وفيه ما قيل من أن المعتبر في الأولية عدم تقدّم غيره، لا وجود آخر متأخرا عنه، فتأمل. (القمر) أخرجه الحاكم وصححه وابن مردويه والبيهقي في الدلائل بطرق وألفاظ مختلفة عن عائشة [إشراق الأبصار: ٢٩] وغيرها.
Chapter of Qiyas. Definition of Qiyas and its ruling. And we found rice and others as equal parallels, so excess in similarity was excess free from [reason] due to existence of quantity and genus, meaning things with parallels these equal parallels, the measured things rice and others from the consideration in sale contract like the ruling of the text without difference, so we are required to prove it, i.e., to prove the ruling of the text, which is obligation of equality and prohibition of riba except for the six specified things and weighed things, whether edible or not edible, on condition of existence of quantity and genus. On the method of i'tibar commanded in His statement: 'So take a lesson, O people of vision' (Al-Hashr:2), and it is analogous to the punishments, i.e., this legal qiyas is analogous to considering the punishments descending upon the disbelievers, for Allah said: 'He it is Who drove out those who disbelieved from among the People of the Book from their homes at the first gathering...' (Al-Hashr:2) ... (continues with commentary on the verse and analogy
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a definition of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It opens by declaring the chapter on qiyas and then immediately defines its ruling: qiyas establishes the same legal norm (hukm) for a new case (far') as for the original case (asl) due to a shared effective cause ('illa). The commentator uses the example of rice (and other foodstuffs) analogized to the six specified commodities in the hadith on riba. The key condition for qiyas in this case is the presence of both quantity (qadr, meaning standard measure like weight or volume) and genus (jins, meaning the same category). If these two are present, then the ruling of the original text—obligation of equality and prohibition of disparity—applies to the new case. The author then justifies qiyas by quoting the Quranic verse 'fai'tabiru' (so take a lesson) from Surah al-Hashr, arguing that just as the Quran commands considering historical punishments to deduce consequences of sin, so too Islamic law commands considering evidence to deduce rulings. The verse about the expulsion of Banu Nadir is then expounded to show that expulsion (ikhraj) is a punishment analogous to death in some contexts, and that the occurrence of the cause (kufr) leads to the effect (expulsion). This supports the principle that patterns (muthulat) discerned from revealed texts can be extended by analogy. The commentary relies on classical sources like al-Tanwir, Tafsir al-Baydawi, and glosses by al-Sunbuli and al-Qamar. Throughout, the text maintains a Hanafi perspective, emphasizing that 'i'tibar (taking lesson) is the basis for qiyas.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: transferring the ruling of an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause ('illa).
علة (‘illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that is common between original and branch cases, providing the basis for extending the ruling.
مثلات (muthulāt): Precedents or patterns of punishments in the Quran that serve as analogies for similar cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two essential conditions for applying qiyas to a new commodity like rice, according to this passage?
A) Edibility and being a foodstuff
B) Existence of quantity (qadr) and genus (jins)
C) Weight and volume
D) Being a staple food and traded by volume

Key Takeaway
Qiyas requires both quantity (qadr) and genus (jins) for the ruling to transfer from the original to the branch case.

The Quranic Foundation of Qiyas: The Command of I'tibar
Grounding qiyas in the Quran via i'tibar and muthulat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Quranic command 'fai'tabiru' serves as the foundation for legal qiyas in the Hanafi school, and apply the concept of muthulat (punishment patterns) to analogical reasoning.

Core Idea
The Quranic command to 'take a lesson' is the primary textual basis for the validity of qiyas in Hanafi usul.

The author of this passage grounds the methodology of qiyas directly in the Quran. By citing Surah al-Hashr verse 2, he argues that legal analogical reasoning is a form of i'tibar (taking a lesson) that God commands. The passage explores how the pattern of punishment for sin—expulsion of the Jews—can be analogized to other cases of sin. This establishes the principle that legal rulings can be extended based on shared causes.

Guided Path
1
1. Locate the Quranic verse
Find the verse 'فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الْأَبْصَارِ' in the text. It is the central proof quoted.
Surah al-Hashr, verse 2.
2
2. Interpret the command 'i'tabiru'
Understand that 'i'tibar' here is interpreted as analogical reasoning, not just passive reflection. The author uses the example of punishments to show that the Quran itself uses patterns.
The command is imperative, indicating obligation.
3
3. See the analogy of punishments (muthulat)
The text says 'وهو نظير المثلات' — this legal qiyas is analogous to the pattern of punishments. The expulsion of the Jews due to kufr serves as a pattern: whenever kufr occurs, expulsion follows.
Just as legal qiyas transfers a ruling based on a shared 'illah, divine punishment follows a pattern based on a shared cause (sin).
4
4. Apply the pattern to legal rulings
The same method of identifying a cause (e.g., sin or kufr) and extending the consequence (expulsion or punishment) is used in legal reasoning: identify the 'illah and transfer the hukm.
This reinforces that qiyas is a valid method rooted in the Quranic approach.

(السنبلي) وغيره من المكيلات والموزونات كالجص والحديد. (القمر) أمثالاً متساوية: أي أشياء متوافقة جنسًا ومتساويًا قدراً. (القمر) مثل حكم النص: أي في الأشياء الستة المنصوص عليها في الحديث. (القمر) فلزمنا إثباته أي بسبب المشاركة في العلة أي القدر مع الجنس. (القمر) هذا القياس أي القياس الذي ذكرنا في الأرز وغيره. (القمر) لأوّل الحشر : أي في وقت أول الحشر، أي أول جمع عسكر الإسلام، قال البيضاوي: أي في أول حشرهم من جزيرة العرب؛ إذ لم يصبهم هذا الذلّ قبل ذلك. والحشر إخراج جمع من مكان إلى آخر، وبنو نضير حيّ من اليهود ومن أولاد هارون عليه السلام، كذا في بعض حواشي "تفسير البيضاوي". (القمر) لأول الحشر إلخ قال في "التنوير" : هذا لليهود كان أول الحشر، ثم بعد ذلك أخذوا بالحشر الثاني في زمان أمير المؤمنين عمر رضي الله عنه وقت وصول عسكر الإسلام حيث ذهب اليهود من المكان وأقاموا فيه (السنبلي) أن لا يكونوا عليه أي أن لا يكونوا مخاصمين عليه. (القمر)
فنقضوا العهد في وقعة أحد، فأمرهم صلى الله عليه وسلم بالخروج من المدينة فاستمهلوا عشرة أيام وطلبوا الصلح، فأبى عليهم إلا الجلاء، فأخرجهم الله من المدينة لأوّل الحشر والإخراج حال كونكم يا أيها المسلمون ما ظننتم أن يخرجوا، وظنّوا أي اليهود أنهم مانعتهم حصونهم من الله، فأتاهم الله أي عذابه وحكمه بالجلاء من حيث لم يحتسبوا ذلك، وقذف أي ألقى الله في قلوبهم الرعب حالَ كونهم يُخربون بيوتهم بأيديهم وأيدي المؤمنين لحاجتهم إلى الخشب والحجارة، فحملوا أثقالهم هذه على حمال كثيرة، وخرجوا منها، واستوطنوا بخيبر، ثم أخرجهم عمر من خيبر إلى الشام، هذا تفسير الآية. فالإخراج من الديار عقوبة كالقتل حيث سوى بينهما في قوله: ﴿وَلَوْ أَنَّا كَتَبْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ أَنِ اقْتُلُوا أَنْفُسَكُمْ أَوِ اخْرُجُوا مِنْ دِيَارِكُمْ مَا فَعَلُوهُ إِلَّا قَلِيلٌ مِنْهُمْ﴾ (النساء: ٦٦) والكفر يصلح داعيًا إليه، فكلما وجد الكفر يترتب عليه الإخراج وأول الحشر يدل على تكرار هذه العقوبة، في وقعة أحد التي هزم المسلمون فيها. (القمر) فأمرهم إلخ وحاصرهم إحدى وعشرين ليلة.(القمر) ما ظننتم إلخ لشدة بأسهم ووثاقة حصولهم. (القمر) من حيث لم يحتسبوا فإنهم كانوا يحسبون أنهم يغلبون على المؤمنين. (القمر) حال كونهم يُخربون إلخ أي يخربون بواطن بيوتهم بأيديهم، والمؤمنون يُخربون ظواهر لما نقضوا العهد فوقعوا أسبابًا لتخريب المؤمنين، فكأنهم أمروا المسلمين وكلّفوهم بهذا التخريب، ولهذا قال الله تعالى: ﴿يُحْرِبُونَ بُيُوتَهُمْ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ وَأَيْدِي الْمُؤْمِنِينَ﴾ (الحشر : ٢) (القمر) بينهما : أي بين القتل والإخراج فالتسوية والتخيير بينهما دليل على أنهما بمنزلة واحدة. (القمر) ولو أنا كتبنا عليهم أي على ضعفاء الإسلام أن مفسرة ﴿اقْتُلُوا أَنْفُسَكُمْ أَوِ اخْرُجُوا مِنْ دِيَارِكُمْ﴾ (النساء: ٦٦) كما كتبنا على بني إسرائيل ﴿مَا فَعَلُوهُ﴾ (النساء: ٦٦) أي المكتوب عليهم إلا ﴿قَلِيلٌ مِنْهُمْ﴾ (النساء: ٦٦) (القمر) داعيًا إليه أي إلى الإخراج الذي هو كالقتل. (القمر) يدل إلخ إذ الأول لا بد له من ثانٍ، وفيه ما قيل من أن المعتبر في الأولية عدم تقدّم غيره، لا وجود آخر متأخرا عنه، فتأمل. (القمر) أخرجه الحاكم وصححه وابن مردويه والبيهقي في الدلائل بطرق وألفاظ مختلفة عن عائشة [إشراق الأبصار: ٢٩] وغيرها.
Chapter of Qiyas. Definition of Qiyas and its ruling. And we found rice and others as equal parallels, so excess in similarity was excess free from [reason] due to existence of quantity and genus, meaning things with parallels these equal parallels, the measured things rice and others from the consideration in sale contract like the ruling of the text without difference, so we are required to prove it, i.e., to prove the ruling of the text, which is obligation of equality and prohibition of riba except for the six specified things and weighed things, whether edible or not edible, on condition of existence of quantity and genus. On the method of i'tibar commanded in His statement: 'So take a lesson, O people of vision' (Al-Hashr:2), and it is analogous to the punishments, i.e., this legal qiyas is analogous to considering the punishments descending upon the disbelievers, for Allah said: 'He it is Who drove out those who disbelieved from among the People of the Book from their homes at the first gathering...' (Al-Hashr:2) ... (continues with commentary on the verse and analogy
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a definition of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It opens by declaring the chapter on qiyas and then immediately defines its ruling: qiyas establishes the same legal norm (hukm) for a new case (far') as for the original case (asl) due to a shared effective cause ('illa). The commentator uses the example of rice (and other foodstuffs) analogized to the six specified commodities in the hadith on riba. The key condition for qiyas in this case is the presence of both quantity (qadr, meaning standard measure like weight or volume) and genus (jins, meaning the same category). If these two are present, then the ruling of the original text—obligation of equality and prohibition of disparity—applies to the new case. The author then justifies qiyas by quoting the Quranic verse 'fai'tabiru' (so take a lesson) from Surah al-Hashr, arguing that just as the Quran commands considering historical punishments to deduce consequences of sin, so too Islamic law commands considering evidence to deduce rulings. The verse about the expulsion of Banu Nadir is then expounded to show that expulsion (ikhraj) is a punishment analogous to death in some contexts, and that the occurrence of the cause (kufr) leads to the effect (expulsion). This supports the principle that patterns (muthulat) discerned from revealed texts can be extended by analogy. The commentary relies on classical sources like al-Tanwir, Tafsir al-Baydawi, and glosses by al-Sunbuli and al-Qamar. Throughout, the text maintains a Hanafi perspective, emphasizing that 'i'tibar (taking lesson) is the basis for qiyas.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: transferring the ruling of an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause ('illa).
علة (‘illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that is common between original and branch cases, providing the basis for extending the ruling.
مثلات (muthulāt): Precedents or patterns of punishments in the Quran that serve as analogies for similar cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author mean by 'nazir al-muthulat' in the context of qiyas?
A) Qiyas is similar to mathematical equations.
B) Qiyas is analogous to the pattern of punishments in the Quran.
C) Qiyas is based on speculative reasoning.
D) Qiyas is unique to Hanafis.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic command 'i'tabiru' and the pattern of punishments (muthulat) provide the foundational proof for qiyas in Hanafi usul.

Definition of Qiyas and its Quranic Proof
Defining qiyas and proving its validity from Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qiyas linguistically and technically, and derive its validity from the Quranic command 'i'tabiru'.

Core Idea
Qiyas is a valid source of law mandated by the Quranic imperative to reason analogically.

This lesson opens the chapter on Qiyas with its definition and primary scriptural proof. Understanding qiyas is essential for deriving rulings for new cases. The author connects the linguistic meaning to the technical concept, then cites Quran 59:2 to establish the obligation of analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning of qiyas
Qiyas linguistically means measuring or comparing, as in the exile of the Jews or the gathering on Judgment Day.
2
State the technical definition
Technically, qiyas is extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new branch (far') based on a shared effective cause ('illah).
This definition is implicit in the passage's explanation of 'i'tibar.
3
Locate the Quranic proof
The verse 'fā‘tabirū yā ulī l-absār' (59:2) is the primary textual evidence for qiyas.
4
Understand the istidlal from the imperative
The command 'i'tabiru' is an imperative, which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is contrary evidence. The context shows 'i'tibar means analogy.
This step applies the usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
5
Apply the derivation
Therefore, performing qiyas is obligatory for a mujtahid when no explicit text exists, making qiyas a valid source of law.
The final ruling: qiyas is hujjah (a proof) and wajib when needed.

باب القياس
تعريف القياس وحكمه
وهو إجلاء عمره إياهم من خيبر إلى الشام وقيل هو حشرهم يوم القيامة. أي الحشر الثاني
دعانا إلى الاعتبار في قوله فَاعْتَبِرُ والله بالتأمل في معنى النص للعمل به فيما لا نص أي الله تعالى (الحشر: ۲) متعلق بالاعتبار فيه، فنعتبر أحوالنا بأحوالهم، ونحترز عن مثل ما فعلوا توقيًا عن مثل ما نزل بهم. فكذلك ههنا، أي في القياس الشرعي، فنتأمل في علة النص وتعديها إلى الفرع لنثبت حكم النص فيه.
Chapter of Qiyas. Definition of Qiyas and its ruling. And it is the exile of 'Umar [ibn al-Khattab] of them from Khaybar to Sham, and it is said it is their gathering on the Day of Judgment, i.e. the second gathering. He [Allah] invited us to reflection in His statement: 'So take heed' [Quran 59:2] – meaning reflection on the meaning of the text to act by it where there is no text. So we reflect on our conditions by their conditions, and we avoid like what they did, guarding against like what befell them. Similarly here in legal qiyas: we reflect on the cause of the text and its transference to the branch to establish the ruling of the text therein.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Qiyas by defining it both linguistically and technically. Linguistically, qiyas is measuring or comparing, exemplified by 'Umar's exile of the Jews or the gathering on Judgment Day. Technically, it is extending a ruling from an original text (Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma) to a new case that shares the same effective cause ('illah). The Quranic proof is verse 59:2, where Allah commands 'i'tibar' (taking heed/reasoning by analogy). The author explains that just as we learn from past nations' fates, we analogize from textual rulings to new situations by identifying the 'illah and applying it to the branch (far'). This establishes the legitimacy of qiyas in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original (asl) to a branch (far') based on shared cause ('illah).
العلة (al-'illah): The effective cause or ratio legis that justifies a ruling and allows its extension to similar cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 'Follow what has been revealed to you from your Lord' (6:106)
D) 'And consult them in the affairs' (3:159)

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a legitimate source of Islamic law, mandated by the Quranic command to analogical reasoning.

Three Requirements for Qiyas and the Debate on the Need for a Separate Proof of Causality
Explaining three required proofs for qiyas and debating the second

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three preliminary requirements for qiyas and evaluate the ikhtilaf regarding the necessity of the second requirement.

Core Idea
Finding the 'illah itself proves the text is causal – no separate proof needed.

This passage outlines three preliminary requirements a mujtahid must consider before performing qiyas. The central debate is whether we need an independent proof that a specific text is causal (the second requirement) or whether extracting a valid 'illah suffices. The text presents the evidence for both sides and clarifies that the author and commentator align with Imam Fakhr al-Islam, who insists on the necessity of the second proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three requirements
List the three matters mentioned: (1) the default that every text is causal, (2) a separate proof that this text is causal, (3) a proof distinguishing the 'illah from other attributes.
These are conditions for the validity of qiyas.
2
Locate the ikhtilaf
Which scholar requires the second requirement and which view is preferred? Imam Fakhr al-Islam requires it; the chosen view says it is not necessary.
The text states 'al-mukhtar annahu laysa bi-daruri' – the chosen view is that it is not necessary.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil for the chosen view
The proof for the 'illah itself demonstrates causality; the Companions practiced qiyas without a prior proof of causality.
4
Consider the opposing argument
Why might a separate proof be needed? Some texts may be devotional ('ta'abbudi') and not causal; a prior proof ensures we do not wrongly assume causality.
5
Note the author's tarjih
Despite the preferred view, the author and commentator ultimately choose Fakhr al-Islam's position, requiring all three steps.
The final sentence says 'the author and commentator have chosen the madhhab of Imam Fakhr al-Islam'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي دليل يدل على أن هذه هي العلة لا غيرُ كما يعلم في قوله عليه: "الحنطة بالحنطة" من المقابلة، ومن قوله: "مثلاً بمثل" كون القدر والجنس علة.
ولا بد قبل ذلك من قيام الدليل على أنه للحال شاهد أي على أن هذا النص في الحال دلالة التمييز أي النص أو الإجماع معلول مع قطع النظر عن كون الأصول في الأصل معلولة، فقوله: "للحال" معناه في الحال، وقوله: "شاهد" كنى به عن كونه معلولاً؛ لأنه إذا كان معلولاً بعلة جامعة كان شاهدًا على حكم الفرع والحاصل أن ههنا ثلاثة أمور الأول: أن الأصل في كل نص أي في حجية القياس أن يكون معلولاً، والثاني: أن لا بد من دليل مستقل يدل على أن هذا النص في الحال معلول بقطع النظر عن ذلك الأصل، والثالث: أنْ لا بد من دليل يميز العلة من غيرها،
ولا بد قبل ذلك إلخ الحاصل أنه لا بد قبل إقامة الدليل على إثبات العلة من الدليل على أن حكم أصل النص معلول، وهذا هو مذهب الإمام فخر الإسلام له والمختار أنه ليس بضروري بل متى ورد النص على حكم صار هذا سببًا لاستحقاق المجتهد بأن يجتهد ويستخرج العلة بدليل، فإن وجدها عمل بها، وإلا لا، وهذا القول هو الصحيح؛ لأن الدليل لما قام على عليّة العلة فثبت عليّتها وعُلم أن النص معلّل؛ لأن مقتضى الدليل لا يترك، فإقامة الدليل على كون النص معللاً على سبيل الإجمال قبل هذا الأمر زائد بلا فائدة، وأيضا كانت الصحابة له يقيسون في بدأ الأمر بدون الاستدلال على كون النص معللاً بشرط وجدانهم العلة لحكم النص، وإلا تركوه، و مشايخنا نقلوا مذهبين آخرين ههنا الأول: أن الأصل في النصوص ليس بتعليل، وإنما يُطلب الدليل إذا دل دليل على كون النص الخاص معللاً، والثاني: أن الأصل في النصوص التعليل لكن فيه كفاية، لا حاجة إلى التمييز بين الصفات لتعيين صفة منها للعلية إلا وقت تعارض الصفات وتضادها، وبطلان هذا القول أظهر من أن يُبيّن، وعُزي إلى أصحاب الطرد فافهم وتدبّر ليظهر لك أن المصنف له والشارح له اختارا ههنا مذهب الإمام فخر الإسلام له، وهذا البيان أخذنا من كلام صاحب "التنوير" والله تعالى أعلم.
That is, a proof that indicates that this is the cause and no other, as known from his statement 'wheat for wheat' by comparison, and from his statement 'like for like' that quantity and genus are the cause. And before that, it is necessary to establish a proof that it is a witness in the present case, i.e., that this text at present is causal, disregarding the fact that the sources are inherently causal. So his statement 'in the present case' means at the moment, and his statement 'witness' is a metaphor for being causal; because if it is causal with a comprehensive cause, it serves as a witness for the ruling of the branch. The summary is that there are three matters. First: the default in every text regarding the authority of qiyas is that it is causal. Second: there must be an independent proof indicating that this particular text is causal at present, disregarding that default. Third: there must be a proof that distinguishes the cause from others. ... This is the position of Imam Fakhr al-Islam. The chosen view is that it is not necessary; rather, whenever a text on a ruling comes, this becomes a reason for the mujtahid to exert effort and extract the cause by proof; if he finds it, he acts by it, otherwise not. This statement is correct because once the proof for the causality of the cause is established, the causality is proven and it is known that the text is causal, since the implication of the proof cannot be abandoned. So establishing a proof that the text is causal in general before this step is redundant and useless. Moreover, the Companions used to engage in analogy from the beginning without first establishing that the text is causal, provided they found a cause for the ruling; otherwise they abandoned it. Our scholars transmitted two other positions here: first, that the default in texts is not causal, and a proof is sought only if a proof indicates that a specific text is causal; second, that the default in texts is causal but it is sufficient, and there is no need to distinguish among attributes to identify one as the cause except when attributes conflict and contradict. The invalidity of this position is clearer than can be explained, and it is attributed to the followers of mere pattern (as'hab al-tard). So understand and reflect so that it becomes clear to you that the author and the commentator have chosen the position of Imam Fakhr al-Islam. This explanation is taken from the words of the author of 'al-Tanwir'. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage details the three preliminary requirements for performing qiyas, and then critically examines the necessity of the second requirement. The first requirement: the general principle that all source texts are inherently causal (already covered). The second: a specific proof that the particular text under consideration is indeed causal in this instance, independent of the general principle. The third: a proof that distinguishes the exact cause among the text's attributes. The author (likely the commentator of Noor al-Anwar) then presents a dispute: Imam Fakhr al-Islam (al-Pazdawi) insists the second proof is necessary, but the preferred (mukhtar) view is that it is not. The reasoning: once you find the 'illah through a valid proof, that itself proves the text is causal; there is no need for a prior general proof. The practice of the Companions supports this: they directly looked for causes and analogized without a separate step. Two other weaker views are mentioned: one denies default causality altogether, the other says default causality suffices and need for tamyeez only at conflict. The commentator rejects the latter as invalid. Ultimately, the author of the commentary (al-Sanbali) aligns with Fakhr al-Islam's requirement of all three steps. This reflects a key difference in Hanafi usul: the balance between default causality and the need for specific indicators.

Key Terms
دلالة التمييز (dalalat al-tamyeez): The indicator that distinguishes the effective cause from other attributes of the text.
أصحاب الطرد (as'hab al-tard): Those who blindly analogize based on any superficial similarity without proper identification of the 'illah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred view (al-mukhtar) regarding the need for a separate proof that a specific text is causal?
A) It is absolutely necessary before any qiyas.
B) It is not necessary; finding the 'illah suffices.
C) It is only required for texts from the Quran, not Sunnah.
D) It is required only when the cause is hidden.

Key Takeaway
The necessity of a separate proof of causality for the base text is debated; the preferred view says it is redundant, but some Hanafis require it.

Conditions for Qiyas: Original Not Restricted and Proving Mu'allal (Dispute)
Explaining the condition that the original is not restricted and the dispute on proving the text is mu'allal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the condition that the original must not be restricted in qiyas and evaluate the dispute on whether proving the text is mu'allal is required before extracting the illah.

Core Idea
A text with a ruling restricted to a specific case cannot serve as an asl for qiyas; whether you need to prove a text is caused before using it is a debated methodological step.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary addresses two key topics in the theory of qiyas. First, it clarifies that if a ruling is confined to a particular case by another text (like the acceptance of Khuzaymah's sole testimony), that case cannot be used as an analogy for others. Second, it presents a dispute: must a mujtahid first establish that the original text is 'caused' (mu'allal) before seeking the illah? The text explains the views of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and the preferred (mukhtar) position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
Recognize that the passage deals with the condition of the asl not being makhsus and the dispute on proving mu'allal.
Both are prerequisites for valid qiyas.
2
Analyze the condition of makhsus
Understand what it means for an asl to be makhsus: its ruling is confined to itself by a separate text, making qiyas invalid.
Example: Khuzaymah's individual testimony ruling cannot be extended.
3
Deconstruct the dispute on mu'allal
Identify the three matters mentioned: original principle of causality, need for evidence of this text being mu'allal, and need for evidence distinguishing the illah. Then contrast Fakhr al-Islam's requirement of the second matter with the mukhtar view that it is superfluous.
The mukhtar view relies on the third matter to suffice.
4
Examine the evidence from Companions' practice
Note how the Companions performed qiyas directly by extracting the illah without first proving the text is mu'allal in general.
This supports the mukhtar view.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical difference: Fakhr al-Islam requires an extra step; the mukhtar bypasses it, making ijtihad more efficient.
The passage declares the mukhtar as the correct view.

باب القياس
تعريف القياس وحكمه
ولا بد قبل ذلك من قيام الدليل على أنه للحال شاهد أي على أن هذا النص في الحال دليل على أنه معلول مع قطع النظر عن كون الأصول في الأصل معلولة، فقوله: "للحال" معناه في الحال، وقوله: "شاهد" كنى به عن كونه معلولاً؛ لأنه إذا كان معلولاً بعلة جامعة كان شاهدًا على حكم الفرع والحاصل أن ههنا ثلاثة أمور الأول: أن الأصل في كل نص أي في حجية القياس أن يكون معلولاً، والثاني: أن لا بد من دليل مستقل يدل على أن هذا النص في الحال معلول بقطع النظر عن ذلك الأصل، والثالث: أنْ لا بد من دليل يميز العلة من غيرها، ولا بد قبل ذلك إلخ الحاصل أنه لا بد قبل إقامة الدليل على إثبات العلة من الدليل على أن حكم أصل النص معلول، وهذا هو مذهب الإمام فخر الإسلام له والمختار أنه ليس بضروري بل متى ورد النص على حكم صار هذا سببًا لاستحقاق المجتهد بأن يجتهد ويستخرج العلة بدليل، فإن وجدها عمل بها، وإلا لا، وهذا القول هو الصحيح؛ لأن الدليل لما قام على عليّة العلة فثبت عليّتها وعُلم أن النص معلّل؛ لأن مقتضى الدليل لا يترك، فإقامة الدليل على كون النص معللاً على سبيل الإجمال قبل هذا الأمر زائد بلا فائدة، وأيضا كانت الصحابة له يقيسون في بدأ الأمر بدون الاستدلال على كون النص معللاً بشرط وجدانهم العلة لحكم النص، وإلا تركوه، و مشايخنا نقلوا مذهبين آخرين ههنا الأول: أن الأصل في النصوص ليس بتعليل، وإنما يُطلب الدليل إذا دل دليل على كون النص الخاص معللاً، والثاني: أن الأصل في النصوص التعليل لكن فيه كفاية، لا حاجة إلى التمييز بين الصفات لتعيين صفة منها للعلية إلا وقت تعارض الصفات وتضادها، وبطلان هذا القول أظهر من أن يُبيّن، وعُزي إلى أصحاب الطرد فافهم وتدبّر ليظهر لك أن المصنف له والشارح له اختارا ههنا مذهب الإمام فخر الإسلام له، وهذا البيان أخذنا من كلام صاحب "التنوير" والله تعالى أعلم.
فشرطه أن لا يكون الأصل مخصوصاً بحكمه بنص آخر الظاهر أن الأصل هو المقيس عليه، والباء في "بحكمه" داخل على المقصور والمعنى: أن لا يكون المقيس عليه كخزيمة له مثلاً مقصوراً عليه حكمه بنص آخر؛ إذ لو كان حكمه مقصوراً عليه بالنص فكيف يقاس عليه غيره؟ ولا يجوز أن يراد بالأصل النص الدال على حكم المقيس عليه ويكون الباء بمعنى مع؛ إذ يكون المعنى حينئذٍ أن لا يكون النص الدال على حكم المقيس عليه مخصوصا مع حكمه الفرع على المقيس عليه. فإذا اجتمعت هذه إلخ هذا عند فخر الإسلام له، وأما عند غيره فلا حاجة إلى الأمر الثاني، بل الأمر الثالث مُعْنٍ عنه، فإنه إذا قام الدليل المميز للعلة عن غيرها فإقامة الدليل على أن هذا النص في الحال معلول إجمالاً أمر زائد لا طائل تحته، والصحابة له يقيسون باستخراج علة الحكم في بُدو الأمر ابتداء، ولو لم يجدوها تركوا القياس، ولا يقيمون الدليل على أن هذا النص معلول في الحال إجمالا. وشريعة وهو تقدير الفرع بالأصل في الحكم والعلة. ودفع أي دفع القياس خصمه، أو دفع الإيرادات عن القياس. بنص آخر أي بسبب نص آخر يدلّ على اختصاص المقيس عليه بحكمه، والمراد بالنص ههنا الدليل من قبيل ذكر الخاص وإرادة العام كتابًا كان أو سنةً أو إجماعًا.
Chapter of Qiyas. Definition of Qiyas and its ruling. And before that, it is necessary to establish evidence that it is, for the present, a witness, i.e., that this text is currently evidence that it is caused, disregarding the fact that the principles are originally caused. He said: 'for the present' means currently, and he said 'witness' as a metonym for being caused; because if it is caused by a comprehensive cause, it is a witness for the ruling of the branch. The summary is that there are three matters: First, that the principle for every text, i.e., regarding the authority of qiyas, is that it is caused. Second, that there must be an independent evidence indicating that this text is currently caused, disregarding that principle. Third, that there must be evidence distinguishing the cause from others. 'And before that etc.' The summary is that before establishing evidence for proving the cause, there must be evidence that the ruling of the original text is caused. This is the doctrine of Imam Fakhr al-Islam, and the chosen [view] is that it is not necessary; rather, whenever a text arrives on a ruling, it becomes a reason entitling the mujtahid to exert effort and extract the cause by evidence; if he finds it, he acts on it, otherwise not. This statement is correct because when evidence is established on the causality of the cause, its causality is proven, and it is known that the text is caused because the implication of the evidence is not abandoned. So establishing evidence that the text is caused in a general way before this matter is superfluous without benefit. Also, the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, used to perform qiyas at the beginning without arguing that the text is caused, provided they found the cause for the text's ruling; otherwise, they abandoned it. Our scholars transmitted two other doctrines here: First, that the principle in texts is not causality; rather, evidence is sought only when evidence indicates that a particular text is caused. Second, that the principle in texts is causality, but it suffices; there is no need to distinguish among attributes to designate one for causality except when attributes conflict and oppose. The invalidity of this doctrine is more apparent than need be shown. It is attributed to the proponents of [الطرد]. So understand and reflect so that it becomes clear to you that the author and the commentator chose here the doctrine of Imam Fakhr al-Islam. This explanation is taken from the words of the author of 'al-Tanwir'. And Allah knows best. Then its condition is that the original should not be restricted to its ruling by another text. Apparently the original is the analogized-upon (al-maqis 'alayhi). The letter ba in 'bi-hukmihi' enters upon the restricted, meaning: the analogized-upon, like Khuzaymah for example, should not have its ruling confined to it by another text; for if its ruling is confined to it by the text, then how can something else be analogized to it? It is not permissible to mean by 'original' the text indicating the ruling of the analogized-upon, with the ba meaning 'with', because then the meaning would be that the text indicating the ruling of the analogized-upon is not restricted along with its ruling of the branch to the analogized-upon. 'When these are combined etc.' This is according to Fakhr al-Islam. As for others, there is no need for the second matter; rather, the third suffices. For when the evidence distinguishing the cause from others is established, then establishing evidence that this text is currently caused in general terms is superfluous with no benefit underneath. The Companions used to perform qiyas by extracting the cause of the ruling at the beginning directly; if they did not find it, they abandoned qiyas, and they did not establish evidence that this text is currently caused in general. And legally it is equating the branch with the original in ruling and cause. And 'deflection' means deflecting the qiyas of the opponent, or deflecting objections against qiyas. 'By another text' means due to another text indicating the confinement of the analogized-upon to its ruling; what is meant by 'text' here is evidence of the type mentioning the specific and intending the general, be it Book, Sunnah, or consensus.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the rules of qiyas discusses two important issues: the condition that the original (asl) is not restricted to its ruling by a separate text, and the dispute over whether it is necessary to first prove that the original text is mu'allal (caused) before extracting the illah. The passage begins by explaining that before establishing the illah, there are three required matters: (1) the principle that every text is generally intended to be caused, (2) a specific proof that this particular text is currently caused, and (3) a proof that distinguishes the illah from other attributes. The author then presents the view of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi that proving the text is caused is necessary, but the preferred (mukhtar) view is that it is not necessary, because once evidence for the illah is established, the causality is automatically known. The Companions' practice supports this: they would directly seek the illah without separately proving that the text is caused. The passage then addresses the condition that the asl must not have its ruling confined to it by another text, using the example of Khuzaymah ibn Thabit, whose individual testimony is accepted by a specific text, so his case cannot be used as an analogy for others. The commentary clarifies terminology and resolves potential misunderstandings, emphasizing that the asl in this context is the analogized-upon (maqis 'alayhi), not the textual evidence.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): تفسير القياس شرعاً: تقدير الفرع بالأصل في الحكم والعلة.
الأصل (al-asl): هنا المقيس عليه (مرادف للأصل في باب القياس).
العلة (al-illah): الصفة التي هي باعث الحكم، والتي يميزها الدليل عن غيرها.
مخصوص (makhsus): المقيس عليه إذا كان حكمه مقصوراً عليه بنص آخر، فلا يصح القياس عليه.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the case of Khuzaymah ibn Thabit not suitable as an asl for qiyas?
A) Because he is a Companion.
B) Because his testimony ruling is confined to him by a text.
C) Because qiyas is not allowed in testimony matters.
D) Because his case is not analogizable.

Key Takeaway
The original for qiyas must not have its ruling restricted to itself by another text, and according to the preferred view, no separate proof that the text is caused is required before extracting the illah.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
10 min
Condition of the Original in Qiyas: Not Exclusive
Elaborating the condition that the original must not be exclusive to its ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the original (asl) in qiyas must not be exclusive to its ruling, identify the hadith of Khuzayma as evidence, and apply the condition to determine when qiyas is invalid.

Core Idea
An original case restricted to its ruling by a text cannot be used for qiyas.

In this lesson, we examine a critical condition for valid qiyas: the original case (asl) must not have its ruling exclusively confined to it by another text. Without this, analogy would contradict divine specification. We will explore the example of Khuzayma ibn Thabit, whose solitary testimony was accepted due to a specific prophetic statement, and understand why this cannot be extended to others via qiyas. We also touch on the proper definition of 'asl' in this context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its textual basis
Locate the condition 'an la yakuna al-asl makhsusan bi hukmihi bi nassin akhar' and the hadith of Khuzayma as its proof.
The hadith is: 'Whoever has Khuzayma testify for him, that suffices.'
2
Understand the meaning of 'asl' in this context
The preferred view is that 'asl' refers to the measured-upon case (maqis alayh), not the text indicating the ruling. See how the commentator clarifies this distinction.
If 'asl' were the text, the condition would become absurd.
3
Examine the Khuzayma example
The hadith makes acceptance of Khuzayma's solitary testimony a unique ruling. Applying qiyas to extend it to others would contradict the specific text.
Even higher-status individuals like the caliphs cannot be analogized to Khuzayma.
4
Consider the consequence and reasoning
Why can't we analogize? Because it would nullify Khuzayma's special honor and contradict the text. The text restricts the ruling exclusively to him.
This is a protection of the divine specificity.
5
Note the rejected alternative interpretation
Some interpreted 'asl' as the text and 'bi' as 'with', but the commentator refutes this as leading to an absurd meaning.
The Hanafi consensus follows the preferred interpretation.

حكمه
عن
ولا شك إلخ فعلم من هذا أن النص اثنان والحال أن النص واحد (السنبلي النص هو النص الدال على حكم المقيس عليه لا غير، فيلوح على المعنى الذي ذكر آنفًا أثر الإهمال، ثم اعلم أن الشارح الله لا يدعي أن المراد نفي خصوصية النص الدال على حكم المقيس عليه مع الحكم عن العمومات الواردة، بل غرضه أنه لو أريد بالأصل النص الدال على حكم المقيس عليه، ويكون الباء في "بحكمه" بمعنى مع، ويكون المراد نفي خصوصية النص الدال على حكم تلك العمومات فلا يستقيم المعنى، بل يحدث المعنى المهمل، وهذا كلام حق لا غبار عليه وليس بمحل التأمل، فما في "مسير" الدائر" من أن في كلام الشارح له تأملاً فلا يخلو عن تأمل، نعم، إذا أريد بالأصل الدال على حكم المقيس عليه ويكون الباء في "بحكمه" بمعنى مع ويكون الخصوص بمعنى التفرد، ويكون المخصوص به محذوفًا، ويكون الباء في "بنص آخر" للسببية يحصل معنى مستقيم صحيح، وهو معنى آخر ما تعرض به الشارح له صحة وفسادًا، وقد بينه الشارح الحسامي بتفصيل لا مزيد عليه حيث قال: أي يشترط أن لا يكون النص المثبت للحكم في المحل أي المقيس عليه مختصاً مع حكمه بذلك المحل بسبب نص آخر يدلّ على اختصاصه بذلك المحل مثل قوله عليه من شهد له خزيمة فهو حسبه، فإنه مختص مع حكمه هو قبول شهادة الفرد بمحل وروده، آخر يدل على اختصاصه به وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاسْتَشْهِدُوا شَهِيدَيْنِ مِنْ رِجَالِكُمْ (البقرة : ۲۸۲) فإنه لما أوجب على الجميع مراعاة العدد لزم منه نفي قبول شهادة الفرد فإذا ثبت بدليل في موضع كان مختصا به، ولا يعدوه النص النافي غيره وما فهم البعض من أن توجيه شارح "الحسامى" والتوجيه الذي حكم الشارح ساله بعدم جوازه واحد وقال رادًا على الشارح أن عدم جوازه مدفوع بما قال صاحب "التحقيق"، فلا تصغ إليه لثبوت البون البين بين التوجيهين، كيف وقد قال الشارح له في "المنهية": ولو فسّر النص الآخر بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاسْتَشْهِدُوا شَهِيدَيْنِ مِنْ رِجَالِكُمْ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۸۲) وجعل الباء للاستعانة أي علم ذلك باستعانة النص الآخر كما وجه به ابن الملك لكان أيضا وجيهًا. (القمر) على حكم المقيس إلخ : فكيف يكون هو مخصوصا بذلك النص؛ لأنه يلزم اختصاص الشيء بنفسه. (السنبلي) حينئذٍ : أي حين قياس غيره عليه. (القمر) اختصاصه أي اختصاص خزيمة الا الله ، ثم اعلم أنه إنما اختص خزيمة الا الله بهذه الكرامة لاختصاصه من الحاضرين بفهم جواز الشهادة للرسول علي بناءً على أن قوله عليها في إفادة العلم بمنزلة العيان. (القمر)
وهو خزيمة
رواه عبد الحارث بن أبي أسامة في مسنده"، وأخرجه أبو نعيم وابن عساكر عن خزيمة بن ثابت له حديثا طويلاً، وفيه من شهد له خزيمة" أو "شهد عليه "فحسبه" قال الذهبي وابن الجوزي: كان البائع سواد بن الحارث المحاربي. [إشراق الأبصار: ۲۹] .
Chapter of Qiyas. 15. Definition of Qiyas and Its Ruling. And it explains that this is 'then for qiyas an interpretation lexically and legally as we mentioned, and condition, pillar, ruling, and rebuttal. So it is necessary to explain the cause without other than it. So when these three are combined, then qiyas must be a proof. And it is the estimation. These four for the sake of preserving his qiyas and rebutting the qiyas of his opponent. So its condition is that the original should not be specific to its ruling by another text. It is apparent that the original is the measured-upon, and the preposition 'bi' in 'bi hukmihi' enters upon the restricted, and the meaning: that the measured-upon should not be such as Khuzayma for example, restricted to him its ruling by another text; for if its ruling were restricted to it by the text, how can something else be measured to it? And it is not permissible that by 'original' is meant the text indicating the ruling of the measured-upon and the 'bi' is in the sense of 'with'; for then the meaning would be: the text indicating the ruling of the measured-upon should not be specific along with its ruling. The branch upon the measured-upon. So when these are combined etc. This according to Fakhr al-Islam, but according to others there is no need for the second matter; rather the third suffices for it, because when the evidence distinguishing the cause from others stands, then establishing the evidence that this text is in the present condition caused summarily is an extra matter with no benefit. And the Companions used to analogize by extracting the cause of the ruling in the first instance initially, and if they did not find it they abandoned qiyas, and they did not establish evidence that this text is caused in the present condition summarily. (al-Qamar) 'And legally' i.e., it is the estimation of the branch by the original in the ruling and the cause. (al-Muhashi) 'and rebuttal' i.e., rebutting the qiyas of his opponent, or rebutting objections against qiyas. (al-Qamar) 'by another text' i.e., because of another text that indicates the specificness of the measured-upon with its ruling, and what is meant by 'text' here is evidence, of the type mentioning the specific intending the general, whether it be Book, Sunnah, or Ijma'. (al-Qamar) 'It is apparent that the original is the measured-upon' as is the view of most jurists and theoreticians; because qiyas in law is the estimation of the branch by the original in the ruling and the cause, and what is meant by 'original' here is the measured-upon. (al-Qamar) 'upon the restricted' not upon the one restricted to; for the one restricted to is the measured-upon. (al-Qamar) 'like Khuzayma ibn Thabit' may Allah be pleased with him, a noble companion from the senior companions, the one with two testimonies, witnessed Badr, and was killed with the Commander of the Faithful at Siffin in the year thirty-seven. (al-Qamar) 'its ruling' is the acceptance of the testimony of an individual. (al-Qamar) 'by another text' which is his statement peace be upon him: 'Whoever has Khuzayma testify for him, that suffices.' (al-Qamar) since if etc. is evidence for his statement: 'should not be' etc. (al-Qamar) 'then how can it be measured to it?' because then the analogy would be contradictory to the specific text, thus it is invalid. The text i.e., his statement peace be upon him: 'Whoever has Khuzayma testify for him, that suffices.' (al-Qamar) 'upon the ruling of the measured-upon' like Khuzayma, and it is acceptance of his testimony alone. (al-Qamar) 'and the 'ba'' i.e., that occurring in the statement of the author: 'bi hukmihi'. (al-Qamar) 'since' etc. is evidence for his statement: 'it is not permissible' (al-Qamar) 'specific' i.e., from the general texts requiring the condition of number in testimony like His statement: 'And bring to witness two just men from among you' (At-Talaq: 2). (al-Qamar) And it is not doubted that the other text is the text indicating the ruling of the measured-upon. Like the testimony of Khuzayma may Allah be pleased with him alone; for it is specific by his statement peace be upon him: 'Whoever has Khuzayma testify for him, that suffices.' And it should not be measured to it one who is higher in status than him like the Rightly Guided Caliphs; for then the honor of his specialness would be nullified. (al-Qamar) 'upon the ruling' etc.: then how would it be specific by that text? Because it would necessitate the specificness of a thing to itself. (al-Sanbali) 'then' i.e., when measuring something else to it. (al-Qamar) 'its specificness' i.e., the specificness of Khuzayma may Allah be pleased with him. And know that Khuzayma was only singled out for this honor because he was distinctive among those present in understanding the permissibility of testifying for the Messenger peace be upon him based on the fact that his statement in imparting knowledge is like direct observation. (al-Qamar) And it is Khuzayma. Narrated by Abdul-Harith ibn Abi Usama in his Musnad, and narrated by Abu Nu'aym and Ibn Asakir from Khuzayma ibn Thabit a long hadith, and in it: 'Whoever has Khuzayma testify for him' or 'testified against him, that suffices.' Adh-Dhahabi and Ibn al-Jawzi said: the seller was Suwad ibn al-Harith al-Muharibi. [Ishraq al-Absar: 29].
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the definition and conditions of qiyas (analogical deduction) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It begins by reaffirming that qiyas has a lexical and legal definition, and that its validity requires a condition (shart), a pillar (rukn), a ruling (hukm), and a rebuttal (daf'). The author then focuses on one specific condition: that the original case (asl) must not be restricted to its ruling by a separate textual evidence. The 'original' here is the measured-upon case (maqis alayh). The commentator explains that if the ruling of the original is exclusively confined to it by a text (e.g., the special acceptance of Khuzayma ibn Thabit's solitary testimony as per the hadith 'Whoever has Khuzayma testify for him, that suffices'), then it cannot serve as a basis for analogy because that would contradict the specific textual allocation. The passage further discusses a nuanced debate: whether 'original' refers to the case itself or to the text indicating its ruling. The preferred Hanafi view is that it refers to the case (al-maqis alayh). The commentator refutes an alternative interpretation that would lead to an absurd meaning. The example of Khuzayma is used: his unique status in testimony cannot be extended to others, even higher-ranking caliphs, as that would nullify the specific divine honor granted to him. The passage also notes that the Companions practiced qiyas by directly extracting the cause, without needing a preliminary proof that the text is legally caused. Overall, this is a technically dense elaboration on the boundaries of analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-asl): The original case (maqis alayh) upon which analogy is based
مخصوص بحكمه (makhsusan bi hukmihi): Specific/exclusive to its ruling; the original's ruling is confined to it by another text
الفرع (al-far'): The branch case to which the ruling of the asl is extended via qiyas
العلة (al-illa): The cause that is common to both asl and far', justifying the analogy

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because Khuzayma is lower in status than the caliphs
B) Because the ruling of Khuzayma's testimony is restricted to him by a specific text, making it exclusive
C) Because the caliphs already have a higher degree of testimony accepted
D) Because the Companions did not practice qiyas in testimonies

Key Takeaway
An original case whose ruling is exclusively confined to it by a text cannot serve as a basis for qiyas, as analogy would contradict the text's specificity.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Condition in Qiyas: The Asl Must Not Be Specific to Its Text
Stating a condition of qiyas with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition of khususiyyat al-nass to determine whether a ruling can be extended via qiyas.

Core Idea
A ruling based on a text specific to its case cannot be generalized by analogy.

Qiyas (analogical reasoning) is a cornerstone of Hanafi usul, but it has strict conditions. One essential condition is that the original case (asl) must not have a ruling that is specific to it by virtue of a separate text. In this lesson, we examine the famous case of Khuzaymah ibn Thabit, whose single testimony was accepted by the Prophet ﷺ as sufficient—a special honor. The Hanafi scholars explain why this ruling cannot be extended to others, even to the Rightly Guided Caliphs, because the Prophet's statement is a text of specification (khususiyyat al-nass). Understanding this condition helps you distinguish between generalizable rulings and unique exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the passage and note the first condition for qiyas: the ruling in the asl must not be specific to its text (khususiyyat al-nass). This means there must be no separate text indicating that the ruling is limited to that particular case.
2
Examine the example
Consider the example of Khuzaymah: the Prophet ﷺ said 'Whoever Khuzaymah testifies for, it is sufficient for him.' This is a specific ruling that contradicts the general requirement of two witnesses (Quran 2:282). The hadith is a text of specification.
3
Analyze why qiyas fails
Since the ruling is based on a specific text, it is limited to Khuzaymah. Attempting to analogize another person (e.g., a Caliph) would ignore the specification. There is no shared effective cause (illa) because the basis is the Prophet's honorific decree, not a generalizable attribute.
4
Distinguish from general rulings
Not every hadith with a specific occasion is non-analogizable. The condition requires an explicit text indicating that the ruling is exclusive. If the text is general in its wording, it can be analogized even if the occasion was specific.
5
Apply to new cases
When encountering a ruling from a text, check if there is any evidence (Quran, Sunnah, or consensus) that confines it to its original context. If so, qiyas is invalid. If not, proceed to check other conditions.

Source Text
