(القمر) على حكم المقيس إلخ : فكيف يكون هو مخصوصا بذلك النص؛ لأنه يلزم اختصاص الشيء بنفسه. (السنبلي) حينئذٍ : أي حين قياس غيره عليه. (القمر) اختصاصه أي اختصاص خزيمة الا الله ، ثم اعلم أنه إنما اختص خزيمة الا الله بهذه الكرامة لاختصاصه من الحاضرين بفهم جواز الشهادة للرسول علي بناءً على أن قوله عليها في إفادة العلم بمنزلة العيان. (القمر)

رواه عبد الحارث بن أبي أسامة في مسنده"، وأخرجه أبو نعيم وابن عساكر عن خزيمة بن ثابت له حديثا طويلاً، وفيه من شهد له خزيمة" أو "شهد عليه "فحسبه" قال الذهبي وابن الجوزي: كان البائع سواد بن الحارث المحاربي. [إشراق الأبصار: ۲۹] .
بهذا الحكم. وقصته ما روي أن النبي عليا اشترى ناقة من أعرابي وأوفاه الثمن، فأنكر الأعرابي استيفاءه وقال: هَلُمَّ شهيدًا، فقال: من يشهد لي ولم يحضرني أحد؟ فقال خزيمة : أنا أشهد يا رسول الله أنك أوفيت الأعرابي ثمن الناقة، فقال عليه: "كيف تشهد لي ولم تحضرني؟ فقال: يا رسول الله إنا نصدقك فيما تأتينا به من خبر السماء، أفلا نصدقك فيما تخبر به من أداء ثمن الناقة؟ فقال عليها: "من شهد له خزيمة فهو حسبه، فجعلت شهادته كشهادة رجلين كرامة وتفضيلاً على غيره مع أن النصوص أو جبت اشتراط العدد في حق العامة، فلا يقاس عليه غيره.
خزيمة
Chapter of Qiyas. Definition of Qiyas and its ruling: By another text, and there is no doubt that the other text is the text indicating the ruling of the analogized-upon case. Like the testimony of Khuzaymah alone; for it is specific by his saying: 'Whoever Khuzaymah testifies for, it is sufficient for him.' And it should not be analogized to him to one who is higher in status, like the Rightly Guided Caliphs, because then the honor of his specificity would be invalidated. ... (continues with commentary and story). So his testimony was made like the testimony of two men as an honor and preference over others, while the texts required the condition of number for the common people. So no one else is analogized to him.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage explains the first condition for the validity of qiyas: the original ruling (asl) must not be specific to its own text (khususiyyat al-nass). That is, if the proof for the ruling in the original case is accompanied by another text that indicates its specificity to that very case, then it cannot be extended by analogy. The example is the case of Khuzaymah ibn Thabit (may Allah be pleased with him). The Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'Whoever Khuzaymah testifies for, it is sufficient for him,' making his single testimony equivalent to two men—a special honor. This is despite the general Qur'anic requirement of two male witnesses (Surah al-Baqarah 2:282). Since the ruling is based on a specific text (the Prophet's statement) that contradicts the general rule, it is unique to Khuzaymah and cannot be analogized to others, even to the Caliphs. The commentary elaborates on the nuances of interpreting the phrase 'by another text' and confirms that the condition is well-established.

Key Terms
خصوصية النص (khususiyyat al-nass): The specificity of a textual proof to its own particular case, preventing analogical extension.
المقيس عليه (al-maqis 'alayh): The original case (asl) upon which analogy is based.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Condition: Asl Not Contrary to Qiyas
Explaining the condition that the asl must not be an exception to qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a ruling is an exception to qiyas and explain why such a ruling cannot serve as the asl in qiyas.

Core Idea
An exception to qiyas cannot be analogized to other cases.

In qiyas, the original case (asl) must be governed by a ruling that conforms to general legal principles. If the asl itself is an exception—established by a specific textual proof (istihsan)—then it cannot be used as a basis for extending the ruling to new cases. This lesson explores that condition using the example of fasting while eating forgetfully.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Recognize that the asl must not be 'ma'dul bihi an al-qiyas'—deviated from qiyas.
The Arabic phrase is critical: معدول به عن القياس.
2
Understand the rationale
If the asl itself is an exception, its ruling is not generalizable. Qiyas requires a consistent principle.
3
Examine the example
Forgetful eating during fasting is valid by hadith, contradicting qiyas that eating invalidates fasting.
The hadith establishes istihsan, an exception.
4
Recognize the implication
This exceptional ruling cannot be used as an asl for other cases, e.g., forgetful vomiting.
Thus, qiyas from this ruling is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن لا يكون معدولاً به عن القياس، أي لا يكون الأصل مخالفا للقياس؛ إذ لو كان هو بنفسه أي حكم الأصل مخالفا للقياس فكيف يُقاس عليه غيره كبقاء الصوم مع الأكل أو الشرب ناسيا، فإنه مخالف للقياس؛ إذ القياس يقتضي فساد الصوم، وإنما أبقيناه لقوله عليه السلام للذي أكل ناسيا: أتمّ على صومك فإنما أطعمك الله وسقاك. هلم في "منتهى الأرب" هلم بـ"يا" وأصله "لم" و"ها" للتنبيه، حُذفت ألفها، وجعلا اسما واحدا، واستعملت استعمال البسيطة، يستوي فيه الواحد والجمع والتذكير والتأنيث. (القمر العدد أي الرجلين أو رجل وامرأتين. (القمر) معدولاً به الباء للتعدية فإن العدول لازم وهو الميل عن الطريق، كذا قيل ويمكن أن يجعل معلولاً من العدل وهو الصوف، فيكون متعديًا، وحينئذ فالباء زائدة. (القمر) هو : أي الأصل، أي حكم الأصل. (القمر) يقتضي فساد الصوم: أي بالأكل والشرب ناسيا لفوات ركن الصوم وهو الإمساك عن قضاء شهوتي الفرج والبطن والشيء لا يبقى بدون ركنه. (القمر) ذكر البخاري رقم: ٢٦٥٢، باب قول الله تعالى: ﴿وَمِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ رِجَالٌ صَدَقُوا مَا عَاهَدُوا اللَّهَ﴾ (الأحزاب:۲۳) جعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم شهادته شهادة رجلين، ولم يبين القصة، و لم أجد الرواية التي ذكرها الشارح بلفظه [إشراق الأبصار: ٢٩] روى ابن حبان والدار قطني أن رجلاً سأل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال : إني كنت صائمًا فأكلت وشربت ناسيا، فقال عليه السلام: أتم على صومك فإنما أطعمك الله وسقاك، وفي لفظ: لا قضاء عليك، ورواه البزار بلفظ الجمع وزاد: فلا تفطر، وفي الصحيحين عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من نسي وهو صائم فأكل وشرب فليتم صومه فإنما أطعمه الله وسقاه . [إشراق الأبصار: ۲۹]
And that it is not deviated from qiyas, meaning the original ruling should not be contrary to qiyas; because if it itself, i.e., the ruling of the original, is contrary to qiyas, then how can something else be analogized to it? Like the continuation of fasting while eating or drinking forgetfully, for it is contrary to qiyas; because qiyas would require the invalidation of the fast, but we uphold it due to his saying (peace be upon him) to the one who ate forgetfully: 'Complete your fast, for Allah fed you and gave you drink.' ... The hadith is narrated by Ibn Hibban and al-Daraqutni, and in the Two Sahihs from Abu Hurayrah.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage presents the second condition for qiyas: the original ruling (asl) must not itself be an exception to general qiyas (i.e., it must not be ma'dulan 'an al-qiyas). If the ruling in the original case was established as an exception—deviating from what analogy would dictate—then it cannot be used as a basis for extending to other cases. The example is the validity of fasting despite eating or drinking forgetfully. According to qiyas, since the fast requires abstention, intentional or forgetful eating should break it. However, a specific hadith exempts the forgetful person: 'Complete your fast, for Allah fed you and gave you drink.' This ruling is an exception (istihsan) and thus cannot be analogized to other cases. The commentary also explains the linguistic points of the word 'halumma' and the hadith sources.

Key Terms
معدول به عن القياس (ma'dul bihi 'an al-qiyas): A ruling that deviates from the general principle of qiyas, i.e., an exception established by a specific textual proof (istihsan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the ruling of fasting while eating forgetfully not used as a basis for analogy?
A) Because the ruling is based on a weak hadith.
B) Because the ruling itself is an exception to qiyas, so it cannot be analogized.
C) Because the ruling only applies to the Prophet himself.
D) Because the ruling is only for a specific person.

Key Takeaway
A ruling that deviates from qiyas (istihsan) cannot be used as the original case in qiyas.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Original Must Not Be Contrary to Qiyas
Explains a condition of qiyas with examples and a madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify rulings that are exceptions to qiyas and explain why they cannot serve as the original (asl) in analogical deduction, and distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on analogizing from such rulings.

Core Idea
A ruling that is a special dispensation contrary to qiyas cannot be used as the asl in qiyas.

In usul al-fiqh, qiyas requires that the original case (asl) have a ruling established by a source that is consistent with general principles. If the asl itself is a deviation from qiyas—a rukhsah—then it cannot be extended to new cases via analogy. This lesson examines two prophetic examples and the ikhtilaf with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The passage states: 'the original should not be deviated from qiyas.' This means the asl must be a ruling that is in line with qiyas, not an exception.
This is part of the conditions of qiyas in Hanafi usul.
2
Analyze the Khuzaymah example
The Prophet accepted Khuzaymah's sole testimony as sufficient, contrary to the usual requirement of two witnesses. This was a special honor, not a rule to be analogized.
The text says 'so no one else is analogized to him.'
3
Analyze the forgetful fasting example
Fasting remains valid despite forgetful eating, which contradicts the qiyas that eating breaks the fast. But it is based on a specific hadith. Hence, it cannot be used as an asl to argue for the validity of fasting for the mistaken or coerced.
The Hanafi position is that the mistaken and coerced are aware of their actions, so they are not covered by the dispensation.
4
Understand the Shafi'i disagreement
Al-Shafi'i analogized the mistaken and coerced to the forgetful due to the perceived similarity in lacking intent to break the fast. The Hanafi response is that the forgetful lacks awareness, while the others are aware, so the ruling is specific.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi says the fast of mistaken/coerced is invalid; Shafi'i says it is valid.
5
Apply the condition to new cases
When encountering a hadith that seems to contradict qiyas, ask: is it a general rule or a specific dispensation? Only general rules can be analogized.
This prevents improper extension of rukhsas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
تعريف القياس وحكمه
بهذا الحكم. وقصته ما روي أن النبي عليا اشترى ناقة من أعرابي وأوفاه الثمن، فأنكر الأعرابي استيفاءه وقال: هَلُمَّ شهيدًا، فقال: من يشهد لي ولم يحضرني أحد؟ فقال خزيمة : أنا أشهد يا رسول الله أنك أوفيت الأعرابي ثمن الناقة، فقال عليه: "كيف تشهد لي ولم تحضرني؟" فقال: يا رسول الله إنا نصدقك فيما تأتينا به من خبر السماء، أفلا نصدقك فيما تخبر به من أداء ثمن الناقة؟ فقال عليه: "من شهد له خزيمة فهو حسبه"، فجعلت شهادته كشهادة رجلين كرامة وتفضيلاً على غيره مع أن النصوص أوجبت اشتراط العدد في حق العامة، فلا يقاس عليه غيره.
وأن لا يكون معدولاً به عن القياس، أي لا يكون الأصل مخالفا للقياس؛ إذ لو كان هو بنفسه أي حكم الأصل مخالفا للقياس فكيف يُقاس عليه غيره كبقاء الصوم مع الأكل أو الشرب ناسيا، فإنه مخالف للقياس؛ إذ القياس يقتضي فساد الصوم، وإنما أبقيناه لقوله عليه للذي أكل ناسيا : أتمّ على صومك فإنما أطعمك الله وسقاك الله.
فلا يقاس عليه الخاطئ والمكره كما قاسهما الشافعي
Chapter of Qiyas. Definition of Qiyas and its ruling. By this ruling. Its story is what was narrated: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) bought a she-camel from a Bedouin and paid him the price, but the Bedouin denied receiving it and said: 'Bring a witness.' He said: 'Who will testify for me when no one is present?' Khuzaymah said: 'I testify, O Messenger of Allah, that you paid the Bedouin the price of the she-camel.' He said: 'How can you testify for me when you were not present?' He said: 'O Messenger of Allah, we believe you in what you bring from the news of the heaven, so should we not believe you in what you inform about paying the price of the she-camel?' He said: 'Whoever has Khuzaymah as a witness is sufficient.' So his testimony was made like the testimony of two men as an honor and preference over others, despite the texts requiring the condition of number for the general public, so no one else is analogized to him. And that [the original] should not be deviated from qiyas, meaning the original should not be contrary to qiyas; because if it itself, i.e., the ruling of the original, is contrary to qiyas, then how can anything else be analogized to it? Like the continuation of fasting despite eating or drinking forgetfully, for it is contrary to qiyas, since qiyas would require the invalidity of fasting, but we maintained it due to his saying (peace be upon him) to the one who ate forgetfully: 'Complete your fast, for Allah fed you and gave you drink.' So the mistaken and coerced are not analogized to him, as al-Shafi'i analogized them.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on qiyas, discussing a key condition: the original (asl) must not be itself contrary to qiyas. The author gives two examples. First, the story of Khuzaymah: the Prophet accepted his sole testimony as equal to two witnesses, which is against the general rule requiring two witnesses. This special dispensation cannot be analogized to others because it is a specific honor. Second, the ruling that fasting remains valid if one eats or drinks forgetfully: qiyas would nullify the fast because eating and drinking break it, but a hadith exempts the forgetful. Therefore, this ruling cannot be used as a basis for analogizing other cases, such as the mistaken or coerced eater, who are aware of their action. The passage explicitly rejects the Shafi'i position that analogizes the mistaken and coerced to the forgetful.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to shared effective cause (illah).
الأصل (al-asl): The original case with a known ruling from the text.
معدولاً به عن القياس (ma'dūlan bihi 'an al-qiyās): A ruling that is deviated from qiyas, i.e., contrary to what analogy would require.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why cannot the ruling of Khuzaymah's testimony be analogized to other cases?
A) Because the Prophet allowed it for Khuzaymah only
B) Because the ruling is contrary to qiyas and is a specific honor
C) Because there is a consensus against it
D) Because Khuzaymah was a companion

Key Takeaway
The original case in qiyas must itself be in line with qiyas; exceptions and special dispensations (rukhsas) are binding only in their specific context and cannot be extended via analogy.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
The Four Sub-Conditions of Ta'diyah in Qiyas
Parsing the condition of ta'diyah into four sub-conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the four sub-conditions of ta'diyah to determine whether a ruling is transmissible via qiyas.

Core Idea
A ruling must be shar‘i, transferred exactly, to a counterpart branch with no existing text — four conditions under one.

Qiyas requires that the ruling from the original case (asl) be transmissible to a new case (far'). But this single condition of transmissibility actually comprises four essential sub-conditions. Understanding these will help you correctly apply qiyas only when the ruling is truly transferable.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the overarching condition
The passage states that the ruling must be transmissible from the asl to the far‘. This is one condition in name, but it bundles four requirements.
Think of ta'diyah as a package deal.
2
Extract sub-condition 1: Hukm is shar‘i
The ruling must be a legal (shar‘i) ruling, not a linguistic (lughawi) one. Only shar‘i rulings can be extended via qiyas.
Linguistic rulings (e.g., definition of a word) are not transferable.
3
Extract sub-condition 2: Transfer unchanged
The ruling must be transferred as it is, without any alteration (bi-la taghyir). The same hukm applies to the far‘, though its application may differ due to context.
We transfer the ruling, not its specific application details.
4
Extract sub-condition 3: Far‘ is a counterpart (nazir)
The far‘ must be a proper counterpart (nazir) to the asl, not inferior. A weaker far‘ would not justify the same ruling.
Nazir means equal in the effective cause (illah).
5
Extract sub-condition 4: No text in far‘
There must be no existing text (nass) in the far‘ that addresses the ruling. A contradictory text invalidates qiyas; a supportive text may not make qiyas futile, but it is debated.
If a text exists, qiyas is unnecessary or invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن يتعدّى الحكم الشرعي الثابت بالنص بعينه إلى فرع هو نظيره، ولا نص فيه، هذا الشرط وإن كان واحدًا تسمية لكنه يتضمن شروطا أربعة : أحدها: كون الحكم شرعيًا لا لغويًا، والثاني: تعديته بعينه بلا تغيير والثالث كون الفرع نظيرًا للأصل لا أدون منه، والرابع عدم وجود النص في الفرع. وقد فرّع المصنف له على كل من هذه الأربعة
And that the legal ruling established by the text itself should extend to a branch that is its counterpart, and there is no text in it. This condition, although one in name, includes four conditions: First: the ruling is legal, not linguistic. Second: its extension as it is without change. Third: the branch is a counterpart to the original, not inferior. Fourth: the absence of a text in the branch. The author has elaborated on each of these four.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage presents a key condition of qiyas: the ruling from the asl must be transmissible to a far' that is similar and has no text of its own. The author then explains that this single condition actually comprises four sub-conditions. The ruling must be a shar'i hukm (not a linguistic ruling), it must be transferred exactly without alteration (though its application may differ due to the different locus), the far' must be a proper counterpart (nazir) of the asl and not inferior, and there must be no existing text (nass) that governs the far'—neither a contradictory text (which would invalidate qiyas) nor a supportive text (which would make qiyas redundant, as the text suffices). The author notes that some scholars argue that a supportive text does not make qiyas futile since it reinforces the evidence.

Key Terms
تعدية (ta'diyah): The transfer of the ruling from the asl to the far' via qiyas.
نظير (nazir): A counterpart; the far' must be similar to the asl in the effective cause.
نص (nass): A clear textual ruling from the Quran or authentic Sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the four sub-conditions for a ruling to be transmissible via qiyas?
A) The ruling must be shar‘i.
B) The ruling must be transferred exactly as it is.
C) The far‘ must be a linguistic counterpart.
D) There must be no text in the far‘.

Key Takeaway
A ruling is transmissible via qiyas only if it is shar‘i, transferred exactly, to a counterpart branch with no contradictory text.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Definition of Qiyas and Its Four Conditions
Defining qiyas and its four required conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of qiyas, list its four conditions, and explain why each condition is necessary for valid analogical reasoning.

Core Idea
Qiyas extends a Shari ruling from an original to a branch only when four conditions are met.

Qiyas (analogical reasoning) is a fundamental source of Islamic law when no direct text exists. However, it is not a free exercise; it must satisfy strict conditions. This lesson explains the official Hanafi definition of qiyas and unpacks its four essential conditions: the ruling must be Shari, transferred exactly, the branch must be equivalent, and no text must exist in the branch.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of qiyas
Find the definition given in the text and identify its key components: extension of a Shari ruling from an original to a branch with no text.
The definition is concise: 'Extending a Shari ruling established by text itself to a branch that is its equivalent, and there is no text therein.'
2
List the four conditions
The text states that one condition implies four: Shari ruling, exact extension, equivalent branch, no text in branch.
3
Explain each condition
For each condition, explain why it is necessary: if the ruling is linguistic, qiyas cannot change language; if extended with change, a new ruling is created; if branch is lesser, the cause is not common; if text exists, qiyas is either invalid or unnecessary.
The text provides detailed justification for each.
4
Apply to the mistaken/coerced example
See how these conditions prevent qiyas from applying to the mistaken (khāṭi’) and coerced (mukrah) because they are not equivalent to the forgetful (nāsī) in the cause.
This illustrates the third condition.
5
Distinguish the forgetful case
The forgetful person is not liable because his action is attributed to Allah, based on the hadith, illustrating the condition of equivalent cause.
The hadith is cited as proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
تعريف القياس وحكمه
فلا يقاس عليه الخاطئ والمكره كما قاسهما الشافعي
وأن يتعدّى الحكم الشرعي الثابت بالنص بعينه إلى فرع هو نظيره، ولا نص فيه، هذا الشرط وإن كان واحدًا تسمية لكنه يتضمن شروطا أربعة : أحدها: كون الحكم شرعيًا لا لغويًا، والثاني: تعديته بعينه بلا تغيير والثالث كون الفرع نظيرًا للأصل لا أدون منه، والرابع عدم وجود النص في الفرع. وقد فرّع المصنف له على كل من هذه الأربعة
فلا يقاس إلخ على أنه ليس بينهما اشتراك في العلة، فإن الخاطئ ذاكر للصوم لكنه قاصر بضرب قصور كما إذا تمضمض ولم يثبت فدخل الماء في حلقه، والمكره أيضًا ذاكر للصوم ومختار في فعله، وأما الناسي فليس هو ذاكرًا للصوم، ولا يعلم أن هذا اليوم يوم الصوم، وكان فعله ليس بفعله، فليس هو تاركًا للكف بالأكل والشرب، وإليه أشار بقوله: "فإنما أطعمك الله وسقاك" أي هو الذي ألقى عليه النسيان حتى أكلت وشربت.
الخاطئ أي بالأكل في نهار رمضان.
والمكره أي بالأكل في نهار رمضان.
وأن يتعدّى إلخ المراد منه تصور التعدي فإنه شرط القياس، وأما حصول التعدي بالفعل فمن ثمرة القياس وأحكامه المترتبة عليه.
الثابت أي في الأصل المقيس عليه بالنص، أي بالكتاب أو السنة أو الإجماع بعينه، أي بلا تغيّر بزيادة وصف أو بنقصانه، وهذا متعلق لقوله وأن يتعدّى.
هو نظيره أي نظير الأصل في وجود العلة المشتركة
ولا نص فيه أي والحال أن لا يكون نص في الفرع، وهذا القول بإيراد لا التبرية إيماء إلى انتفاء النص مطلقًا، أي لا يكون فيه نص يكون حكمه مخالفًا لحكم القياس، ولا يكون فيه نص يكون حكمه موافقًا لحكم القياس، أما الأول؛ فلأنه لو كان فيه نص كذلك للزم بالقياس إبطال ذلك النص، وهو باطل، وأما الثاني؛ فلأن القياس مع وجود النص الكذائي تطويل بلا طائل؛ لأن النص يغني عن القياس وهذا ما ذهب إليه عامة أصحابنا ولك أن تقول: إن القياس حين وجود النص الموافق ليس تطويلا بلا طائل بل فائدته تعاضد الدليل بدليل فالقياس يكون معاضدًا للنص، وهذا ظاهر بلا شبهة، ألا ترى أن الشرع قد ورد بآيات كثيرة وأحاديث متعدّدة في حكم واحد.
كون الحكم: أي الذي تعدّى من الأصل إلى الفرع.
لا لغويًا فإنه لو كان الحكم لغويا فلا يجوز القياس؛ إذ وجود مناسبة العلة لا يوجب وضع اللفظ لغة، وأما الحكم العقلي فهو نظر الأصوليين، فلذا لم يذكر الشارح
بعينه إذ التعدية مع التغيّر إثبات حكم آخر في الفرع ابتداءً غير الحكم الثابت في الأصل، وهو باطل
بلا تغيير كإطلاقه وتقييده، نعم، إنما يقع التغيير باعتبار المحل، فإن محله الأصل فقط قبل القياس، وبعده صار محله الفرع
نظيراً للأصل لأنه لو لم يكن الفرع نظير الأصل في وجود العلة المشتركة كيف يتعدّى الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع؟ وهذا ظاهر.
تفريعا على ما سيأتي، وهذا هو رأي جمهور الأصوليين اقتداءً بفخر الإسلام له، وقد ابتدع بعض الشارحين فقال : إنه يتضمن ست شروط الأربعة منها هي والاثنان التعدية وكون الحكم الشرعي ثابتا بالنص لا فرعًا لشيء آخر، وهذا وإن كان مما يستقيم لكن ليست له ثمرة صحيحة فلا يستقيم التعليل لإثبات اسم الزنا للواطة؛ لأنه ليس بحكم شرعي، تفريع على أول الشرط، وهو كون الحكم شرعيًا، فإن الشافعي حلبه يقول: الزنا سفح ماءٍ محرم في محل مشتهى محرم، وهذا المعنى موجود في اللواطة، بل هي فوقه في الحرمة والشهوة وتضييع الماء، فيجري عليها اسم الزنا وحكمه وإليه ذهب أبو يوسف ومحمد جمالها، وهذا يسمى قياسًا في اللغة، ولكنه فُرّق بين أن يعطي للواطة اسم الزنا وبين أن يجري عليها حكمه فقط لأجل اشتراك العلة؛
وهذا أي تضمن هذا الشرط أربعة شروط.
التعدية إلخ المراد بالتعدية أن يثبت حكم الأصل للفرع، وليس المراد به أن ينتقل الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع فإن الحكم وصف، ونقل الأوصاف محال.
الحكم الشرعي: أي الذي في المقيس عليه.
بالنص : أي الكتاب أو السنة أو الإجماع.
لا فرعًا إلخ أي لا يكون الحكم الشرعي الذي في المقيس عليه فرعًا لشيء آخر بأن يكون ثابتا لقياس على شيء آخر؛ لأنه لو كان ذلك الحكم الشرعي ثابتا بالقياس فلا بد له من أصل، وهو الشيء الآخر من علته، فيقاس عليه بهذه العلة لا على هذا المقيس عليه الفرع، فإنه تطويل بلا طائل.
وهذا: أي تضمن هذا الشرط ست شروط.
لأنه أي لأن إثبات اسم الزنا للواطة.
بل هي: أي اللواطة فوق أي فوق الزنا في الحرمة، فإن الإيلاج في الدبر لا يحلّ قطعا، بخلاف الإيلاج في القبل فإنه يحل بالنكاح وملك اليمين والشهوة فإن المحل اليابس محل شهوة زائدة.
فيجري عليها إلخ فيدخل اللائط تحت قوله تعالى: ﴿الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ﴾ (النور: 2) فيجري عليه حكم الزنا أيضًا، فإن اللواطة حينئذ من أفراد الزنا لغة وقيل إن الشافعي حلبه أيضًا لا يجوز القياس في اللغة، وإنما أوجب الحدّ على اللائط بدلالة النص، لا أنه قياس في اللغة
وهذا [أي جريان اسم الزنا على اللواطة أولًا، وجريان حكم الزنا ثانيًا على جريان الاسم يسمى قياسا] قياسًا في اللغة والقياس في اللغة لا يجوز، وهو عبارة عن أن يوضع لفظ لمسمى مخصوص باعتبار معنى يوجد في غيره فيطلق ذلك اللفظ على ذلك الغير.
Chapter of Qiyas. Definition of Qiyas and its ruling. So the mistaken one and the coerced one are not analogized, as al-Shafi'i analogized them. And that the Shari ruling established by text itself be extended to a branch that is its equivalent, and there is no text therein. This condition, although one in name, implies four conditions: First: the ruling be a Shari ruling, not linguistic. Second: its extension takes place with the same ruling without change. Third: the branch is equivalent to the original, not lesser. Fourth: the absence of text regarding the branch. The author has branched off for each of these four... So it is not analogized, etc., indicating that there is no commonality in the cause between them. Indeed, the mistaken one is mindful of fasting but deficient in a certain way, like rinsing the mouth without swallowing, then water enters his throat. The coerced one is also mindful of fasting and has choice in his action. As for the forgetful one, he is not mindful of fasting, nor does he know that this day is a day of fasting, and his action is not considered his action; thus he is not refraining from eating and drinking. The Prophet alluded to this by his saying: "Indeed Allah fed you and gave you drink." i.e., He is the one who cast forgetfulness upon you until you ate and drank. The mistaken one: meaning by eating during the day of Ramadan. The coerced one: meaning by eating during the day of Ramadan. 'And that it be extended, etc.' — the intended meaning is the possibility of extension, for it is a condition of qiyas. As for the actual occurrence of extension, that is a result of qiyas and its rules. 'Established' i.e., in the original analogized upon by text, i.e., by the Book, Sunnah, or consensus, itself, i.e., without change by addition or reduction of a description; this relates to his statement 'and that it be extended.' 'It is its equivalent' i.e., equivalent to the original in the existence of the common cause. 'And there is no text therein' i.e., while there is no text in the branch. This statement with the word 'لا' (no) indicates the absolute absence of text, i.e., there is neither a text whose ruling contradicts the qiyas ruling nor a text whose ruling agrees with the qiyas ruling. As for the first, because if there were such a text, qiyas would necessitate nullifying that text, which is invalid. As for the second, because qiyas alongside such a text is useless prolongation; for the text renders qiyas unnecessary. This is the position of most of our companions. But you may say: qiyas when there is a supporting text is not useless prolongation; rather its benefit is strengthening the evidence with another evidence, so qiyas becomes a support for the text. This is clear without doubt. Do you not see that the Shariah has come with many verses and multiple hadiths concerning one ruling. 'That the ruling' i.e., which is transferred from the original to the branch. 'Not linguistic' because if the ruling were linguistic, qiyas would not be permitted; for the existence of a suitable cause does not necessitate the linguistic placement of the word. As for the rational ruling, it is the concern of the usuliyyun, so the commentator did not mention it. 'Itself' because extension with change establishes another ruling in the branch from the beginning, different from the ruling established in the original, which is invalid. 'Without change' such as its absolute or restricted form. Yes, change occurs only with respect to the place (mahall), for its place was only the original before qiyas, and after qiyas its place becomes the branch. 'Equivalent to the original' because if the branch were not equivalent to the original in the existence of the common cause, how could the ruling extend from the original to the branch? This is clear. Branching off based on what will come; this is the opinion of the majority of usuliyyun following Fakhr al-Islam. Some commentators have innovated by saying it includes six conditions, the four mentioned plus two: the extension and the fact that the Shari ruling is established by text, not being a branch of something else. But even if this is plausible, it has no correct result, so the reasoning to establish the name of zina for liwat cannot be sound because it is not a Shari ruling. Branching off from the first condition, which is that the ruling be Shari. Indeed, al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him, says: Zina is the emission of prohibited water in a prohibited place of desire. This meaning exists in liwat, rather it is above it in prohibition, desire, and waste of water. Thus the name of zina and its ruling apply to it. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may God have mercy on them, held this view. This is called qiyas in language, but it is distinguished between giving liwat the name of zina and applying its ruling only due to the commonality of cause. And this: meaning this condition implies four conditions. 'Extension etc.' — the intended meaning of extension is that the ruling of the original is established for the branch; it does not mean that the ruling transfers from the original to the branch, for a ruling is a description, and transfer of descriptions is impossible. 'The Shari ruling' i.e., that which is in the analogized-upon case. 'By text' i.e., the Book, Sunnah, or consensus. 'Not a branch etc.' i.e., the Shari ruling in the analogized-upon case should not be a branch of something else by being established on the basis of qiyas on something else; because if that ruling were established by qiyas, it must have an original, which is the other thing with its cause; then analogy is made to that other thing with this cause, not to this branch analogized-upon — that would be useless prolongation. And this: meaning this condition implies six conditions. 'Because it' i.e., because establishing the name of zina for liwat. 'Rather it is above' i.e., liwat is above zina in prohibition, because insertion in the anus is absolutely impermissible, unlike insertion in the front which is permissible by marriage and ownership of the right hand; and desire, because the dry place is a place of greater desire. 'Thus it applies, etc.' so the one who commits liwat falls under the verse: "The female and male fornicators, flog each of them one hundred lashes" (Quran 24:2); thus the ruling of zina applies to him as well. Then liwat would be a member of zina linguistically. It is said that al-Shafi'i also does not permit qiyas in language; rather he mandated the hadd punishment for the one who commits liwat by textual indication, not by qiyas in language. And this [i.e., the application of the name of zina to liwat first, and then the application of the ruling of zina after the application of the name] is called qiyas in language, and qiyas in language is not permissible. It is defined as a word placed for a specific meaning based on a meaning found in another, so that word is applied to that other.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition and conditions of Qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul. It begins with the statement that qiyas is not applied to the mistaken (khāṭi’) or coerced (mukrah) person, contrary to Imam Shafi'i who extended the ruling to them. The reason is that these individuals are mindful of fasting but act involuntarily, unlike the forgetful (nāsī) who is not considered to have broken the fast by eating, based on the hadith 'Indeed Allah fed you and gave you drink.' The text then presents the four conditions for valid qiyas: (1) the ruling must be a Shari ruling (not linguistic or rational), (2) it must be extended exactly without change, (3) the branch must be equivalent to the original in cause, and (4) there must be no text (either contradicting or supporting) in the branch. The commentator notes that although these are listed as one condition, they actually encompass four. A dispute arises with some scholars who add two more conditions, but the author dismisses this as fruitless. The passage then discusses the controversial issue of liwāṭ (sodomy) and whether it can be analogized to zinā (fornication) linguistically, as held by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The Shafi'i position is that qiyas in language is invalid, and the hadd punishment for liwāṭ is based on textual indication (dalālat al-nass) rather than analogical extension of the term 'zinā'. The Hanafi authorities cited (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider liwāṭ as falling under the linguistic meaning of zinā, thereby subjecting it to the same ruling. The commentary emphasizes that qiyas in language is not the same as qiyas in Shari rulings; the former is not accepted in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Extending a Shari ruling established by text from an original case to a branch case that shares a common cause (ʿilla) and for which no text exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this lesson, if a text exists in the branch that supports the same ruling as the qiyas, what should be done?
A) Use qiyas to strengthen the text.
B) Do not use qiyas because the text renders it unnecessary.
C) Use qiyas only if the text is from the Quran.
D) Use qiyas to override the text if there is a conflict.

Key Takeaway
Valid qiyas requires that the ruling be Shari, extended exactly, the branch equivalent in cause, and no text existing in the branch.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Why Qiyas Does Not Apply to the Mistaken and Coerced: The Forgetful Person's Exception
Inter-madhhab dispute on the fasting of the mistaken and coerced

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi condition of equivalent cause to distinguish the forgetful person (nāsī) from the mistaken (khāṭi’) and coerced (mukrah), and cite the hadith that supports this distinction.

Core Idea
The forgetful person’s fast is valid because his action is attributed to Allah; the mistaken and coerced are not equivalent.

The text uses the case of a person who eats while fasting to illustrate the condition that the branch must be equivalent to the original in the cause. The forgetful person (nāsī) is excused because his eating is attributed to Allah, whereas the mistaken (khāṭi’) and coerced (mukrah) are mindful and their actions are their own. This lesson examines the hadith evidence and the Hanafi position that Shafi'i's analogy is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Understand the definitions of nāsī, khāṭi’, and mukrah given in the text.
nāsī = forgetful; khāṭi’ = mistaken; mukrah = coerced.
2
Find the hadith
Locate the hadith 'إنما أطعمك الله وسقاك' and note its chain (at least zanni thubut).
The hadith is from al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah, etc.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove that the nāsī is not liable? It attributes the eating to Allah.
The phrase 'أطعمك الله' indicates Allah caused the eating, so no sin or expiation.
4
Compare the khāṭi’ and mukrah
Why are they not analogous? Because they are mindful and have choice, so the ruling does not transfer.
The text says the khāṭi’ is 'dhākir' (mindful) and the mukrah is 'mukhtār' (has choice).
5
Contrast with Shafi'i
Shafi'i analogizes them to the nāsī; the Hanafi response is that the cause (being non-deliberate) is not present in the khāṭi’ and mukrah.
The Hanafi position is that qiyas does not apply here.

فلا يقاس عليه الخاطئ والمكره كما قاسهما الشافعي
وأن يتعدّى الحكم الشرعي الثابت بالنص بعينه إلى فرع هو نظيره، ولا نص فيه، هذا الشرط وإن كان واحدًا تسمية لكنه يتضمن شروطا أربعة : أحدها: كون الحكم شرعيًا لا لغويًا، والثاني: تعديته بعينه بلا تغيير والثالث كون الفرع نظيرًا للأصل لا أدون منه، والرابع عدم وجود النص في الفرع. وقد فرّع المصنف له على كل من هذه الأربعة
فلا يقاس إلخ على أنه ليس بينهما اشتراك في العلة، فإن الخاطئ ذاكر للصوم لكنه قاصر بضرب قصور كما إذا تمضمض ولم يثبت فدخل الماء في حلقه، والمكره أيضًا ذاكر للصوم ومختار في فعله، وأما الناسي فليس هو ذاكرًا للصوم، ولا يعلم أن هذا اليوم يوم الصوم، وكان فعله ليس بفعله، فليس هو تاركًا للكف بالأكل والشرب، وإليه أشار بقوله: "فإنما أطعمك الله وسقاك" أي هو الذي ألقى عليه النسيان حتى أكلت وشربت.
الخاطئ أي بالأكل في نهار رمضان.
والمكره أي بالأكل في نهار رمضان.
وأن يتعدّى إلخ المراد منه تصور التعدي فإنه شرط القياس، وأما حصول التعدي بالفعل فمن ثمرة القياس وأحكامه المترتبة عليه.
الثابت أي في الأصل المقيس عليه بالنص، أي بالكتاب أو السنة أو الإجماع بعينه، أي بلا تغيّر بزيادة وصف أو بنقصانه، وهذا متعلق لقوله وأن يتعدّى.
هو نظيره أي نظير الأصل في وجود العلة المشتركة
ولا نص فيه أي والحال أن لا يكون نص في الفرع، وهذا القول بإيراد لا التبرية إيماء إلى انتفاء النص مطلقًا، أي لا يكون فيه نص يكون حكمه مخالفًا لحكم القياس، ولا يكون فيه نص يكون حكمه موافقًا لحكم القياس، أما الأول؛ فلأنه لو كان فيه نص كذلك للزم بالقياس إبطال ذلك النص، وهو باطل، وأما الثاني؛ فلأن القياس مع وجود النص الكذائي تطويل بلا طائل؛ لأن النص يغني عن القياس وهذا ما ذهب إليه عامة أصحابنا ولك أن تقول: إن القياس حين وجود النص الموافق ليس تطويلا بلا طائل بل فائدته تعاضد الدليل بدليل فالقياس يكون معاضدًا للنص، وهذا ظاهر بلا شبهة، ألا ترى أن الشرع قد ورد بآيات كثيرة وأحاديث متعدّدة في حكم واحد.
كون الحكم: أي الذي تعدّى من الأصل إلى الفرع.
لا لغويًا فإنه لو كان الحكم لغويا فلا يجوز القياس؛ إذ وجود مناسبة العلة لا يوجب وضع اللفظ لغة، وأما الحكم العقلي فهو نظر الأصوليين، فلذا لم يذكر الشارح
بعينه إذ التعدية مع التغيّر إثبات حكم آخر في الفرع ابتداءً غير الحكم الثابت في الأصل، وهو باطل
بلا تغيير كإطلاقه وتقييده، نعم، إنما يقع التغيير باعتبار المحل، فإن محله الأصل فقط قبل القياس، وبعده صار محله الفرع
نظيراً للأصل لأنه لو لم يكن الفرع نظير الأصل في وجود العلة المشتركة كيف يتعدّى الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع؟ وهذا ظاهر.
تفريعا على ما سيأتي، وهذا هو رأي جمهور الأصوليين اقتداءً بفخر الإسلام له، وقد ابتدع بعض الشارحين فقال : إنه يتضمن ست شروط الأربعة منها هي والاثنان التعدية وكون الحكم الشرعي ثابتا بالنص لا فرعًا لشيء آخر، وهذا وإن كان مما يستقيم لكن ليست له ثمرة صحيحة فلا يستقيم التعليل لإثبات اسم الزنا للواطة؛ لأنه ليس بحكم شرعي، تفريع على أول الشرط، وهو كون الحكم شرعيًا، فإن الشافعي حلبه يقول: الزنا سفح ماءٍ محرم في محل مشتهى محرم، وهذا المعنى موجود في اللواطة، بل هي فوقه في الحرمة والشهوة وتضييع الماء، فيجري عليها اسم الزنا وحكمه وإليه ذهب أبو يوسف ومحمد جمالها، وهذا يسمى قياسًا في اللغة، ولكنه فُرّق بين أن يعطي للواطة اسم الزنا وبين أن يجري عليها حكمه فقط لأجل اشتراك العلة؛
وهذا أي تضمن هذا الشرط أربعة شروط.
التعدية إلخ المراد بالتعدية أن يثبت حكم الأصل للفرع، وليس المراد به أن ينتقل الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع فإن الحكم وصف، ونقل الأوصاف محال.
الحكم الشرعي: أي الذي في المقيس عليه.
بالنص : أي الكتاب أو السنة أو الإجماع.
لا فرعًا إلخ أي لا يكون الحكم الشرعي الذي في المقيس عليه فرعًا لشيء آخر بأن يكون ثابتا لقياس على شيء آخر؛ لأنه لو كان ذلك الحكم الشرعي ثابتا بالقياس فلا بد له من أصل، وهو الشيء الآخر من علته، فيقاس عليه بهذه العلة لا على هذا المقيس عليه الفرع، فإنه تطويل بلا طائل.
وهذا: أي تضمن هذا الشرط ست شروط.
لأنه أي لأن إثبات اسم الزنا للواطة.
بل هي: أي اللواطة فوق أي فوق الزنا في الحرمة، فإن الإيلاج في الدبر لا يحلّ قطعا، بخلاف الإيلاج في القبل فإنه يحل بالنكاح وملك اليمين والشهوة فإن المحل اليابس محل شهوة زائدة.
فيجري عليها إلخ فيدخل اللائط تحت قوله تعالى: ﴿الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ﴾ (النور: 2) فيجري عليه حكم الزنا أيضًا، فإن اللواطة حينئذ من أفراد الزنا لغة وقيل إن الشافعي حلبه أيضًا لا يجوز القياس في اللغة، وإنما أوجب الحدّ على اللائط بدلالة النص، لا أنه قياس في اللغة
وهذا [أي جريان اسم الزنا على اللواطة أولًا، وجريان حكم الزنا ثانيًا على جريان الاسم يسمى قياسا] قياسًا في اللغة والقياس في اللغة لا يجوز، وهو عبارة عن أن يوضع لفظ لمسمى مخصوص باعتبار معنى يوجد في غيره فيطلق ذلك اللفظ على ذلك الغير.
Chapter of Qiyas. Definition of Qiyas and its ruling. So the mistaken one and the coerced one are not analogized, as al-Shafi'i analogized them. And that the Shari ruling established by text itself be extended to a branch that is its equivalent, and there is no text therein. This condition, although one in name, implies four conditions: First: the ruling be a Shari ruling, not linguistic. Second: its extension takes place with the same ruling without change. Third: the branch is equivalent to the original, not lesser. Fourth: the absence of text regarding the branch. The author has branched off for each of these four... So it is not analogized, etc., indicating that there is no commonality in the cause between them. Indeed, the mistaken one is mindful of fasting but deficient in a certain way, like rinsing the mouth without swallowing, then water enters his throat. The coerced one is also mindful of fasting and has choice in his action. As for the forgetful one, he is not mindful of fasting, nor does he know that this day is a day of fasting, and his action is not considered his action; thus he is not refraining from eating and drinking. The Prophet alluded to this by his saying: "Indeed Allah fed you and gave you drink." i.e., He is the one who cast forgetfulness upon you until you ate and drank. The mistaken one: meaning by eating during the day of Ramadan. The coerced one: meaning by eating during the day of Ramadan. 'And that it be extended, etc.' — the intended meaning is the possibility of extension, for it is a condition of qiyas. As for the actual occurrence of extension, that is a result of qiyas and its rules. 'Established' i.e., in the original analogized upon by text, i.e., by the Book, Sunnah, or consensus, itself, i.e., without change by addition or reduction of a description; this relates to his statement 'and that it be extended.' 'It is its equivalent' i.e., equivalent to the original in the existence of the common cause. 'And there is no text therein' i.e., while there is no text in the branch. This statement with the word 'لا' (no) indicates the absolute absence of text, i.e., there is neither a text whose ruling contradicts the qiyas ruling nor a text whose ruling agrees with the qiyas ruling. As for the first, because if there were such a text, qiyas would necessitate nullifying that text, which is invalid. As for the second, because qiyas alongside such a text is useless prolongation; for the text renders qiyas unnecessary. This is the position of most of our companions. But you may say: qiyas when there is a supporting text is not useless prolongation; rather its benefit is strengthening the evidence with another evidence, so qiyas becomes a support for the text. This is clear without doubt. Do you not see that the Shariah has come with many verses and multiple hadiths concerning one ruling. 'That the ruling' i.e., which is transferred from the original to the branch. 'Not linguistic' because if the ruling were linguistic, qiyas would not be permitted; for the existence of a suitable cause does not necessitate the linguistic placement of the word. As for the rational ruling, it is the concern of the usuliyyun, so the commentator did not mention it. 'Itself' because extension with change establishes another ruling in the branch from the beginning, different from the ruling established in the original, which is invalid. 'Without change' such as its absolute or restricted form. Yes, change occurs only with respect to the place (mahall), for its place was only the original before qiyas, and after qiyas its place becomes the branch. 'Equivalent to the original' because if the branch were not equivalent to the original in the existence of the common cause, how could the ruling extend from the original to the branch? This is clear. Branching off based on what will come; this is the opinion of the majority of usuliyyun following Fakhr al-Islam. Some commentators have innovated by saying it includes six conditions, the four mentioned plus two: the extension and the fact that the Shari ruling is established by text, not being a branch of something else. But even if this is plausible, it has no correct result, so the reasoning to establish the name of zina for liwat cannot be sound because it is not a Shari ruling. Branching off from the first condition, which is that the ruling be Shari. Indeed, al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him, says: Zina is the emission of prohibited water in a prohibited place of desire. This meaning exists in liwat, rather it is above it in prohibition, desire, and waste of water. Thus the name of zina and its ruling apply to it. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may God have mercy on them, held this view. This is called qiyas in language, but it is distinguished between giving liwat the name of zina and applying its ruling only due to the commonality of cause. And this: meaning this condition implies four conditions. 'Extension etc.' — the intended meaning of extension is that the ruling of the original is established for the branch; it does not mean that the ruling transfers from the original to the branch, for a ruling is a description, and transfer of descriptions is impossible. 'The Shari ruling' i.e., that which is in the analogized-upon case. 'By text' i.e., the Book, Sunnah, or consensus. 'Not a branch etc.' i.e., the Shari ruling in the analogized-upon case should not be a branch of something else by being established on the basis of qiyas on something else; because if that ruling were established by qiyas, it must have an original, which is the other thing with its cause; then analogy is made to that other thing with this cause, not to this branch analogized-upon — that would be useless prolongation. And this: meaning this condition implies six conditions. 'Because it' i.e., because establishing the name of zina for liwat. 'Rather it is above' i.e., liwat is above zina in prohibition, because insertion in the anus is absolutely impermissible, unlike insertion in the front which is permissible by marriage and ownership of the right hand; and desire, because the dry place is a place of greater desire. 'Thus it applies, etc.' so the one who commits liwat falls under the verse: "The female and male fornicators, flog each of them one hundred lashes" (Quran 24:2); thus the ruling of zina applies to him as well. Then liwat would be a member of zina linguistically. It is said that al-Shafi'i also does not permit qiyas in language; rather he mandated the hadd punishment for the one who commits liwat by textual indication, not by qiyas in language. And this [i.e., the application of the name of zina to liwat first, and then the application of the ruling of zina after the application of the name] is called qiyas in language, and qiyas in language is not permissible. It is defined as a word placed for a specific meaning based on a meaning found in another, so that word is applied to that other.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition and conditions of Qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul. It begins with the statement that qiyas is not applied to the mistaken (khāṭi’) or coerced (mukrah) person, contrary to Imam Shafi'i who extended the ruling to them. The reason is that these individuals are mindful of fasting but act involuntarily, unlike the forgetful (nāsī) who is not considered to have broken the fast by eating, based on the hadith 'Indeed Allah fed you and gave you drink.' The text then presents the four conditions for valid qiyas: (1) the ruling must be a Shari ruling (not linguistic or rational), (2) it must be extended exactly without change, (3) the branch must be equivalent to the original in cause, and (4) there must be no text (either contradicting or supporting) in the branch. The commentator notes that although these are listed as one condition, they actually encompass four. A dispute arises with some scholars who add two more conditions, but the author dismisses this as fruitless. The passage then discusses the controversial issue of liwāṭ (sodomy) and whether it can be analogized to zinā (fornication) linguistically, as held by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The Shafi'i position is that qiyas in language is invalid, and the hadd punishment for liwāṭ is based on textual indication (dalālat al-nass) rather than analogical extension of the term 'zinā'. The Hanafi authorities cited (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider liwāṭ as falling under the linguistic meaning of zinā, thereby subjecting it to the same ruling. The commentary emphasizes that qiyas in language is not the same as qiyas in Shari rulings; the former is not accepted in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الخاطئ (al-khāṭi’): One who mistakenly does something prohibited while believing it permissible; here, one who eats during Ramadan mistakenly thinking it is not a fast day.
المكره (al-mukrah): One coerced into performing an act under threat; here, forced to eat during Ramadan.
الناسي (al-nāsī): One who forgets he is fasting and eats; his fast remains valid and no expiation required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, what is the ruling on a person who is forced to eat while fasting (mukrah)?
A) His fast remains valid like the forgetful person.
B) His fast is broken and he must make up the day.
C) He is excused because he had no choice.
D) He must make up the day and also perform expiation.

Key Takeaway
The forgetful person's fast is valid because of the hadith; the mistaken and coerced cannot be analogized due to the condition of equivalent cause.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
12 min
Qiyas in Language: The Case of Liwāṭ and the Dispute with Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on qiyas in language and hadd for liwāṭ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that liwāṭ falls under the linguistic meaning of zinā and thus carries the same hadd penalty, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position that qiyas in language is invalid.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that liwāṭ is included under the linguistic meaning of zinā, so the hadd of one hundred lashes applies.

The text extends the discussion of qiyas conditions to a controversial issue: whether the term 'zinā' in the Quran includes liwāṭ (sodomy). Some commentators attempted to add two extra conditions, but the author dismisses this as fruitless. The passage then presents the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that liwāṭ is a linguistic extension of zinā, while Shafi'i rejects qiyas in language and relies on textual indication (dalālat al-nass).

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The passage discusses whether qiyas in language is permissible and whether liwāṭ falls under the name and ruling of zinā.
2
State the Hanafi position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say yes because the same meaning (safḥ māʿ in mahall mushtahā muḥarram) exists.
The text says 'بل هي فوقه في الحرمة والشهوة' – liwāṭ is even stronger in prohibition.
3
Examine the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i does not permit qiyas in language; the hadd for liwāṭ comes from textual indication.
The text says 'وإنما أوجب الحدّ على اللائط بدلالة النص'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The verse 'الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي' is general; liwāṭ is included linguistically.
The Hanafi view is that the term 'zinā' linguistically covers any unlawful sexual intercourse.
5
Determine the practical difference
If qiyas in language is accepted, the hadd is one hundred lashes; if not, another evidence is needed.
Shafi'i uses dalālat al-nass, which may lead to the same hadd but via different reasoning.

باب القياس
تعريف القياس وحكمه
فلا يقاس عليه الخاطئ والمكره كما قاسهما الشافعي
وأن يتعدّى الحكم الشرعي الثابت بالنص بعينه إلى فرع هو نظيره، ولا نص فيه، هذا الشرط وإن كان واحدًا تسمية لكنه يتضمن شروطا أربعة : أحدها: كون الحكم شرعيًا لا لغويًا، والثاني: تعديته بعينه بلا تغيير والثالث كون الفرع نظيرًا للأصل لا أدون منه، والرابع عدم وجود النص في الفرع. وقد فرّع المصنف له على كل من هذه الأربعة
فلا يقاس إلخ على أنه ليس بينهما اشتراك في العلة، فإن الخاطئ ذاكر للصوم لكنه قاصر بضرب قصور كما إذا تمضمض ولم يثبت فدخل الماء في حلقه، والمكره أيضًا ذاكر للصوم ومختار في فعله، وأما الناسي فليس هو ذاكرًا للصوم، ولا يعلم أن هذا اليوم يوم الصوم، وكان فعله ليس بفعله، فليس هو تاركًا للكف بالأكل والشرب، وإليه أشار بقوله: "فإنما أطعمك الله وسقاك" أي هو الذي ألقى عليه النسيان حتى أكلت وشربت.
الخاطئ أي بالأكل في نهار رمضان.
والمكره أي بالأكل في نهار رمضان.
وأن يتعدّى إلخ المراد منه تصور التعدي فإنه شرط القياس، وأما حصول التعدي بالفعل فمن ثمرة القياس وأحكامه المترتبة عليه.
الثابت أي في الأصل المقيس عليه بالنص، أي بالكتاب أو السنة أو الإجماع بعينه، أي بلا تغيّر بزيادة وصف أو بنقصانه، وهذا متعلق لقوله وأن يتعدّى.
هو نظيره أي نظير الأصل في وجود العلة المشتركة
ولا نص فيه أي والحال أن لا يكون نص في الفرع، وهذا القول بإيراد لا التبرية إيماء إلى انتفاء النص مطلقًا، أي لا يكون فيه نص يكون حكمه مخالفًا لحكم القياس، ولا يكون فيه نص يكون حكمه موافقًا لحكم القياس، أما الأول؛ فلأنه لو كان فيه نص كذلك للزم بالقياس إبطال ذلك النص، وهو باطل، وأما الثاني؛ فلأن القياس مع وجود النص الكذائي تطويل بلا طائل؛ لأن النص يغني عن القياس وهذا ما ذهب إليه عامة أصحابنا ولك أن تقول: إن القياس حين وجود النص الموافق ليس تطويلا بلا طائل بل فائدته تعاضد الدليل بدليل فالقياس يكون معاضدًا للنص، وهذا ظاهر بلا شبهة، ألا ترى أن الشرع قد ورد بآيات كثيرة وأحاديث متعدّدة في حكم واحد.
كون الحكم: أي الذي تعدّى من الأصل إلى الفرع.
لا لغويًا فإنه لو كان الحكم لغويا فلا يجوز القياس؛ إذ وجود مناسبة العلة لا يوجب وضع اللفظ لغة، وأما الحكم العقلي فهو نظر الأصوليين، فلذا لم يذكر الشارح
بعينه إذ التعدية مع التغيّر إثبات حكم آخر في الفرع ابتداءً غير الحكم الثابت في الأصل، وهو باطل
بلا تغيير كإطلاقه وتقييده، نعم، إنما يقع التغيير باعتبار المحل، فإن محله الأصل فقط قبل القياس، وبعده صار محله الفرع
نظيراً للأصل لأنه لو لم يكن الفرع نظير الأصل في وجود العلة المشتركة كيف يتعدّى الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع؟ وهذا ظاهر.
تفريعا على ما سيأتي، وهذا هو رأي جمهور الأصوليين اقتداءً بفخر الإسلام له، وقد ابتدع بعض الشارحين فقال : إنه يتضمن ست شروط الأربعة منها هي والاثنان التعدية وكون الحكم الشرعي ثابتا بالنص لا فرعًا لشيء آخر، وهذا وإن كان مما يستقيم لكن ليست له ثمرة صحيحة فلا يستقيم التعليل لإثبات اسم الزنا للواطة؛ لأنه ليس بحكم شرعي، تفريع على أول الشرط، وهو كون الحكم شرعيًا، فإن الشافعي حلبه يقول: الزنا سفح ماءٍ محرم في محل مشتهى محرم، وهذا المعنى موجود في اللواطة، بل هي فوقه في الحرمة والشهوة وتضييع الماء، فيجري عليها اسم الزنا وحكمه وإليه ذهب أبو يوسف ومحمد جمالها، وهذا يسمى قياسًا في اللغة، ولكنه فُرّق بين أن يعطي للواطة اسم الزنا وبين أن يجري عليها حكمه فقط لأجل اشتراك العلة؛
وهذا أي تضمن هذا الشرط أربعة شروط.
التعدية إلخ المراد بالتعدية أن يثبت حكم الأصل للفرع، وليس المراد به أن ينتقل الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع فإن الحكم وصف، ونقل الأوصاف محال.
الحكم الشرعي: أي الذي في المقيس عليه.
بالنص : أي الكتاب أو السنة أو الإجماع.
لا فرعًا إلخ أي لا يكون الحكم الشرعي الذي في المقيس عليه فرعًا لشيء آخر بأن يكون ثابتا لقياس على شيء آخر؛ لأنه لو كان ذلك الحكم الشرعي ثابتا بالقياس فلا بد له من أصل، وهو الشيء الآخر من علته، فيقاس عليه بهذه العلة لا على هذا المقيس عليه الفرع، فإنه تطويل بلا طائل.
وهذا: أي تضمن هذا الشرط ست شروط.
لأنه أي لأن إثبات اسم الزنا للواطة.
بل هي: أي اللواطة فوق أي فوق الزنا في الحرمة، فإن الإيلاج في الدبر لا يحلّ قطعا، بخلاف الإيلاج في القبل فإنه يحل بالنكاح وملك اليمين والشهوة فإن المحل اليابس محل شهوة زائدة.
فيجري عليها إلخ فيدخل اللائط تحت قوله تعالى: ﴿الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ﴾ (النور: 2) فيجري عليه حكم الزنا أيضًا، فإن اللواطة حينئذ من أفراد الزنا لغة وقيل إن الشافعي حلبه أيضًا لا يجوز القياس في اللغة، وإنما أوجب الحدّ على اللائط بدلالة النص، لا أنه قياس في اللغة
وهذا [أي جريان اسم الزنا على اللواطة أولًا، وجريان حكم الزنا ثانيًا على جريان الاسم يسمى قياسا] قياسًا في اللغة والقياس في اللغة لا يجوز، وهو عبارة عن أن يوضع لفظ لمسمى مخصوص باعتبار معنى يوجد في غيره فيطلق ذلك اللفظ على ذلك الغير.
Chapter of Qiyas. Definition of Qiyas and its ruling. So the mistaken one and the coerced one are not analogized, as al-Shafi'i analogized them. And that the Shari ruling established by text itself be extended to a branch that is its equivalent, and there is no text therein. This condition, although one in name, implies four conditions: First: the ruling be a Shari ruling, not linguistic. Second: its extension takes place with the same ruling without change. Third: the branch is equivalent to the original, not lesser. Fourth: the absence of text regarding the branch. The author has branched off for each of these four... So it is not analogized, etc., indicating that there is no commonality in the cause between them. Indeed, the mistaken one is mindful of fasting but deficient in a certain way, like rinsing the mouth without swallowing, then water enters his throat. The coerced one is also mindful of fasting and has choice in his action. As for the forgetful one, he is not mindful of fasting, nor does he know that this day is a day of fasting, and his action is not considered his action; thus he is not refraining from eating and drinking. The Prophet alluded to this by his saying: "Indeed Allah fed you and gave you drink." i.e., He is the one who cast forgetfulness upon you until you ate and drank. The mistaken one: meaning by eating during the day of Ramadan. The coerced one: meaning by eating during the day of Ramadan. 'And that it be extended, etc.' — the intended meaning is the possibility of extension, for it is a condition of qiyas. As for the actual occurrence of extension, that is a result of qiyas and its rules. 'Established' i.e., in the original analogized upon by text, i.e., by the Book, Sunnah, or consensus, itself, i.e., without change by addition or reduction of a description; this relates to his statement 'and that it be extended.' 'It is its equivalent' i.e., equivalent to the original in the existence of the common cause. 'And there is no text therein' i.e., while there is no text in the branch. This statement with the word 'لا' (no) indicates the absolute absence of text, i.e., there is neither a text whose ruling contradicts the qiyas ruling nor a text whose ruling agrees with the qiyas ruling. As for the first, because if there were such a text, qiyas would necessitate nullifying that text, which is invalid. As for the second, because qiyas alongside such a text is useless prolongation; for the text renders qiyas unnecessary. This is the position of most of our companions. But you may say: qiyas when there is a supporting text is not useless prolongation; rather its benefit is strengthening the evidence with another evidence, so qiyas becomes a support for the text. This is clear without doubt. Do you not see that the Shariah has come with many verses and multiple hadiths concerning one ruling. 'That the ruling' i.e., which is transferred from the original to the branch. 'Not linguistic' because if the ruling were linguistic, qiyas would not be permitted; for the existence of a suitable cause does not necessitate the linguistic placement of the word. As for the rational ruling, it is the concern of the usuliyyun, so the commentator did not mention it. 'Itself' because extension with change establishes another ruling in the branch from the beginning, different from the ruling established in the original, which is invalid. 'Without change' such as its absolute or restricted form. Yes, change occurs only with respect to the place (mahall), for its place was only the original before qiyas, and after qiyas its place becomes the branch. 'Equivalent to the original' because if the branch were not equivalent to the original in the existence of the common cause, how could the ruling extend from the original to the branch? This is clear. Branching off based on what will come; this is the opinion of the majority of usuliyyun following Fakhr al-Islam. Some commentators have innovated by saying it includes six conditions, the four mentioned plus two: the extension and the fact that the Shari ruling is established by text, not being a branch of something else. But even if this is plausible, it has no correct result, so the reasoning to establish the name of zina for liwat cannot be sound because it is not a Shari ruling. Branching off from the first condition, which is that the ruling be Shari. Indeed, al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him, says: Zina is the emission of prohibited water in a prohibited place of desire. This meaning exists in liwat, rather it is above it in prohibition, desire, and waste of water. Thus the name of zina and its ruling apply to it. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may God have mercy on them, held this view. This is called qiyas in language, but it is distinguished between giving liwat the name of zina and applying its ruling only due to the commonality of cause. And this: meaning this condition implies four conditions. 'Extension etc.' — the intended meaning of extension is that the ruling of the original is established for the branch; it does not mean that the ruling transfers from the original to the branch, for a ruling is a description, and transfer of descriptions is impossible. 'The Shari ruling' i.e., that which is in the analogized-upon case. 'By text' i.e., the Book, Sunnah, or consensus. 'Not a branch etc.' i.e., the Shari ruling in the analogized-upon case should not be a branch of something else by being established on the basis of qiyas on something else; because if that ruling were established by qiyas, it must have an original, which is the other thing with its cause; then analogy is made to that other thing with this cause, not to this branch analogized-upon — that would be useless prolongation. And this: meaning this condition implies six conditions. 'Because it' i.e., because establishing the name of zina for liwat. 'Rather it is above' i.e., liwat is above zina in prohibition, because insertion in the anus is absolutely impermissible, unlike insertion in the front which is permissible by marriage and ownership of the right hand; and desire, because the dry place is a place of greater desire. 'Thus it applies, etc.' so the one who commits liwat falls under the verse: "The female and male fornicators, flog each of them one hundred lashes" (Quran 24:2); thus the ruling of zina applies to him as well. Then liwat would be a member of zina linguistically. It is said that al-Shafi'i also does not permit qiyas in language; rather he mandated the hadd punishment for the one who commits liwat by textual indication, not by qiyas in language. And this [i.e., the application of the name of zina to liwat first, and then the application of the ruling of zina after the application of the name] is called qiyas in language, and qiyas in language is not permissible. It is defined as a word placed for a specific meaning based on a meaning found in another, so that word is applied to that other.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition and conditions of Qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul. It begins with the statement that qiyas is not applied to the mistaken (khāṭi’) or coerced (mukrah) person, contrary to Imam Shafi'i who extended the ruling to them. The reason is that these individuals are mindful of fasting but act involuntarily, unlike the forgetful (nāsī) who is not considered to have broken the fast by eating, based on the hadith 'Indeed Allah fed you and gave you drink.' The text then presents the four conditions for valid qiyas: (1) the ruling must be a Shari ruling (not linguistic or rational), (2) it must be extended exactly without change, (3) the branch must be equivalent to the original in cause, and (4) there must be no text (either contradicting or supporting) in the branch. The commentator notes that although these are listed as one condition, they actually encompass four. A dispute arises with some scholars who add two more conditions, but the author dismisses this as fruitless. The passage then discusses the controversial issue of liwāṭ (sodomy) and whether it can be analogized to zinā (fornication) linguistically, as held by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The Shafi'i position is that qiyas in language is invalid, and the hadd punishment for liwāṭ is based on textual indication (dalālat al-nass) rather than analogical extension of the term 'zinā'. The Hanafi authorities cited (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider liwāṭ as falling under the linguistic meaning of zinā, thereby subjecting it to the same ruling. The commentary emphasizes that qiyas in language is not the same as qiyas in Shari rulings; the former is not accepted in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Extending a Shari ruling established by text from an original case to a branch case that shares a common cause (ʿilla) and for which no text exists.
اللواطة (al-liwāṭ): Sodomy; the act of anal intercourse between males.
الزنا (al-zinā): Unlawful sexual intercourse; traditionally defined as vaginal intercourse, but extended linguistically by some Hanafi authorities.
القياس في اللغة (al-qiyās al-lughawī): Linguistic analogy: extending a word from its original meaning to a new case based on a shared attribute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Abu Yusuf and Muhammad applying the hadd penalty of zinā to liwāṭ?
A) They consider the hadith 'إنما أطعمك الله وسقاك' as evidence.
B) They consider liwāṭ as a form of zinā through linguistic extension (qiyas in language).
C) They rely on consensus of the Companions.
D) They consider the verse 'الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي' as specific to liwāṭ.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accepts qiyas in language, allowing the term 'zinā' to include liwāṭ, while Shafi'i rejects it and requires textual indication for the hadd.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Definition of Qiyas, Its Conditions, and the Dispute over Qiyas in Language
Defining qiyas and arguing against qiyas in language.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qiyas, list its conditions according to Hanafi usul, and explain why qiyas in language is invalid by analyzing the zina/liwat and khamr examples.

Core Idea
Qiyas is valid only when the ruling is transferred identically; extending names based on common meanings (qiyas lughawi) is not permissible.

Qiyas is a foundational source of Islamic law, but its application is strictly governed by conditions. This passage from Noor al-Anwar defines qiyas and outlines its conditions, then engages in a sharp critique of qiyas in language (qiyas fi al-lugha) – the attempt to extend linguistic names based on shared meanings. Through dialogues about zina/liwat and khamr, the Hanafi position that language is conventional, not based on reasoning, is defended.

Guided Path
1
Define qiyas and identify its conditions
Read the opening section where qiyas is defined and the majority opinion on its conditions is stated. Note that some commentators claim six conditions, but the author questions their utility.
Focus on the concept of transitivity (ta'diyah) – the ruling must be carried over identically.
2
Understand the condition that the ruling must be legal and text-based
The text explains that the ruling in the original case must be established by a text (Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma), not itself derived from qiyas. Otherwise, the analogy becomes baseless.
This is the 'not a branch' (la far'an) condition.
3
Analyze the dispute over qiyas in language with the zina/liwat example
Examine how al-Shafi'i (and some Hanafis) argued that liwat is included under zina because of a shared 'meaning'. The Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes between extending a ruling (qiyas shar'i) and extending a name (qiyas lughawi).
See how the Hanafi uses the Quranic verse (24:2) but argues the hadd is from dalalat al-nass, not qiyas.
4
Consider the khamr and jarjir dialogues
The Hanafi scholar's rhetorical questions to the Shafi'is show that linguistic analogies lead to absurdities, proving that language is conventional, not rational.
The bottle and jarjir examples are meant to be reductio ad absurdum.
5
Apply the condition of transitivity to the dhihar of a dhimmi
The Shafi'i attempt to analogize a dhimmi's dhihar to a Muslim's fails because the ruling changes (perpetual vs. finite). This illustrates the Hanafi requirement that the ruling be transferred identically.
The dhimmi cannot perform expiation, so the analogical extension is invalid.

Source Text
