بيان ركن القياس
إليه مشايخ العراق؛ لأن النص دليل قطعي، وإضافة الحكم إليه في الأصل أولى من إضافته إلى النص العلة، وإنما أضيف في الفرع إليها للضرورة حيث لم يوجد فيه النص، وقيل: أضيف حكم أي الحكم العلة العلة الفرع الأصل والفرع جميعًا إلى العلة؛ لأنه ما لم يكن لها تأثير في الأصل كيف تؤثر في الفرع. مما اشتمل عليه النص، أي حال كون ذلك العلم ممّا اشتمل عليه النص إمّا صيغةً كاشتمال نص الربا على الكيل ،والجنس أو بغير صيغة كاشتمال نص النهي عن بيع الآبق على العجز عن التسليم.
وجعل الفرع نظيراً له أي للأصل في حكمه بوجوده فيه، أي وجود ذلك المعنى في الفرع ، ويفهم من ههنا أن أركان القياس أربعة الأصل والفرع، والعلة، والحكم، وإن كان أصل الركن هو العلة.
مما اشتمل: أي من الأوصاف التي اشتمل إلخ (القمر) نص: أي لفظ مثلاً بمثل. (المحشي) بغير صيغة بأن يكون ذلك المعنى مستنبطا من النص بالالتزام أو بغيره. (القمر) نص النهي إلخ روى الترمذي عن حكيم بن حزام الله قال : نهاني رسول الله له أن أبيع ما ليس عندي. (القمر)
على العجز عن التسليم: فعجز البائع التسليم: فعجز البائع عن التسليم علة للنهي عن بيع الآبق، ولا ذكر لهذا العجز صريحا في نص ذلك النهي إلا أنه مستنبط منه، فإن البيع مذكور فيه ولا بد له من بائع، والعجز صفته، فإذا لم يقدر على التسليم فكيف يتحقق المبادلة. (القمر) وجعل الفرع إلخ قلت احترز به عن المعنى في الدلالة؛ لأن لفظ الفرع يُنبئ عما لا يكون منصوصاً أصلاً، والثابت بمعنى النص في حكم المنصوص. (السنبلي) في حكمه من الحل والحرمة والجواز والفساد (القمر) والعلة أي العلة المشتركة بين الأصل والفرع الموجبة لحكم الأصل. (القمر) والحكم: المراد من الحكم حكم الأصل؛ لأن حكم الفرع ثمرة القياس لتوقفه عليه، ولو كان ركنا من القياس لتوقف على نفسه، وهو باطل (السنبلي)
وإن كان أصل الركن إلخ لأن القياس ليس له وجود إلا بالمعنى الذي هو مناط الحكم.(السنبلي) أصل الركن أي الركن الأعظم هو العلة، فإنه ما لم يتحقق العلة لا يتحقق أصل، ولا فرع، ولا حكم (القمر) يدل عليه قول حكيم بن حزام له: نهاني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن بيع ما ليس في يدي، رواه الترمذي رقم: ۱۲۳۲، باب ما جاء في كراهية ما ليس عندك.
Chapter of Qiyas. Section: Explanation of the Pillar of Qiyas. The scholars of Iraq leaned toward this because the text is a decisive proof, and attributing the ruling to it in the original is more appropriate than attributing it to the cause. Rather, in the branch it is attributed to the cause due to necessity where there is no text. And it was said: The ruling is attributed to the cause, and the original and branch are both attributed to the cause, because if it had no effect in the original, how could it affect the branch? 'From what the text contains' means: the knowledge being from what the text contains either by wording, like the text on riba including measurement and type, or without wording, like the text prohibiting the sale of an absconding slave including inability to deliver. And making the branch analogous to the original in its ruling by the existence of that meaning in the branch. From here it is understood that the pillars of qiyas are four: the original, the branch, the cause, and the ruling, even though the original pillar is the cause. 'From what it contains': i.e., among the descriptions that it contains etc. (al-Qamar) 'Text': meaning a wording like for like. (al-Muhashi) 'Without wording': meaning that meaning is derived from the text by implication or otherwise. (al-Qamar) 'Text of the prohibition etc.' Tirmidhi reported from Hakim ibn Hizam: The Messenger of Allah prohibited me from selling what I do not possess. (al-Qamar) 'Inability to deliver': the seller's inability to deliver is the cause for the prohibition of selling an absconding slave, and this inability is not explicitly mentioned in the text of that prohibition, but it is derived from it. For the sale is mentioned in it and it necessarily has a seller, and inability is his attribute. So if he cannot deliver, how can the exchange be realized? (al-Qamar) 'And making the branch etc.' He said: By this he guarded against the meaning in indication, because the term 'branch' indicates what is not textually stated at all, and that which is established by the meaning of the text is in the ruling of the textual. (al-Sanbuli) 'In its ruling' from permissibility, prohibition, validity, and invalidity. (al-Qamar) 'And the cause' meaning the common cause between the original and the branch that necessitates the ruling of the original. (al-Qamar) 'And the ruling': what is intended by 'ruling' is the ruling of the original, because the ruling of the branch is the fruit of qiyas, as it depends on it. If it were a pillar of qiyas, it would depend on itself, which is invalid. (al-Sanbuli) 'Even though the original pillar etc.' Because qiyas has no existence except through the meaning which is the basis of the ruling. (al-Sanbuli) 'The original pillar' meaning the greatest pillar is the cause, for if the cause is not realized, neither original, nor branch, nor ruling is realized. (al-Qamar) This is supported by the saying of Hakim ibn Hizam: The Messenger of Allah prohibited me from selling what is not in my possession, narrated by Tirmidhi no. 1232, chapter on the dislike of what is not with you.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the pillars (arkan) of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author discusses the rationale for attributing rulings to the cause rather than the text in the branch case. He emphasizes that qiyas has four pillars: the original (asl), the branch (far'), the cause (illah), and the ruling (hukm). However, the most fundamental pillar is the cause, because without it, qiyas cannot exist. The text also clarifies that the ruling attributed to the branch is actually the ruling of the original, as the branch's ruling derives from the analogy. The example of riba illustrates a cause expressed in wording (measurement and type), while the example of selling an absconding slave illustrates a cause derived without explicit wording (inability to deliver). The passage includes marginal commentary from scholars like al-Qamar and al-Sanbuli, who further refine the definitions. Notably, the author cites a hadith from Hakim ibn Hizam to support the principle.

Key Terms
الركن (al-rukn): The essential component of qiyas; the four pillars are original, branch, cause, and ruling, but the most fundamental is the cause.
العلة (al-illah): The common attribute or cause that links the original and branch and necessitates the same ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the cause considered the 'original pillar' of qiyas?
A) Because it is the only pillar mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because without the cause, neither the original, branch, nor ruling can be realized.
C) Because the cause is always explicit in the text.
D) Because the cause determines the validity of the original case.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas has four pillars, but the cause is the most essential; its derivation from the text—whether explicit or implicit—determines the validity of analogical reasoning.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Types of Illah: Description (Lazim and 'Arid) vs. Noun
Explanation of types of illah (cause) in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between necessary and accidental descriptions as causes in qiyas and evaluate the Hanafi debate over whether a noun can serve as an illah.

Core Idea
The illah in qiyas is a description, not a noun; it is either necessary or accidental.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text clarifies the types of effective cause (illah) in analogical reasoning. It teaches that the cause must be a description (wasf)—either necessary (lazim) or accidental (ārid)—and not merely a noun or substance. The example of blood in the hadith on istihadah illustrates the distinction: the cause is the bursting, not the blood itself. A minority Hanafi view allowing nouns is examined and set aside.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of wasf
Recognize that the illah can be a description that is either inseparable from the original (lazim) or separable (ārid). The text gives examples: thumaniyya for gold/silver (lazim), and bursting for blood (ārid).
Thumaniyya is the quality of being a standard of monetary value.
2
Analyze the necessary description example
Examine how thumaniyya is a necessary attribute of gold and silver—they were created for this purpose. It serves as the cause for zakat and, according to al-Shafi'i, for riba, but note that it is intransitive in the Hanafi view.
This demonstrates that a necessary cause can be shared across rulings but may not extend beyond the original.
3
Analyze the accidental description example
Focus on the hadith 'فإنها دم عرق انفجر' (it is a blood vessel that burst). The cause for wudu is the bursting (infijār), not the blood itself. This attribute is accidental because not every blood vessel bursts.
The cause is transitive—it applies wherever bursting occurs, even in non-mustahada cases.
4
Evaluate the debate on noun as illah
Consider the claim that a noun (e.g., 'blood') can be the illah. Fakhr al-Islam al-Razi allowed it, but the majority, supported by al-Qamar and al-Sanbuli, reject it. The true illah is always a description.
The apparent wording 'it is blood' might mislead, but the cause is the attribute of exit.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the operative view in the Hanafi school is that the illah must be a description (wasf), not a noun. This ensures transitivity and proper analogical reasoning.
This aligns with the majority of Hanafi usul scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان علة القياس
بيان علة القياس]
ثم شرع في بيان أن ذلك المعنى يكون على عدة أنحاء فقال: وهو جائز أن يكون وصفا أي العلة الجامعة لازماً وعارضًا، فالوصف اللازم أن لا ينفك عن الأصل كالثمنية علّة لوجوب الزكاة في الذهب والفضة لا ينفك عنهما؛ لأنهما خُلقا في الأصل على معنى الثمنية، وهي مشتر أي الثمنية كة بين مضروب الذهب والفضة وتبرهما وحُليّهما، فيكون في حُلي النساء الزكاة بالثمنية لعلة الثمنية، والشافعي الله يعلّل حرمة الربا بها، وهي غير متعدية إلى شيء، والوصف العارض كالانفجار في قوله عليه: "فإنها دم عرق انفجر"* علة لوجوب الوضوء في وهي عارضة للدم؛ إذ لا يلزم أن يكون كل دم العرق منفجرا، فأينما وجد المستحاضة أي العلة انفجار الدم، سواء كان للمستحاضة أو لغيرها من غير السبيلين يجب به الوضوء. واسما، عطف على قوله: "وصفا" ومقابل له أي يجوز أن يكون ذلك المعنى اسما كالدم أي اسم جنس في عين هذا المثال، وهو قوله علي: "فإنها دم عرق انفجر"، فإنه إن اعتبر فيه لفظ الدم كان مثالاً للاسم، وإن اعتبر فيه معنى الانفجار كان مثالاً للوصف العارض كما مرّ.
وهو : أي المعنى الذي جعل علمًا على حكم النص. (القمر) وصفًا أي للأصل المقيس عليه. (القمر) كالثمنية إلخ : المراد بالثمنية أن يكون الذهب والفضة بحال يقدّر به مالية الأشياء، كذا قال ابن الملك. (القمر) عنهما إلخ : أي عن الذهب والفضة (القمر) والوصف العارض: هو الذي يمكن انفكاكه عن الأصل. (القمر) في المستحاضة: هي التي ترى الدم من قبلها في زمان لا يعدّ من الحيض ولا من النفاس، كذا قيل. واسما إلخ اعتد بهذا القسم الإمام فخر الإسلام منه، والظاهر أن هذا الاعتداد تسامح وتساهل، وفي الحقيقة العلة منحصرة في الوصف كما يُفهم من عبارات القوم، فالدم في هذا المثال ليس بعلة، بل خروجه وهو وصف، "التنوير" (السنبلي) أي يجوز أن يكون إلخ كذا قال فخر الإسلام له، والظاهر أن الدم ليس بعلة لوجوب الوضوء، خروج الدم، ولذا ما تفوّه الجمهور بكون العلة اسما. (القمر) كالدم: فهو اسم موضوع وليس في حديث أم حبيبة بنت جحش ولكن هذا عرق، وفي حديث فاطمة بنت جحش فإنما هو عرق، وفي حديث حمنة بنت جحش إنما هذه ركضة من ركضات الشيطان أخرج الكل أبو داود في سننه. [إشراق الأبصار: ٣٠]
Explanation of the Cause of Qiyas: Then he began to explain that that meaning can be of several types. He said: It is possible for it to be a description—i.e., the comprehensive cause—necessary or accidental. The necessary description is that which is inseparable from the original, like being a standard of value (thumaniyya) as a cause for the obligation of zakat on gold and silver; it is inseparable from them because they were originally created on the meaning of being a standard of value, and this meaning is shared between minted gold and silver, their ores, and their ornaments. Thus, there is zakat on women's ornaments due to the cause of being a standard of value. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, uses it as the cause for the prohibition of riba, but it is not transitive to anything else. The accidental description is like the bursting [of blood] in his saying: 'It is a blood vessel that burst' as a cause for the obligation of wudu in the case of mustahada (a woman with chronic uterine bleeding); it is accidental to blood, because it is not necessary that every blood vessel bursts. So wherever there is bursting of blood, whether in the mustahada or in others from other than the two passages, wudu becomes obligatory. And (it can be) a noun—coordinated with 'description' and opposite to it. That is, that meaning may be a noun like 'blood'—a generic noun in this same example, i.e., his saying: 'It is a blood vessel that burst.' If the word 'blood' is considered, it is an example of a noun; if the meaning of 'bursting' is considered, it is an example of the accidental description as passed. 'And it': meaning the meaning which is made a sign of the ruling of the text. (al-Qamar) 'Description' meaning of the original being measured upon. (al-Qamar) 'Like thumaniyya etc.': intended by thumaniyya is that gold and silver are in a state by which the value of things is measured, as said by Ibn al-Malik. (al-Qamar) 'From them etc.': meaning from gold and silver. (al-Qamar) 'And the accidental description': that which can be separated from the original. (al-Qamar) 'In the mustahada': she who sees blood from her front in a time not considered menstruation nor postpartum bleeding, thus it is said. (al-Qamar) 'And a noun etc.': Imam Fakhr al-Islam counted this as a category, but apparently this counting is lenient and lax, for in reality the cause is confined to description as understood from the expressions of the scholars. So blood in this example is not a cause, but rather its exit which is a description. 'Al-Tanwir' (al-Sanbuli). Al-Qamar said: Fakhr al-Islam allowed it, but apparently blood is not a cause for wudu; rather, the exit of blood is. That is why the majority did not speak of the cause being a noun. (al-Qamar) 'Like blood': it is a noun of substance and not (a description) in the hadith of Umm Habiba bint Jahsh 'but this is a blood vessel', and in the hadith of Fatima bint Jahsh 'it is only a blood vessel', and in the hadith of Hamna bint Jahsh 'it is only a kick from the kicks of Satan'—all recorded by Abu Dawood in his Sunan. [Ishraq al-Absar: 30]
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the types of illah (cause) in qiyas according to Hanafi usul. The author, likely from the Hanafi tradition, states that the cause can be a description (wasf) which is either necessary (lazim) or accidental (arid). A necessary description is inseparable from the original, like 'being a standard of value' (thumaniyya) for gold and silver, which necessitates zakat. This cause is also used by al-Shafi'i but not extended to other items. An accidental description is one that can be separated, like 'bursting' in a hadith about blood causing wudu; it is not inherent to blood itself. The author then mentions that the cause can also be a noun (ism), such as 'blood' in the same hadith. However, some Hanafi scholars like Fakhr al-Islam al-Razi considered this a valid category, but others argue it is a leniency and that the true cause is actually the description of exit (bursting). The marginal notes clarify that blood is not a cause; rather, the exit of blood is the description. The passage concludes with references to hadiths from Abu Dawood about chronic bleeding (istihadah). The overall message is to refine the understanding of what constitutes the cause in analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
الوصف اللازم (al-wasf al-lazim): A description that is inseparable from the original, like thumaniyya for gold and silver.
الوصف العارض (al-wasf al-'arid): An accidental description that can be separated from the original, like bursting of blood.
الاسم (al-ism): A noun or substance term that some scholars consider a possible cause, but the majority view is that the cause is a description.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of the mustahada, what is the actual illah for the obligation of wudu according to the majority of Hanafi scholars?
A) The blood itself.
B) The bursting of the blood vessel.
C) The word 'blood' mentioned in the hadith.
D) The fact that it is from the front passage.

Key Takeaway
The effective cause (illah) in qiyas must be a description (wasf), not a noun, and it is either necessary (lazim) or accidental (ārid).

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Necessary and Accidental Descriptions as 'Illah
Explains the first division of 'illah into necessary and accidental descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a given attribute as a necessary (lazim) or accidental ('arid) 'illah and explain the difference using the examples of thumaniyya and bursting blood.

Core Idea
The 'illah must be a description; a necessary description is inseparable, while an accidental one may be absent.

In this passage, the commentator begins the taxonomy of the 'illah in qiyas, dividing it into necessary and accidental descriptions. Understanding this distinction is fundamental to identifying the effective cause in analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of wasf
The text states that the 'illah can be a description (wasf) that is either necessary (lazim) or accidental ('arid). Recognise that these are the primary categories for Hanafi usul.
The passage later clarifies that the 'illah is always a description; the noun category is a lenient view.
2
Define necessary and accidental
A necessary description never separates from the original (e.g., thumaniyya from gold/silver). An accidental description can separate (e.g., bursting of blood is not always present in blood).
Use the definitions from Ibn al-Malik and Al-Qamar.
3
Apply to textual examples
For thumaniyya: gold and silver are created as mediums of exchange, so thumaniyya is inseparable. For bursting blood: the hadith 'it is a blood of a bursting vein' shows that the cause is the bursting (infijar), not the blood itself, because not all blood bursts.
The bursting is accidental because it is not a constant property of blood.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i alternative
Al-Shafi'i also uses thumaniyya as a cause, but for riba rather than zakat. Note that the Hanafi school restricts thumaniyya as a cause for riba only to gold and silver, not all valuables.
This will be elaborated in the hidden description section.

باب القياس
بيان علة القياس
ثم شرع في بيان أن ذلك المعنى يكون على عدة أنحاء فقال: وهو جائز أن يكون وصفا أي العلة الجامعة لازماً وعارضاً، فالوصف اللازم أن لا ينفك عن الأصل كالثمنية علّة لوجوب الزكاة في الذهب والفضة لا ينفك عنهما؛ لأنهما خُلقا في الأصل على معنى الثمنية، وهي مشتركة بين مضروب الذهب والفضة وتبرهما وحُليّهما، فيكون في حُلي النساء الزكاة بالثمنية لعلة الثمنية، والشافعي رحمه الله يعلّل حرمة الربا بها، وهي غير متعدية إلى شيء، والوصف العارض كالانفجار في قوله عليه: "فإنها دم عرق انفجر" علة لوجوب الوضوء في المستحاضة، وهي عارضة للدم؛ إذ لا يلزم أن يكون كل دم العرق منفجرا، فأينما وجد انفجار الدم، سواء كان للمستحاضة أو لغيرها من غير السبيلين يجب به الوضوء. واسما، عطف على قوله: "وصفا" ومقابل له أي يجوز أن يكون ذلك المعنى اسما كالدم أي اسم جنس في عين هذا المثال، وهو قوله عليه: "فإنها دم عرق انفجر"، فإنه إن اعتبر فيه لفظ الدم كان مثالاً للاسم، وإن اعتبر فيه معنى الانفجار كان مثالاً للوصف العارض كما مرّ. وهو أي المعنى الذي جعل علمًا على حكم النص. (القمر) وصفًا أي للأصل المقيس عليه. (القمر) كالثمنية إلخ : المراد بالثمنية أن يكون الذهب والفضة بحال يقدّر به مالية الأشياء، كذا قال ابن الملك. (القمر) عنهما إلخ : أي عن الذهب والفضة (القمر) والوصف العارض: هو الذي يمكن انفكاكه عن الأصل. (القمر) في المستحاضة: هي التي ترى الدم من قبلها في زمان لا يعدّ من الحيض ولا من النفاس، كذا قيل. واسما إلخ اعتد بهذا القسم الإمام فخر الإسلام منه، والظاهر أن هذا الاعتداد تسامح وتساهل، وفي الحقيقة العلة منحصرة في الوصف كما يُفهم من عبارات القوم، فالدم في هذا المثال ليس بعلة، بل خروجه وهو وصف، "التنوير" (السنبلي) أي يجوز أن يكون إلخ كذا قال فخر الإسلام له، والظاهر أن الدم ليس بعلة لوجوب الوضوء، خروج الدم، ولذا ما تفوّه الجمهور بكون العلة اسما. (القمر) كالدم: فهو اسم موضوع وليس مشتقاً. في حديث أم حبيبة بنت جحش ولكن هذا عرق، وفي حديث فاطمة بنت جحش فإنما هو عرق، وفي حديث حمنة بنت جحش إنما هذه ركضة من ركضات الشيطان أخرج الكل أبو داود في سننه. [إشراق الأبصار: ٣٠]

وجليا وخفيًا، الظاهر أنه تقسيم للوصف كاللازم والعارض، فالوصف الجلي كل أحد ما يفهمه كالطواف لسؤر الهرة في قوله عليه: "إنها من الطوافين والطوافات عليكم" والوصف الخفي ما يفهم بعض دون بعض كما في علة الربا عندنا القدر والجنس، وعند الشافعي رحمه الله الطعم في المطعومات والثمنية في الأثمان وعند مالك رحمه الله الاقتيات والادخار. وحكمًا، هذا معطوف على قوله: "وصفا" ومقابل له أي يجوز أن يكون ذلك المعنى حكمًا شرعيًا جامعًا بين الأصل والفرع كما روي أن امرأة جاءت إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: إن أبي قد أدركه الحج، وهو شيخ كبير لا يستمسك على الراحلة، أفتجزئ أن أحج عنه؟ فقال عليه: "أرأيت لو كان على أبيك دين فقضيته أما كان يقبل منك؟ قالت: نعم، قال: الله أحق بالقبول"، فقاس النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الحج على دين العباد، والمعنى الجامع بينهما هو الدين، وهو عبارة عن حق ثابت في الذمة واجب الأداء، والوجوب حكم شرعي. وجليا قيل المراد بالجلاء أن يكون مذكورًا في النص صريحًا، وبالخفاء خلافه. (القمر) تقسيم للوصف إلخ : فيكون عطفا على قوله: "لازما" ويجوز أن يكون عطفا على قوله: "وصفا" أو يكون هذا أيضا تقسيما لك المعنى الذي هو العلة (السنبلي كالطواف أي كالطواف علة لطهارة سؤر الهرة (المحشي) الاقتيات والادخار في غير الأثمان، والثمنية فيها، والتفصيل قد مرّ فتذكره. (القمر) أرأيت: هي كلمة تقولها العرب بمعنى أخبرني (القمر) والوجوب حكم شرعي إلخ وكما أن النجاسة علة لحرمة بيع الخمر والخنزير ونجاستهما حكم شرعي (السنبلي)

*** أخرجه الترمذي رقم: ۹۲ باب ما جاء في سؤر الهرة والنسائي رقم ٦٨ باب سؤر الهرة، وأحمد في "مسنده رقم ۲۲٦٣٣ ، وأبوداود رقم: ۷۵ باب سؤر الهرة، وابن ماجه رقم ٣٦٧ ، باب الوضوء بسؤر الهرة والرخصة في ذالك، عن أبي قتادة

أخرجه البخاري رقم: ١٤٤٢ ، باب وجوب الحج وفضله، ومسلم رقم ١٣٣٤ ، باب الحج عن العاجز لزمانة وهرم ونحوهما أو للموت، عن عبد الله بن عباس .
Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of the Cause of Qiyas. Then he began to explain that that meaning can be in several ways. He said: It is permissible for it to be a description, i.e., the comprehensive cause, necessary or accidental. The necessary description is that which does not separate from the original, like thumaniyya (value) as a cause for the obligation of zakat on gold and silver, it does not separate from them; because they were originally created with the meaning of thumaniyya, and it is common between struck gold and silver, their nuggets and their jewelry, so there is zakat on women's jewelry due to thumaniyya for the cause of thumaniyya. Al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) uses it as a cause for the prohibition of riba, but it is not transitive to anything else. The accidental description is like bursting (infijar) in his saying (peace be upon him): 'It is a blood of a bursting vein' as a cause for the obligation of wudu in the case of mustahadah (chronic menstruation), and it is accidental to blood; because it is not necessary that every blood from a vein is bursting. So wherever bursting of blood is found, whether from a mustahadah or from other than her from other than the two passages, wudu becomes obligatory. And as a noun, it is coordinated with 'description' and opposite to it, i.e., it is permissible for that meaning to be a noun, like 'blood' meaning the noun of genus in this very example, which is his saying: 'It is a blood of a bursting vein.' If the word 'blood' is considered in it, it is an example of a noun; if the meaning of bursting is considered, it is an example of an accidental description as passed. And it (the meaning that is made a sign for the ruling of the text) is a description (i.e., for the original being measured upon). (Al-Qamar) like thumaniyya etc.: the meaning of thumaniyya is that gold and silver are in a state by which the value of things is estimated, as Ibn al-Malik said. (Al-Qamar) from them etc.: i.e., from gold and silver. (Al-Qamar) And the accidental description: it is that which can separate from the original. (Al-Qamar) in mustahadah: she is the one who sees blood from her front in a time that is not considered menstruation nor postpartum bleeding, as is said. And as a noun etc., Imam Fakhr al-Islam counted this division from him, but apparently this counting is lenient and relaxed, and in reality the cause is restricted to description as understood from the expressions of the scholars. So blood in this example is not a cause, rather its exit, which is a description. (Al-Tanwir) (Al-Sunbuli) i.e., it is permissible for it to be etc. Fakhr al-Islam said it, but apparently blood is not a cause for the obligation of wudu; it is the exit of blood, and therefore the majority did not say that the cause is a noun. (Al-Qamar) like blood: it is a set noun and not derived. In the hadith of Umm Habiba bint Jahsh: 'But this is a vein'; in the hadith of Fatima bint Jahsh: 'It is only a vein'; in the hadith of Hamna bint Jahsh: 'This is only a kick from the kicks of Satan' — all were narrated by Abu Dawud in his Sunan. [Ishraq al-Absar: 30]

And clear and hidden: apparently it is a division of description like necessary and accidental. The clear description is that which everyone understands, like tawaf (circumambulation) for the leftover water of a cat in his saying: 'It is among those who go around among you (tawwafin)'. The hidden description is that which some understand and some do not, as in the cause of riba according to us: (it is) value and genus; according to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him): edibility in foodstuffs and thumaniyya in valuables; according to Malik (may Allah have mercy on him): being a staple and storable. And as a legal ruling: this is coordinated with 'description' and opposite to it, i.e., it is permissible for that meaning to be a legal ruling that unites the original and the branch, as is narrated that a woman came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: 'My father has reached the time of Hajj while he is a very old man who cannot stay on the riding animal; would it be sufficient if I perform Hajj on his behalf?' He said: 'Tell me, if your father had a debt and you paid it, would it be accepted from you?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Allah is more deserving of acceptance.' So the Prophet (peace be upon him) analogized Hajj to the debts of people, and the unifying meaning between them is debt (dayn), which is an expression for a right established in the liability, obligatory to fulfill, and obligation is a legal ruling. And 'clear': it is said that the meaning of clarity is that it is explicitly mentioned in the text; and hiddenness is the opposite. (Al-Qamar) A division of description etc.: so it is coordinated with his statement 'necessary', and it is permissible that it is coordinated with his statement 'description', or this is also a division of that meaning which is the cause. (Al-Sunbuli) like tawaf: i.e., tawaf is a cause for the purity of the cat's leftover water. (Al-Muhashi) being a staple and storable in non-valuables, and thumaniyya in valuables, and the detail has passed, so remember it. (Al-Qamar) 'Ara'ayt': it is a word that the Arabs say meaning 'tell me'. (Al-Qamar) And obligation is a legal ruling etc., and just as impurity is a cause for the prohibition of selling wine and pigs and their impurity is a legal ruling. (Al-Sunbuli)

*** Al-Tirmidhi no. 92: chapter on the leftover water of a cat; Al-Nasa'i no. 68: chapter on the leftover water of a cat; Ahmad in his Musnad no. 22633; Abu Dawud no. 75: chapter on the leftover water of a cat and the permission for that, from Abu Qatada.

Al-Bukhari no. 1442: chapter on the obligation of Hajj and its virtue; Muslim no. 1334: chapter on Hajj on behalf of the incapacitated due to chronic illness, decrepitude, and the like, or for the deceased, from Abdullah ibn Abbas.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the chapter of Qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh begins the explanation of the types of 'illah (legal cause). The author states that the 'illah can be a description (wasf) — either necessary (lazim) or accidental ('arid). A necessary description is inseparable from the original, like thumaniyya (the quality of being a medium of exchange) for gold and silver, which is the cause for zakat. Al-Shafi'i uses thumaniyya as the cause for riba, but the Hanafi position is that the cause for riba includes both value and genus (jins) as will be explained later. An accidental description can separate from the original, like the bursting of blood (infijar) in the hadith of the mustahadah (woman with chronic uterine bleeding); the cause is the bursting, not blood itself, because it is accidental. Then the author discusses whether the 'illah can be a noun (ism) as opposed to a description. Fakhr al-Islam counts this as a division, but the correct view (as per the later commentator 'Al-Qamar') is that the 'illah is always a description; blood itself is not the cause, but the exit of blood is a descriptive event. The passage then divides description into clear (jali) and hidden (khafi). The clear is understood by everyone, like 'tawwaf' (going around) as the cause for the purity of a cat's leftover water (the cat is likened to one who goes around among you). The hidden requires ijtihad, like the cause of riba: Hanafis say it is value and genus; Shafi'is say it is edibility in food and thumaniyya in valuables; Malikis say it is being a staple and storable. Finally, the 'illah can also be a legal ruling (hukm), as in the hadith where Hajj is analogized to a debt because both are obligatory claims on the person. The commentator also notes that 'jali' can mean explicitly mentioned in the text. Footnotes provide hadith references for the cat's leftover water and Hajj on behalf of another.

Key Terms
علة ('illah): The attribute in the original case that is used to extend the ruling to a new case in qiyas.
وصف لازم (wasf lazim): A description inseparable from the original, e.g., thumaniyya for gold and silver.
وصف عارض (wasf 'arid): An accidental description that can separate from the original, e.g., bursting of blood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between a necessary (lazim) and an accidental ('arid) description as 'illah in qiyas?
A) Necessary is found in all individuals, accidental only in some.
B) Necessary is inseparable from the original; accidental can separate.
C) Necessary is always a noun; accidental is a verb.
D) Necessary applies only to gold and silver; accidental to blood.

Key Takeaway
The 'illah in qiyas must be a description; necessary descriptions are inseparable, while accidental descriptions may be absent, and the noun interpretation is not the relied-upon view.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Clear vs Hidden Descriptions and the 'Illah as a Legal Ruling
Continues with clear/hidden descriptions and introduces legal ruling as 'illah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between clear (jali) and hidden (khafi) descriptions as 'illah, and identify when a legal ruling (hukm) itself serves as the unifying attribute in qiyas.

Core Idea
Clear 'illah is understood by all; hidden 'illah requires ijtihad; a legal ruling can also be the 'illah when it unifies two cases.

This part of the passage continues the taxonomy of the 'illah, dividing descriptions into clear and hidden. It also presents a unique type: the 'illah can be a legal ruling itself, as demonstrated by the Prophet analogizing Hajj to debt repayment.

Guided Path
1
Define clear (jali) and hidden (khafi) descriptions
A clear description is one that any person can understand without deep ijtihad, like 'tawaf' (going around) in the hadith about the cat's leftover water. A hidden description requires careful analysis, like the cause of riba.
The text also notes that 'clear' can mean explicitly mentioned in the source text.
2
Apply to the examples given
For the cat's leftover water: the 'illah is that the cat is 'among those who go around you' (tawwafin), which is a clear description understood by all. For riba, the 'illah is hidden because scholars differ: Hanafis say genus and value, Shafi'is say edibility, Malikis say staple and storable.
This shows how hidden 'illah leads to ikhtilaf.
3
Explain the 'illah as a legal ruling (hukm)
The text gives the hadith where the Prophet analogized Hajj on behalf of another to paying a debt. The unifying attribute is 'debt' (dayn), which is a legal ruling: a right in the liability that must be fulfilled. This shows that a hukm can act as the 'illah connecting original and branch.
The commentator adds that impurity is another example of a legal ruling as 'illah for prohibition of selling wine and pigs.

باب القياس
بيان علة القياس
ثم شرع في بيان أن ذلك المعنى يكون على عدة أنحاء فقال: وهو جائز أن يكون وصفا أي العلة الجامعة لازماً وعارضاً، فالوصف اللازم أن لا ينفك عن الأصل كالثمنية علّة لوجوب الزكاة في الذهب والفضة لا ينفك عنهما؛ لأنهما خُلقا في الأصل على معنى الثمنية، وهي مشتركة بين مضروب الذهب والفضة وتبرهما وحُليّهما، فيكون في حُلي النساء الزكاة بالثمنية لعلة الثمنية، والشافعي رحمه الله يعلّل حرمة الربا بها، وهي غير متعدية إلى شيء، والوصف العارض كالانفجار في قوله عليه: "فإنها دم عرق انفجر" علة لوجوب الوضوء في المستحاضة، وهي عارضة للدم؛ إذ لا يلزم أن يكون كل دم العرق منفجرا، فأينما وجد انفجار الدم، سواء كان للمستحاضة أو لغيرها من غير السبيلين يجب به الوضوء. واسما، عطف على قوله: "وصفا" ومقابل له أي يجوز أن يكون ذلك المعنى اسما كالدم أي اسم جنس في عين هذا المثال، وهو قوله عليه: "فإنها دم عرق انفجر"، فإنه إن اعتبر فيه لفظ الدم كان مثالاً للاسم، وإن اعتبر فيه معنى الانفجار كان مثالاً للوصف العارض كما مرّ. وهو أي المعنى الذي جعل علمًا على حكم النص. (القمر) وصفًا أي للأصل المقيس عليه. (القمر) كالثمنية إلخ : المراد بالثمنية أن يكون الذهب والفضة بحال يقدّر به مالية الأشياء، كذا قال ابن الملك. (القمر) عنهما إلخ : أي عن الذهب والفضة (القمر) والوصف العارض: هو الذي يمكن انفكاكه عن الأصل. (القمر) في المستحاضة: هي التي ترى الدم من قبلها في زمان لا يعدّ من الحيض ولا من النفاس، كذا قيل. واسما إلخ اعتد بهذا القسم الإمام فخر الإسلام منه، والظاهر أن هذا الاعتداد تسامح وتساهل، وفي الحقيقة العلة منحصرة في الوصف كما يُفهم من عبارات القوم، فالدم في هذا المثال ليس بعلة، بل خروجه وهو وصف، "التنوير" (السنبلي) أي يجوز أن يكون إلخ كذا قال فخر الإسلام له، والظاهر أن الدم ليس بعلة لوجوب الوضوء، خروج الدم، ولذا ما تفوّه الجمهور بكون العلة اسما. (القمر) كالدم: فهو اسم موضوع وليس مشتقاً. في حديث أم حبيبة بنت جحش ولكن هذا عرق، وفي حديث فاطمة بنت جحش فإنما هو عرق، وفي حديث حمنة بنت جحش إنما هذه ركضة من ركضات الشيطان أخرج الكل أبو داود في سننه. [إشراق الأبصار: ٣٠]

وجليا وخفيًا، الظاهر أنه تقسيم للوصف كاللازم والعارض، فالوصف الجلي كل أحد ما يفهمه كالطواف لسؤر الهرة في قوله عليه: "إنها من الطوافين والطوافات عليكم" والوصف الخفي ما يفهم بعض دون بعض كما في علة الربا عندنا القدر والجنس، وعند الشافعي رحمه الله الطعم في المطعومات والثمنية في الأثمان وعند مالك رحمه الله الاقتيات والادخار. وحكمًا، هذا معطوف على قوله: "وصفا" ومقابل له أي يجوز أن يكون ذلك المعنى حكمًا شرعيًا جامعًا بين الأصل والفرع كما روي أن امرأة جاءت إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: إن أبي قد أدركه الحج، وهو شيخ كبير لا يستمسك على الراحلة، أفتجزئ أن أحج عنه؟ فقال عليه: "أرأيت لو كان على أبيك دين فقضيته أما كان يقبل منك؟ قالت: نعم، قال: الله أحق بالقبول"، فقاس النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الحج على دين العباد، والمعنى الجامع بينهما هو الدين، وهو عبارة عن حق ثابت في الذمة واجب الأداء، والوجوب حكم شرعي. وجليا قيل المراد بالجلاء أن يكون مذكورًا في النص صريحًا، وبالخفاء خلافه. (القمر) تقسيم للوصف إلخ : فيكون عطفا على قوله: "لازما" ويجوز أن يكون عطفا على قوله: "وصفا" أو يكون هذا أيضا تقسيما لك المعنى الذي هو العلة (السنبلي كالطواف أي كالطواف علة لطهارة سؤر الهرة (المحشي) الاقتيات والادخار في غير الأثمان، والثمنية فيها، والتفصيل قد مرّ فتذكره. (القمر) أرأيت: هي كلمة تقولها العرب بمعنى أخبرني (القمر) والوجوب حكم شرعي إلخ وكما أن النجاسة علة لحرمة بيع الخمر والخنزير ونجاستهما حكم شرعي (السنبلي)

*** أخرجه الترمذي رقم: ۹۲ باب ما جاء في سؤر الهرة والنسائي رقم ٦٨ باب سؤر الهرة، وأحمد في "مسنده رقم ۲۲٦٣٣ ، وأبوداود رقم: ۷۵ باب سؤر الهرة، وابن ماجه رقم ٣٦٧ ، باب الوضوء بسؤر الهرة والرخصة في ذالك، عن أبي قتادة

أخرجه البخاري رقم: ١٤٤٢ ، باب وجوب الحج وفضله، ومسلم رقم ١٣٣٤ ، باب الحج عن العاجز لزمانة وهرم ونحوهما أو للموت، عن عبد الله بن عباس .
Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of the Cause of Qiyas. Then he began to explain that that meaning can be in several ways. He said: It is permissible for it to be a description, i.e., the comprehensive cause, necessary or accidental. The necessary description is that which does not separate from the original, like thumaniyya (value) as a cause for the obligation of zakat on gold and silver, it does not separate from them; because they were originally created with the meaning of thumaniyya, and it is common between struck gold and silver, their nuggets and their jewelry, so there is zakat on women's jewelry due to thumaniyya for the cause of thumaniyya. Al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) uses it as a cause for the prohibition of riba, but it is not transitive to anything else. The accidental description is like bursting (infijar) in his saying (peace be upon him): 'It is a blood of a bursting vein' as a cause for the obligation of wudu in the case of mustahadah (chronic menstruation), and it is accidental to blood; because it is not necessary that every blood from a vein is bursting. So wherever bursting of blood is found, whether from a mustahadah or from other than her from other than the two passages, wudu becomes obligatory. And as a noun, it is coordinated with 'description' and opposite to it, i.e., it is permissible for that meaning to be a noun, like 'blood' meaning the noun of genus in this very example, which is his saying: 'It is a blood of a bursting vein.' If the word 'blood' is considered in it, it is an example of a noun; if the meaning of bursting is considered, it is an example of an accidental description as passed. And it (the meaning that is made a sign for the ruling of the text) is a description (i.e., for the original being measured upon). (Al-Qamar) like thumaniyya etc.: the meaning of thumaniyya is that gold and silver are in a state by which the value of things is estimated, as Ibn al-Malik said. (Al-Qamar) from them etc.: i.e., from gold and silver. (Al-Qamar) And the accidental description: it is that which can separate from the original. (Al-Qamar) in mustahadah: she is the one who sees blood from her front in a time that is not considered menstruation nor postpartum bleeding, as is said. And as a noun etc., Imam Fakhr al-Islam counted this division from him, but apparently this counting is lenient and relaxed, and in reality the cause is restricted to description as understood from the expressions of the scholars. So blood in this example is not a cause, rather its exit, which is a description. (Al-Tanwir) (Al-Sunbuli) i.e., it is permissible for it to be etc. Fakhr al-Islam said it, but apparently blood is not a cause for the obligation of wudu; it is the exit of blood, and therefore the majority did not say that the cause is a noun. (Al-Qamar) like blood: it is a set noun and not derived. In the hadith of Umm Habiba bint Jahsh: 'But this is a vein'; in the hadith of Fatima bint Jahsh: 'It is only a vein'; in the hadith of Hamna bint Jahsh: 'This is only a kick from the kicks of Satan' — all were narrated by Abu Dawud in his Sunan. [Ishraq al-Absar: 30]

And clear and hidden: apparently it is a division of description like necessary and accidental. The clear description is that which everyone understands, like tawaf (circumambulation) for the leftover water of a cat in his saying: 'It is among those who go around among you (tawwafin)'. The hidden description is that which some understand and some do not, as in the cause of riba according to us: (it is) value and genus; according to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him): edibility in foodstuffs and thumaniyya in valuables; according to Malik (may Allah have mercy on him): being a staple and storable. And as a legal ruling: this is coordinated with 'description' and opposite to it, i.e., it is permissible for that meaning to be a legal ruling that unites the original and the branch, as is narrated that a woman came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: 'My father has reached the time of Hajj while he is a very old man who cannot stay on the riding animal; would it be sufficient if I perform Hajj on his behalf?' He said: 'Tell me, if your father had a debt and you paid it, would it be accepted from you?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Allah is more deserving of acceptance.' So the Prophet (peace be upon him) analogized Hajj to the debts of people, and the unifying meaning between them is debt (dayn), which is an expression for a right established in the liability, obligatory to fulfill, and obligation is a legal ruling. And 'clear': it is said that the meaning of clarity is that it is explicitly mentioned in the text; and hiddenness is the opposite. (Al-Qamar) A division of description etc.: so it is coordinated with his statement 'necessary', and it is permissible that it is coordinated with his statement 'description', or this is also a division of that meaning which is the cause. (Al-Sunbuli) like tawaf: i.e., tawaf is a cause for the purity of the cat's leftover water. (Al-Muhashi) being a staple and storable in non-valuables, and thumaniyya in valuables, and the detail has passed, so remember it. (Al-Qamar) 'Ara'ayt': it is a word that the Arabs say meaning 'tell me'. (Al-Qamar) And obligation is a legal ruling etc., and just as impurity is a cause for the prohibition of selling wine and pigs and their impurity is a legal ruling. (Al-Sunbuli)

*** Al-Tirmidhi no. 92: chapter on the leftover water of a cat; Al-Nasa'i no. 68: chapter on the leftover water of a cat; Ahmad in his Musnad no. 22633; Abu Dawud no. 75: chapter on the leftover water of a cat and the permission for that, from Abu Qatada.

Al-Bukhari no. 1442: chapter on the obligation of Hajj and its virtue; Muslim no. 1334: chapter on Hajj on behalf of the incapacitated due to chronic illness, decrepitude, and the like, or for the deceased, from Abdullah ibn Abbas.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the chapter of Qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh begins the explanation of the types of 'illah (legal cause). The author states that the 'illah can be a description (wasf) — either necessary (lazim) or accidental ('arid). A necessary description is inseparable from the original, like thumaniyya (the quality of being a medium of exchange) for gold and silver, which is the cause for zakat. Al-Shafi'i uses thumaniyya as the cause for riba, but the Hanafi position is that the cause for riba includes both value and genus (jins) as will be explained later. An accidental description can separate from the original, like the bursting of blood (infijar) in the hadith of the mustahadah (woman with chronic uterine bleeding); the cause is the bursting, not blood itself, because it is accidental. Then the author discusses whether the 'illah can be a noun (ism) as opposed to a description. Fakhr al-Islam counts this as a division, but the correct view (as per the later commentator 'Al-Qamar') is that the 'illah is always a description; blood itself is not the cause, but the exit of blood is a descriptive event. The passage then divides description into clear (jali) and hidden (khafi). The clear is understood by everyone, like 'tawwaf' (going around) as the cause for the purity of a cat's leftover water (the cat is likened to one who goes around among you). The hidden requires ijtihad, like the cause of riba: Hanafis say it is value and genus; Shafi'is say it is edibility in food and thumaniyya in valuables; Malikis say it is being a staple and storable. Finally, the 'illah can also be a legal ruling (hukm), as in the hadith where Hajj is analogized to a debt because both are obligatory claims on the person. The commentator also notes that 'jali' can mean explicitly mentioned in the text. Footnotes provide hadith references for the cat's leftover water and Hajj on behalf of another.

Key Terms
وصف جلي (wasf jali): A clear description understood by everyone without ijtihad, e.g., tawaf for cat's leftover water.
وصف خفي (wasf khafi): A hidden description requiring ijtihad to identify, e.g., the cause of riba.
علة حكمية ('illah hukmiyyah): A legal ruling that serves as the attribute uniting original and branch in qiyas, e.g., obligation (wujub) in the Hajj hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is an example of a legal ruling (hukm) serving as the 'illah in qiyas?
A) Tawaf for cat's leftover water.
B) Value (thumaniyya) for gold.
C) Obligation (wujub) for Hajj and debt.
D) Edibility (tu'm) for riba.

Key Takeaway
The 'illah can be a clear or hidden description, and even a legal ruling; clear descriptions are understood by all, hidden ones require ijtihad, and legal rulings as 'illah show that qiyas can operate on abstract attributes.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Types of 'Illah: Clear vs Hidden, Singular vs Composite
Classification of 'illah into clear/hidden, singular/composite

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify an 'illah as jali/khafi and fard/'adad, and articulate the Hanafi rebuttal to the impossibility of composite 'illah.

Core Idea
An 'illah can be clear or hidden, singular or composite; Hanafis defend composite 'illah as an extracted attribute.

The effective cause ('illah) in qiyas is not monolithic; it can be clear (jali) or hidden (khafi), and it can be a single attribute (fard) or composite ('adad). This passage from Noor al-Anwar walks through these classifications, grounding them in examples from hadith and the riba debate, and addresses a philosophical objection to composite 'illah that other schools raise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main divisions of 'illah
Read the Arabic passage and note that the 'illah is first divided between wasf (description) and hukm (ruling), then within wasf into jali/khafi and fard/'adad.
The author groups these divisions as subdivisions of wasf.
2
Distinguish jali and khafi with examples
Jali is clear to everyone (e.g., cat's roaming habit as 'illah for purity of its leftover water). Khafi requires ijtihad (e.g., quantity and genus for riba in Hanafi view).
Cross-madhhab comparison helps see the differences.
3
Understand 'illah as hukman
The 'illah can also be a legal ruling (hukm) that unites the original and branch, as in the hadith of Hajj by proxy analogized to debt.
This shows the 'illah need not be a physical attribute.
4
Distinguish fard and 'adad
Fard is a single attribute (e.g., quantity alone for prohibition of deferred sale). 'Adad is composite (e.g., quantity plus genus for prohibition of excess).
The author rebuts the objection that a single causality cannot reside in multiple attributes.
5
Analyze the rebuttal of the impossibility objection
The objection claims that a single cause cannot be in multiple attributes. The Hanafi response: causality is an extracted attribute (ma'na muntazi'), like sonship extracted from a person with many parts.
This defends the validity of composite 'illah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
بيان علة القياس
هو ما يفهمه وجليا وخفيًا، الظاهر أنه تقسيم للوصف كاللازم والعارض، فالوصف الجلي كل أحد كالطواف لسؤر الهرة في قوله عليه: "إنها من الطوافين والطوافات عليكم" والوصف الخفي هو ما يفهم بعض دون بعض كما في علة الربا عندنا القدر والجنس، وعند الشافعي الكيل والوزن وعند مالك الاقتيات والادخار. وحكمًا، هذا معطوف على قوله : "وصفا" ومقابل له أي يجوز أن يكون ذلك المعنى حكمًا شرعيًا جامعًا بين الأصل والفرع كما روي أن امرأة جاءت إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: إن أبي قد أدركه الحج، وهو شيخ كبير لا يستمسك على الراحلة، أفتجزئ أن أحج عنه؟ فقال عليه: "أرأيت لو كان على أبيك دين فقضيته أما كان يقبل منك؟ قالت: نعم، قال: الله أحق بالقبول"، فقاس النبي عليه الحج على دين العباد، والمعنى الجامع بينهما هو الدين، وهو عبارة عن حق ثابت في الذمة واجب الأداء، والوجوب حكم شرعي.
وفردًا وعددًا، الظاهر أنه أيضًا تقسيم للوصف، فالوصف الفرد كالعلة بالقدر وحده والجنس أي الكيل والوزن وحده لحرمة النسأ، والوصف العدد كالقدر مع الجنس علة لحرمة التفاضل، والحاصل أن قوله : "اسما وحكمًا" لا شبهة في أنه مقابل للوصف وأن قوله : "لازما وعارضا" لا شك في أنه قسم للوصف، وأما "الجلى والخفى وكذا الفرد والعدد" فقد أورده على سبيل المقابلة والتداخل والظاهر أنه قسم للوصف؛ إذ لم نجد له مثالاً إلا في قسم الوصف، وصف وفردًا : أي غير مؤلّف من الأجزاء. وعددًا أي مركبًا من الأمور المتعددة، وقيل: إنه يلزم حينئذ قيام العلية التي هو عرض واحد بأمور متعددة وقيام العرض الواحد بمحال مختلفة في زمان واحد محال، وهذا واه؛ فإن العلية ليست من الأعراض الانضمامية، بل انتزاعي ينتزع من المجموع من حيث هو مجموع، ولا ضير فيه، ألا ترى أن البنوّة منتزعة من الابن مع كونه ذا أجزاء متعددة.
Chapter of Analogy. Explanation of the effective cause of analogy. It is what is understood, both clear and hidden. Apparently, this is a division of the description, like the necessary and accidental. So the clear description is [understood] by everyone, like circumambulation for the cat's leftover water in his saying (peace be upon him): 'Indeed, it (the cat) is from those who go around you and go around upon you.' And the hidden description is what some understand and others do not, as in the cause of riba according to us: quantity and genus; according to al-Shafi'i: measurement by weight or volume; according to Malik: being a staple food and storable. And [it can be] a ruling (hukman). This is conjuncted to his saying 'description' and opposite to it, meaning it is permissible that this meaning be a legal ruling that unites the original and the branch, as narrated that a woman came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: 'My father has reached the obligation of Hajj, and he is a very old man who cannot stay steady on a mount. Will it suffice if I perform Hajj on his behalf?' He (peace be upon him) said: 'Tell me, if your father had a debt and you paid it, would it be accepted from you?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Allah is more deserving of acceptance.' So the Prophet (peace be upon him) analogized Hajj to the debt of servants, and the unifying meaning is debt, which is an obligation established in the liability that must be fulfilled, and obligation is a legal ruling. And [it can be] singular and composite. Apparently, this is also a division of the description. So the singular description is like the cause by quantity alone and genus (i.e., weight/volume) alone for the prohibition of deferred sale, and the composite description is like quantity together with genus as the cause for the prohibition of excess. The conclusion is that his saying 'name and ruling' is undoubtedly opposite to description, and his saying 'necessary and accidental' is undoubtedly a division of description. As for 'clear and hidden', and likewise 'singular and composite', he has mentioned them in the manner of opposition and overlap, and apparently they are a division of description, for we have not found an example for them except in the division of description. Singular: i.e., not composed of parts. Composite: i.e., composed of multiple matters. It is said: this would necessitate the occurrence of causality, which is a single attribute, in multiple matters, and the occurrence of a single attribute in different loci at one time is impossible. But this is weak, for causality is not one of the joining attributes; rather it is an extracted attribute extracted from the totality insofar as it is a totality, and there is no harm in that. Do you not see that sonship is extracted from the son despite his having multiple parts?
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar is from the chapter on Qiyas (analogical reasoning) and discusses the classification of the 'illah (effective cause). The author, Imam al-Birjandi, explains that the 'illah can be described in several ways. First, it is divided into jali (clear) and khafi (hidden). A clear description is one that anyone can understand, such as the cat's habit of roaming around people, which explains why its leftover water is considered pure. This is taken from the hadith about the cat. A hidden description is one that requires some reflection, like the causes of riba (usury). According to the Hanafis, the 'illah for riba is quantity and genus; for al-Shafi'i it is measurement by weight or volume; for Malik it is being a staple food and storable. The 'illah can also be hukman, i.e., a legal ruling that unites the original and the branch, as in the hadith of Hajj by proxy: the Prophet analogized Hajj to debt because both are obligations that must be fulfilled. The second division is fard (singular) and 'adad (composite). A singular 'illah is a single attribute, like quantity alone prohibiting deferred sale. A composite 'illah is a combination, like quantity and genus together prohibiting excess. The author notes that the divisions of jali/khafi and fard/'adad are ultimately subdivisions of wasf (description), not opposed to it. He then addresses a potential objection: how can a single causality reside in multiple attributes? He responds that causality is an abstract attribute extracted from the combination, similar to sonship being abstracted from a person despite his many parts. This explanation preserves the validity of composite 'illahs in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
وصف جلي (wasf jali): A clear description that is understood by everyone, such as the cat's habit of roaming (طواف) used as 'illah for the purity of its leftover water.
وصف خفي (wasf khafi): A hidden description that requires ijtihad to identify, such as quantity/genus, weight/volume, or being a staple food/storable in riba.
علة فرد ('illa fard): A singular 'illah composed of one attribute, e.g., quantity alone or genus alone for the prohibition of nasa (deferred riba).
علة عدد ('illa 'adad): A composite 'illah composed of multiple attributes, e.g., quantity together with genus for the prohibition of fadl (excess riba).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a singular 'illah (fard) mentioned in the text?
A) The cat's roaming for purity of leftover water
B) Quantity alone for prohibition of deferred riba (nasa)
C) Quantity plus genus for prohibition of excess riba (fadl)
D) Debt as a ruling for Hajj by proxy

Key Takeaway
The effective cause in qiyas can be classified by visibility (jali/khafi) and composition (fard/'adad); the Hanafi school validates composite 'illah by treating causality as an extracted attribute.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Classifications of the Legal Cause: Singular, Composite, Clear, and Hidden
Explaining classifications of the legal cause and debating composite cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a legal description (wasf) as singular (fard) or composite (adad), clear (jali) or hidden (khafi), and evaluate the Hanafi proof for the validity of a composite cause.

Core Idea
A composite legal cause is valid because causality is an abstractive attribute, not a conjunctive accident.

This lesson explores the Hanafi classification of the descriptive cause ('wasf') in qiyas. The cause is divided into singular (fard) and composite (adad), as well as clear (jali) and hidden (khafi). A key debate arises regarding the composite cause: some scholars argue that a single accident (causality) cannot inhere in multiple attributes. The Hanafi school refutes this by demonstrating that causality is an abstractive (i'tibari) attribute, similar to fatherhood, and can thus be abstracted from a composite whole. This lesson will walk through the definitions, the objection, and the Hanafi response using rational proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary classifications of wasf
The passage mentions two pairs: singular/composite and clear/hidden. Recognize that these are divisions of the description (wasf), not of the name or ruling.
The text notes that these are presented by way of contrast and overlap.
2
Define singular and composite descriptions
A singular description (al-wasf al-fard) consists of a single attribute, e.g., measure alone. A composite description (al-wasf al-adad) consists of multiple attributes, e.g., measure and genus together.
Examples given: measure alone causes prohibition of credit (nasi'ah); measure+genus causes prohibition of excess (tafadul).
3
Understand the objection against composite cause
Some scholars argue that a composite cause is impossible because it would require a single accident (causality) to inhere in multiple loci at once, which they consider impossible.
This is the opposing dalil.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi refutation states that causality is not a conjunctive accident but an abstractive attribute (i'tibari). It can be abstracted from the composite whole, just as fatherhood is abstracted from a human with parts.
The text calls the opposing view a 'weak illusion' (wahm wahin).
5
Apply the classification to an example
Consider the prohibition of selling one sa' of wheat for another on credit (nasi'ah). The 'illah is the genus (measure/weight) alone – a singular description. For excess (tafadul), the 'illah is measure plus genus – a composite description.
This shows the practical application of the two types.

Source Text

(القمر) قلت وخالفه بعض فقالوا: لا يصح أن يكون العلة مركبا، وإلا يلزم قيام العرض الواحد وهو العلية بمحال متعددة وهو وهم واه؛ لأن العلية اعتباري واحد ينتزع من الشيئين وقت اجتماعهما كما أن الأبوّة وصف واحد ينتزع من إنسان ذات أجزاء، فهي وصف منتزع من أمور متعددة، ويحتمل أن يكون الأمور المتعددة عللاً مستقلة لهذا الواحد، فإنه عند الجمهور جائز، والذين يمنعونه فقولهم توهم باطل، وجه المنع أن المعلول متى تحقق بعلة واحدة انعدمت الحاجة إلى الأخرى، فلزم أن يكون كل واحد من العلتين علة مستقلة وأن لا يكون ووجه فساده أن هذه العلل المستقلة إنما هي للكليات، ولها تحققات يحصل كل منها من علة من العلل ولا خلف، ولو تحقق كل واحد من العلتين فيكون الأولى علة يترتب عليها المعلول الخاص وأما العلة الثانية فلتأثيرها مانع وهو أن كل واحد منهما علة وقت الانفراد، ولم يبق الانفراد للعلة الثانية، ولو تحقق العلتان معًا فالأظهر أن العلة حينئذ القدر المشترك؛ لأن وقت الاجتماع كل من العلتين غير محتاج في التأثير إلى أمر زائد فالقدر المشترك بينهما أيضا لا يكون محتاجًا إلى أمر زائد في التأثير، وعند البعض في هذه الصورة مجموع العلل الموجودة علة، وعند البعض كل واحد منهما علة واردة على المعلول الواحد الشخصي، وهو باطل للاستحالة المذكورة، فافهم وتدبّر (السنبلي) لحرمة النسأ: فبيع صاع من الحنطة بصاع من الحنطة مماثلاً نسيئة لا يجوز. Statement of the cause of analogy. And as singular and composite, apparently that is also a division of the description. So the singular description like the cause by measure alone and the genus i.e. measurement and weight alone for the prohibition of sale on credit. And the composite description like measure with genus as cause for the prohibition of excess. The conclusion is that his saying 'name and ruling' is no doubt that it is opposite to description, and his saying 'necessary and accidental' is clearly a division of description. As for 'clear' and 'hidden' and likewise 'singular' and 'composite', he mentioned them by way of contrast and overlap, and apparently it is a division of description; because we did not find an example for it except in the division of description. Description: and singular: i.e., not composed of parts. (al-Qamar) and composite: i.e., composed of multiple matters. It was said: then it necessitates the existence of causality which is a single accident in multiple matters, and the existence of a single accident in different loci at one time is impossible. But this is weak; for causality is not among the conjunctive accidents, rather it is an abstractive [accident] abstracted from the aggregate as a whole, and there is no harm in it. Do you not see that sonship is abstracted from the son despite his having multiple parts. (al-Qamar) I said: And some disagreed saying: It is not valid for the cause to be composite, otherwise it would necessitate the existence of a single accident - causality - in multiple loci, and that is a weak illusion; because causality is a single mental consideration abstracted from the two things at the time of their conjunction, just as fatherhood is a single description abstracted from a human having parts. So it is a description abstracted from multiple matters. And it is possible that the multiple matters are independent causes for this single [effect], for that is permissible according to the majority. Those who prevent it, their statement is an invalid illusion. The reason for prevention: when an effect is realized by one cause, the need for the other disappears, so it follows that each of the two causes is an independent cause and that it does not... and the invalidity of this is that these independent causes are only for universals, and they have realizations each of which occurs from one of the causes with no alternation. And if each of the two causes is realized, then the first is a cause upon which the particular effect follows, and as for the second cause, for its effect there is a preventer; and that is that each of them is a cause at the time of isolation, and isolation does not remain for the second cause. And if the two causes occur together, then the more apparent is that the cause then is the common factor; because at the time of conjunction each of the two causes does not need anything extra for effect, so the common factor between them also does not need anything extra for effect. According to some in this scenario, the sum of existing causes is the cause. According to some, each of them is a cause affecting the single individual effect, and that is invalid due to the aforementioned impossibility. So understand and deliberate. (al-Sunbulī) For the prohibition of sale on credit: So selling a sa' of wheat for a sa' of wheat equal on credit is not permissible. (al-Qamar) By way of contrast: [It is the aspect mentioned in some commentaries; because each one i.e. of hidden and clear, and likewise singular and composite, is mentioned after his saying 'name and ruling' and they are opposite to description decisively, so likewise these.] And overlap: because each of clear, hidden, singular and composite is mentioned by way of hesitation, so it is known that it is conjoined to his saying 'necessary or accidental'. Since we did not find for it i.e. for each of clear, hidden, singular and composite (al-Qamar).
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Usul al-Fiqh explains the divisions of the descriptive cause (wasf) in legal analogy. It first distinguishes between a singular description (like measure alone) and a composite description (like measure with genus). A singular description is that which is not composed of parts, while a composite consists of multiple attributes. The text then addresses a dispute: some scholars argue that a composite cause is impossible because it would require a single accident (causality) to inhere in multiple loci, which they consider impossible. The author refutes this by arguing that causality is an abstractive attribute, not a conjunctive accident; it can be abstracted from a composite whole, just as fatherhood is abstracted from a human being who has parts. The majority (jumhur) allow multiple attributes to serve as a cause, while a minority oppose it. The passage provides a rational proof (dalil aqli) to demonstrate the validity of a composite cause. It also clarifies that the terms 'clear' and 'hidden' as well as 'singular' and 'composite' are presented as divisions of the description, not of the name and ruling. Finally, an example is given: the prohibition of selling a sa' of wheat for a sa' of wheat on credit (nasī'a) illustrates the cause of genus (measurement/weight) alone causing prohibition of credit, while the combination of measure and genus causes prohibition of excess (tafādul). The commentary by al-Qamar and al-Sunbulī adds further elaboration on the points raised.

Key Terms
الوصف الفرد (al-waṣf al-fard): The singular description; a cause consisting of a single attribute (e.g., measure alone).
الوصف العدد (al-waṣf al-'adad): The composite description; a cause consisting of multiple attributes (e.g., measure with genus).
الجلي (al-jalī): The clear description; one whose suitability as a cause is obvious.
الخفي (al-khafī): The hidden description; one whose suitability requires investigation.
العلة المركبة (al-'illah al-murakkabah): The composite cause; a cause composed of multiple attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A composite cause violates the principle that one effect can only have one cause.
B) Causality is an abstractive attribute, not a conjunctive accident, so it can be abstracted from multiple attributes.
C) The Prophet explicitly forbade composite causes in qiyas.
D) Composite causes lead to infinite regress.

Key Takeaway
A composite legal cause is valid because causality is an abstractive attribute, not a conjunctive accident, as demonstrated by the fatherhood analogy and the majority view (jumhur).

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Conditions for a Description as a Valid Cause: Ṣalāḥ and ʿAdālah
Stating conditions for waṣf to be ʿillah via witness analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions of ṣalāḥ and ʿadālah to evaluate whether a description (waṣf) is a valid cause (ʿillah) for a ruling in qiyas, and identify evidence that establishes causality.

Core Idea
A waṣf is a valid ʿillah only if it is sound like a witness and its causality is proven by text or consensus.

The author of Noor al-Anwar introduces two key conditions for a waṣf to be a valid ʿillah in qiyas: ṣalāḥ (soundness) and ʿadālah (uprightness). These are inspired by conditions for a witness's testimony. Just as a witness must be fit and just, a waṣf must be appropriate for the ruling and its causal effect must be evident. This lesson unpacks these conditions and shows how they are verified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the analogy
Recognize that the waṣf in qiyas is likened to a witness in a lawsuit. Both require soundness (ṣalāḥ) and uprightness (ʿadālah) to be accepted.
The analogy drives the entire discussion.
2
Define ṣalāḥ and ʿadālah
Ṣalāḥ means the description is appropriate (e.g., freedom, sanity, adulthood, Islam). ʿAdālah means its causality is demonstrable: the description's effect appears in the genus of the ruling.
These are not arbitrary; they are based on evidence.
3
Understand ẓuhūr al-athar
ʿAdālah is verified by 'the appearance of its effect in the genus of the ruling' – meaning the causality is established by textual evidence (nass) or consensus (ijma).
The effect must be in the same genus (jins qarīb).
4
Recognize the requirement of dalīl
Not every description can be a cause; there must be a proof (dalīl) showing the description's causality. The jurist cannot arbitrarily assign a cause.
The hadith of salam provides an example where the cause (poverty) is implied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أي قبل تحقق الصلاح ثم بين معنى الصلاح والعدالة على غير ترتيب اللف، فبدأ أولاً بذكر العدالة بقوله: بظهور أثره
الوصف
في جنس الحكم المعلّل به، أي بأن ظهر أثر الوصف في جنس الحكم المعلل به من خارج
أي بذلك الوصف

(القمر)
كالأمثلة التي مرّت من اشتمال نص النهي عن بيع الآبق على العجز عن التسليم كما قد مر وغيره.(القمر) ودلالة إلخ اعلم أنه ليس أن أي وصف كان يكون علة للحكم فإنه لا تأثير لبعض الأوصاف في الحكم ككونه في وقت كذا أو مكان كذا مثلاً، وليس أن المعلّل مختار يجعل أي وصف شاء علةً للحكم سواء وجد علية ذلك الوصف لذالك الحكم أو لا، بل لا بد من دليل على كون الوصف علة للحكم، فقال المصنف: ودلالة أي دليل (القمر) للقبول أي لقبول شهادته وإثبات دعوى المدعي. (القمر) صالحا أي للشهادة بأن يكون حراً عاقلاً، بالغًا، مسلما إن كان المدعى عليه مسلمًا. (القمر) وعادلاً أي باجتنابه عن محظورات دينه. (القمر) ولا يجب إلخ أي لا يجب العمل قبل تحقق العدالة، وإنما قال: "لا يجب" ولم يقل: "لا يجوز"؛ لأنه جاز للقاضي القضاء بشهادة الفاسق لكنه لا ينبغي له (القمر) أي بأن ظهر إلخ والمراد بظهور أثره في جنس الحكم المعلل به أن يثبت عليته له شرعًا بالنص أو الإجماع والمراد بالجنس الجنس القريب، كذا قيل. (القمر)
Then he began to explain by what it is known that this description is a description [worthy of being cause] rather than others. He said: And the indication of a description being a cause is its soundness (salāh) and uprightness ('adālah). For the description in analogy is like the witness in a lawsuit. So just as it is required in the witness for acceptance that he be sound and upright, so too in the description. And just as in the witness it is not permissible to act before soundness and it is not obligatory [to act] before uprightness, so too in the description. That is, before the realization of soundness. Then he explained the meaning of soundness and uprightness in non-sequential order. He began first by mentioning uprightness with his saying: by appearance of its effect in the genus of the ruling imputed to it. That is, that the effect of the description appears in the genus of the ruling imputed to it from outside. That is, by that description. And that it be etc. is conjoined to the commentator's saying: i.e., it is permissible that that meaning is not mentioned explicitly in the text, but rather in other than it, however it is necessary that that meaning be established by that text by implication and be among its necessities, as came in the hadith that he (peace be upon him) permitted salam (advance sale) and it is imputed to the poverty of the contracting party, and this poverty is not mentioned explicitly in the text, except that the indication of the text on the contracting party is implication (iltizāmī) and poverty is his attribute. So its indication upon it is also implication. So said the greatest of scholars, so ponder. (al-Qamar) Like the examples that passed from the text of prohibition of selling a runaway slave containing inability to deliver as has passed and others. (al-Qamar) And indication etc. Know that it is not that any description whatsoever is a cause for the ruling; for some descriptions have no effect on the ruling, like being at a particular time or place for example. And it is not that the one who imputes is free to make any description he wishes a cause for the ruling, whether that description has causality for that ruling or not. Rather, there must be evidence (dalīl) on the description being a cause for the ruling. So the author said: And indication i.e., evidence (al-Qamar) for acceptance i.e., for acceptance of his testimony and establishing the claim of the plaintiff. (al-Qamar) Sound i.e., for testimony: that he be free, sane, adult, Muslim if the defendant is Muslim. (al-Qamar) And upright i.e., by his avoidance of forbidden things of his religion. (al-Qamar) And it is not obligatory etc. i.e., it is not obligatory to act before the realization of uprightness. And he only said "not obligatory" and did not say "not permissible" because it is permissible for the judge to judge by the testimony of a sinner (fāsiq) but it is not befitting for him. (al-Qamar) That is, by appearance etc. And what is meant by appearance of its effect in the genus of the ruling imputed to it is that its causality for it is established religiously by text or consensus. And what is meant by genus is the near genus, it is said. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the conditions for a description (wasf) to be considered a valid cause ('illah) in qiyas. The author uses an analogy: just as a witness in court must be sound (fit to testify) and upright (just), so too must the description be sound and upright. Soundness means the description is appropriate for being a cause, and uprightness means its effect is apparent. The passage explains that 'uprightness' is indicated by the appearance of the description's effect in the genus (jins) of the ruling—meaning that the causality is established by text (nass) or consensus (ijma). The description does not have to be explicitly mentioned in the text; it can be implied, as in the case of the poverty of the contracting party in the hadith of salam (advance sale). The poverty is not explicit but implied from the context. The passage emphasizes that not every description can be a cause; only those with evidence (dalil) proving their causality. It also clarifies that a judge may act on the testimony of a sinner if necessary, but it is not recommended. The commentator al-Qamar provides further explanation, linking the concept to the testimony conditions and noting that the effect must appear in the near genus.

Key Terms
الصلاح (al-ṣalāḥ): Soundness of the description: it must be appropriate (like being free, sane, adult, Muslim) to serve as a cause, analogous to the fitness of a witness.
العدالة (al-'adālah): Uprightness of the description: it must show its effect in the genus of the ruling, establishing causality via text or consensus.
ظهور الأثر (ẓuhūr al-athar): Appearance of the effect: the description's causal effect must be evident in the same genus of ruling, established by religious evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'appearance of its effect in the genus of the ruling' mean for a description to be considered an 'illah?
A) The description must be explicitly mentioned in the Qur'an or Sunnah.
B) The description's causality must be established by religious evidence (text or consensus) and affect the same genre of ruling.
C) The description must be physically observable.
D) The description must be agreed upon by all jurists.

Key Takeaway
A description is a valid ʿillah only if it is sound (ṣāliḥ) for the ruling and its causality is proven by the appearance of its effect in the genre, established by text or consensus.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
15 min
Conditions for a Valid 'Illa: Ṣalāḥ and ʿAdāla
Defining the criteria for identifying the effective cause in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ṣalāḥ and ʿadāla as conditions for a valid 'illa in Hanafi qiyas, and apply the four types of ẓuhūr al-athar to evaluate a description's causality.

Core Idea
A valid 'illa must be both suitable (ṣāliḥ) and just (ʿādil), with its effect apparent in the genus or specific ruling.

Just as a witness in court must be suitable and just to be accepted, the description (waṣf) used as the cause ('illa) in qiyas must also meet these two criteria. The author of the commentary explains that 'suitability' (ṣalāḥ) means the description is appropriate to the ruling and not remote, while 'justice' (ʿadāla) is evidenced by the appearance of its effect (ẓuhūr al-athar) in the genus of the ruling. This lesson unpacks these conditions and the four levels of effect appearance, all considered valid proofs for causality in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Understand the witness analogy
Recognize that the author likens the description to a witness: both must be ṣāliḥ (suitable) and ʿādil (just). Just as a court requires these qualities for witness testimony, qiyas requires them for the 'illa.
The analogy is a rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī) for the necessity of these conditions.
2
Define ṣalāḥ and ʿadāla
Ṣalāḥ means the description is appropriate (mulāʾima) to the ruling—i.e., it makes sense to attach the ruling to it. ʿAdāla means the description shows its effect (athar) in the genus of the ruling, established by text (naṣṣ) or consensus (ijmāʿ).
The passage clarifies that ʿadāla is not about personal righteousness but about evident causality.
3
Grasp ẓuhūr al-athar as the sign of ʿadāla
The appearance of the description's effect in the genus of the ruling is the minimal level of ʿadāla. If the effect appears in the specific ruling itself, it is even stronger (bi al-ṭarīq al-ūlā).
The author stresses that evidence of causality (text or consensus) is needed, not mere speculation.
4
Learn the four types of effect appearance
The passage divides ẓuhūr al-athar into four categories: (1) effect of specific description in specific ruling, (2) specific description in genus of ruling, (3) genus of description in specific ruling, (4) genus of description in genus of ruling. Memorize the examples given.
Examples: 1) circumambulation in cat's leftover water (purity), 2) minority in guardianship rights, 3) unconsciousness in dropping many prayers, 4) travel hardship in shortening prayer.
5
Recognize that all four types are acceptable
The author states that all four types are accepted as proofs (ḥujja) for causality, even though there was disagreement on the fourth type. The chosen view (mukhtār) is that it is a valid proof because it leads to a preponderant presumption of causality.
The fourth type (genus-genus) is the weakest but still valid according to the preferred opinion.
