باب القياس بيان علة القياس فلا يدلّ على كونه علة والعدم لا دخل له في علية شيء بالبداهة، ولظهوره لم يتعرّض له. ومن جنسه التعليل بالنفي، أي مثل الاطراد في عدم صلاحيته للدليل التعليل بالنفي، ووقع في بعض النسخ قوله : "ومن جنسه"؛ لأن استقصاء العدم لا يمنع الوجود من وجه آخر؛ أي وجود الحكم لأن الحكم قد يثبت بعلل شتّى، فلا يلزم من انتفاء علةٍ ما انتفاء جميع العلل من الدنيا حتى يكون نفي العلة دالا على نفي الحكم كقول الشافعي بالله في النكاح، أي في عدم انعقاد النكاح بشهادة النساء مع الرجال: إنه ليس مال وكل ما هو ليس بمال لا ينعقد بشهادة النساء مع الرجال، فلا بد في إثباته من أن يكونا رجلين دون رجل وامرأتين، وعندنا النكاح ليس لعدم المالية تأثير في عدم صحته بالنساء؛ لأن علة صحة شهادة النساء هي كونه أي في انعقاد النكاح المشهود به فلا يدل إلخ أي فلا يدل وجود الحكم عند وجود الوصف على كون ذلك الوصف علة له، غاية الأمر أن الدوران يدل على الملزوم بين الحكم والوصف، واللزوم لا يستلزم العلية، ألا ترى أن معلولي علة واحدة يكون بينهما لزوم، وليس أحدهما علة للأخر. (القمر) لا دخل له إلخ : فإن العدم ليس بشيء فكيف يكون علة. (القمر) التعليل بالنفي أي بنفي العلة على نفي الحكم. (القمر) لأن استقصاء العدم أي عدم العلة بأن طلب علة فلم توجد فانتهى إلى عدمها فإضافة الاستقصاء إلى العدم بأدنى ملابسته. (القمر) كقول الشافعي له إلخ : أي هذا التعليل كقول الشافعي يحلله ثم اعلم أنه تمسك بعض الشافعية في كون العدمي علة للوجودي بأن عدم قدرة الجماع علة التفريق والعنة تعبير عنه، والتعبير بالوجودي لا ينفع؛ فإن العنة ليس علة التفريق إلا بسبب عدم قدرة الجماع فهو العلة إصالةً، ونحن نقول: إنه بعروض الفالج وغيره قد لا يقدر الزوج على الجماع مع أنه ليس يوجب التفريق، فليس علة للتفريق، بل العلة للتفريق إنما هو وجودي. (القمر) بشهادة النساء: أي شهادة امرأتين ورجل (القمر) وكل ما هو ليس إلخ لأن المال هو المستهان وكثرت فيه المعاملة والمساهلة فرخص في شهادة النساء مع كونها ذات شبهة لعدم الضبط والإتقان الكامل في النساء دفعًا للضرورة، وأما ما ليس بمال كالنكاح والحدود فليس بمستهان، ولا يكثر فيه المعاملة، فليس فيه ضرورة إلى رخصة الشهادة المشتبهة، فيجب إثباته بالحجة الأصلية، أي شهادة الرجال وحدهم. (القمر) صحته أي عدم صحة النكاح بشهادة النساء. هي كونه أي كون النكاح مع كونه حقا من حقوق العباد مما لا يسقط بشبهة، فإنه إذا طرأت عليه شبهة بعد العنة وهو معنى ثبوته لا يسقط بها، بل إذا كانت الشبهة مقارنة له لا منع هذه الشبهة عن الانعقاد كنكاح الهازل. (القمر)
Chapter of Qiyas: Explanation of the Illa of Qiyas. So it does not indicate that it is the cause, and non-existence has no role in the causality of anything by self-evidence, and due to its obviousness he did not address it. Of its kind is reasoning by negation, i.e., like consistency (itrad) in its unsuitability as evidence: reasoning by negation. And in some copies it occurs: 'Of its kind' because the exhaustive search for non-existence does not prevent existence from another aspect; i.e., the existence of the ruling because the ruling may be established by various causes, so the negation of one cause does not necessitate the negation of all causes from the world such that negation of cause indicates negation of ruling, like the saying of al-Shafi'i, by Allah, concerning marriage: i.e., concerning the non-contractual validity of marriage with the testimony of women along with men: it is not property, and everything that is not property is not contracted with the testimony of women with men, so its establishment requires two men and not one man and two women. And according to us, marriage—the lack of property has no effect on its invalidity with women because the cause of the validity of women's testimony is that it (marriage) is (i.e., regarding the contractual validity of marriage) the thing testified about. So it does not indicate etc., i.e., the existence of the ruling when the description exists does not indicate that that description is its cause. At most, correlation (dawaran) indicates the necessary relation (luzum) between the ruling and the description, but necessary relation does not entail causality. Do you not see that two effects of one cause have a necessary relation between them, yet neither is the cause of the other. (al-Qamar) 'It has no role etc.': non-existence is nothing, so how can it be a cause? (al-Qamar) 'Reasoning by negation': i.e., by negating the cause to negate the ruling. (al-Qamar) 'Because the exhaustive search for non-existence': i.e., the non-existence of the cause by seeking a cause and not finding it, so it ends at its non-existence, so the addition of 'search' to 'non-existence' is with minimal connection. (al-Qamar) 'Like the saying of al-Shafi'i to him etc.' i.e., this reasoning is like the saying of al-Shafi'i. Then know that some Shafi'is argued that the non-existent can be a cause for the existent by saying that the inability to have intercourse is the cause of separation, and impotence ('innah) is an expression of it, but the expression in terms of existent is not helpful; because impotence is not the cause of separation except due to the inability to have intercourse, so it is the cause primarily. And we say: With the occurrence of stroke (falij) and other things, the husband may be unable to have intercourse yet it does not necessitate separation, so it is not a cause for separation. Rather, the cause for separation is only existential. (al-Qamar) 'With the testimony of women': i.e., the testimony of two women and one man. (al-Qamar) 'And everything that is not etc.' because property is held in low esteem and transactions and leniency are abundant therein, so leniency was granted regarding women's testimony despite its ambiguity due to women's lack of full precision and mastery, out of necessity. As for what is not property, like marriage and hadd penalties, it is not held in low esteem, nor are transactions abundant, so there is no necessity for the concession of ambiguous testimony; therefore it must be established by the original evidence, i.e., the testimony of men alone. (al-Qamar) 'Its validity' i.e., the invalidity of marriage with women's testimony. It is that marriage, being a right of the servants that is not nullified by ambiguity, because if an ambiguity arises after its establishment, it is not nullified, but if the ambiguity is concomitant, it does not prevent the contract, like the marriage of a jester. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This is a usul rule passage from the chapter on Qiyas. It explains why absence (adam) cannot serve as an illa (effective cause) for a hukm. The passage begins by stating that the mere existence of a ruling when a description is present does not prove that the description is the cause. Non-existence has no role in causality by self-evidence. The author then discusses 'reasoning by negation' (ta'lil bi'l-nafy), which is akin to consistency (itrad) in its unsuitability as evidence. The point is that exhausting possibilities of non-existence does not rule out the existence of a cause from another direction. A ruling can have multiple causes, so negating one cause does not negate all. The example of Imam al-Shafi'i is given: He argued that nikah (marriage) is not property, and anything not property cannot be established by the testimony of women with men, so nikah requires two male witnesses. The Hanafi response is that the validity of women's testimony in property transactions is due to leniency and necessity. Nikah, being a right of Allah that is not nullified by ambiguities, does not require such leniency. The passage further refutes the Shafi'i attempt to use inability to have intercourse (a non-existent) as a cause for annulment (khul' or faskh), arguing that the true cause is an existential condition. The Hanafi position is that only positive attributes can serve as illa. The commentator (al-Qamar) clarifies that non-existence is nothing and cannot be a cause. This lesson establishes the Hanafi usul principle that causality requires positive existence.

Key Terms
عدمية (adamiyya): A description that is non-existent; absence of an attribute.
تعليل بالنفي (ta'lil bi'l-nafy): Reasoning by negation, i.e., negating the ruling based on the negation of a possible cause.
اطراد (itrad): Consistency; the property of a description being present whenever the ruling is present, but it does not prove causality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul in this passage, why is the argument that 'marriage is not property, so it cannot be established by women's testimony' invalid?
A) Because marriage is actually a type of property.
B) Because the cause for validity of women's testimony is not property but necessity and leniency.
C) Because the Shafi'i school does not accept this argument.
D) Because absence of property status is a positive cause.

Key Takeaway
Absence cannot be an effective cause (illa) in Qiyas; only existent attributes can serve as causes.

Istishab al-Hal and Its Exception: The Role of Sabab Mu'ayyan
Explaining istishab al-hal and its exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when istishab al-hal is inapplicable due to a sabab mu'ayyan and apply the exception to derive rulings in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
When a ruling has an exclusive cause, istishab cannot presume the ruling in the cause's absence.

Istishab al-hal is a foundational principle in Hanafi usul, allowing continuity of a known state. However, this principle has a crucial limitation: when the cause (sabab) of a ruling is explicitly specified and exclusive, the absence of that cause negates the ruling, and istishab cannot be used to argue for its continuation. This lesson explores that exception through two classical examples from Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Define istishab al-hal
State its meaning as presumption of continuity of a previously established state or ruling until evidence of change.
Istishab is a hujja (proof) but weaker than explicit dalil.
2
Identify the exception
Recognize that istishab is overridden when the sabab (cause) for a ruling is mu'ayyan (specified and exclusive) and is absent.
The exception is expressed via istithna' mufargh in the text.
3
Analyze the ghasb example
Apply the exception to the child of a usurped slave: the cause of liability is specifically ghasb, which does not apply to the child, so no liability.
The example shows absence of cause trumps istishab.
4
Analyze the khums example
Apply the exception to sea-extracted goods: the cause for khums is ijaf (charging horses) in battle, not applicable to sea extraction.
Ibn al-Malik explains that khums only applies to property in disbelievers' hands acquired through ijaf.
5
Synthesize the rule
Formulate the complete rule: Istishab is valid in doubt about the existence of a cause, but not when the cause is determined and its absence is certain.
This limitation preserves the principle that rulings are tied to their causes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس بيان استصحاب الحال والاحتجاج باستصحاب الحال، عطف على التعليل بالنفي، أي مثل الاطراد الاحتجاج استثناء مفرغ من قوله إلخ: أي مما يفهم من قوله ومثله إلخ وهو عدم صلاحية التعليل بالنفي، والاستثناء المفرغ عبارة التعليل أي على نفي الحكم. (القمر) إذ لا وجه له أي لوجود الحكم فإن ثبوت الحكم بدون العلة ممتنع ، وهذا متعلّق بقوله : يمنع. (القمر) ليست إلا الغصب فالسبب للضمان متعين. (القمر) ليست إلا إيجاف إلخ فالسبب لخُمس الغنيمة متعين، قال ابن الملك: إنما يجب الخُمس فيما إذا كان في أيدي الكفار وانتقل إلى المسلمين بإيجاف الخيل، والمستخرج من قعر البحر لم يكن في أيدي الكفار؛ لأن قعر الماء يمنع أيديهم، فلا يكون من الغنيمة، فلا يكون فيه الخمس. (القمر)
Chapter of Qiyas: Explanation of Istishab al-Hal. And arguing by istishab al-hal is a conjunction to 'reasoning by negation', i.e., like consistency (itrad) the argument by means of a exceptive construction (istithna' mufargh) from his saying etc.: i.e., from what is understood from his saying 'and the like' etc., which is the unsuitability of reasoning by negation. And the exceptive construction is the expression of reasoning, i.e., for negating the ruling. (al-Qamar) Because there is no basis for it, i.e., for existence of the ruling, for the establishment of a ruling without a cause is impossible; and this relates to his saying 'it prevents'. (al-Qamar) 'It is only usurpation (ghasb)', so the cause for liability is specified. (al-Qamar) 'It is only the charging of horses (ijaf)', so the cause for the khums of booty is specified. Ibn al-Malik said: Khums is obligatory only when the property is in the hands of the disbelievers and is transferred to Muslims by charging horses; what is extracted from the bottom of the sea was not in the hands of the disbelievers because the depth of the water prevents their possession, so it is not booty, and there is no khums on it.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This is a usul rule passage on istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity). The author discusses that istishab is a proof, but it is subject to an exception: when the cause of a ruling is known to be exclusively a specific factor, then the absence of that factor negates the ruling, and istishab cannot be used to presume the ruling. The passage links istishab to the earlier discussion on reasoning by negation. The commentator al-Qamar explains that if there is no basis (wajh) for the ruling's existence, its establishment without a cause is impossible. Two examples from Imam Muhammad are given: (1) In the case of an usurped pregnant slave, the child is not liable because the child was not usurped; the cause of liability is specifically usurpation, which does not apply to the child. (2) In the case of goods extracted from the sea (e.g., pearls), there is no khums because the cause for khums is specifically charging of horses (ijaf) in battle against unbelievers; sea extraction is not included. These examples show that when the cause is determined (mut'ayyan), its absence conclusively negates the ruling, overriding any presumption of continuity. This lesson teaches that istishab is used in cases of doubt about the existence of a cause, but not when the cause is known and its absence is certain.

Key Terms
استصحاب الحال (istishab al-hal): Presumption of continuity: assuming that a previously established state or ruling remains until evidence of change.
استثناء مفرغ (istithna' mufargh): An exceptive construction where the exception is from a general statement that is not explicitly mentioned; here it indicates that the only basis for negating the ruling is when the cause is specified.
سبب معين (sabab mu'ayyan): A specified cause; the exclusive factor that brings about the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is no khums due on items extracted from the sea?
A) Because the sea is not owned by anyone.
B) Because the cause for khums is specifically ‘ijaf (charging of horses), which does not apply to sea extraction.
C) Because such items are not considered wealth.
D) Because the Muslims did not intend to fight for them.

Key Takeaway
Istishab al-hal cannot override a ruling whose exclusive cause is absent.

Acceptance of Ta'lil bi al-Nafy in Hanafi Qiyas
Explaining the rule that causation by negation is valid only when the cause is specified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that causation by negation (al-ta'lil bi al-nafy) is valid only when the cause is specifically identified, and to identify its correct application in qiyas.

Core Idea
Causation by negation is valid only when the cause is uniquely specified.

This passage establishes a critical limit on negative reasoning in Hanafi usul. While some forms of negative inference are common, the Hanafi school restricts ta'lil bi al-nafy to cases where the cause is precisely defined and the only possible cause. Through two examples from Imam Muhammad – the usurped slave girl's offspring and sea-gathered items – we see how this principle operates in actual juristic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Read the Arabic statement: 'إلا أن يكون السبب معينًا... التعليل بالنفي لا يقبل في حال من الأحوال إلا في حال كون السبب معينًا.' Understand that ta'lil bi al-nafy is rejected except when the cause is specific.
2
Understand the rationale
The text says: 'فإن عدمه يمنع وجود الحكم من وجه آخر؛ إذ لا وجه له.' If the cause is not specific, absence of one possible cause does not negate the ruling because there might be another cause.
3
Analyze the first example
Consider the case of a usurped pregnant slave girl. The usurper is liable for the mother but not the child because the cause of liability (usurpation) applies specifically to the mother. The child was not usurped, so the cause is absent.
4
Analyze the second example
Consider items from the sea (pearls, ambergris). No khums is due because the cause of khums (military conquest with horses) is absent. The cause is specific to conquest, not mere acquisition.
5
Summarize the principle
Ta'lil bi al-nafy is valid only when the cause is mu'ayyan (specific) and the only possible cause for the ruling. Otherwise, the ruling may stand on another basis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
بیان استصحاب الحال
مما لا يسقط بشبهة لا كونه مالاً، بخلاف الحدود والقصاص مما يندرء بالشبهات، فإنه لا يثبت بشهادة النساء قطّ وأيضًا هو أدنى درجة من المال بدليل ثبوته بالهزل الذي
أي النكاح
لا يثبت به المال، فلما كان المال يثبت بشهادة النساء فبالأولى أن يثبت بها النكاح. إلا أن يكون السبب معينًا استثناء مُفرّغ من قوله : ومثله" تعليل بالنفي" أي لا يقبل
التعليل بالنفي في حال من الأحوال إلا في حال كون السبب معينًا، فإن عدمه يمنع وجود
أي بالنفي العلة الحكم من وجه آخر؛ إذ لا وجه له.
السبب المعين
كقول محمد له في ولد الغصب إنه لم يضمن؛ لأنه لم يغصب، فإن من غصب جارية حاملة، فولدت في يد الغاصب، ثم هلكا، يضمن قيمة الجارية دون الولد؛ لأن الغصب
أي الجارية والولد
إنما وقع على الجارية دون الولد، فقد علل محمد له ههنا بالنفي بأن علة الضمان في هذه الصورة ليست إلا الغصب؛ فبانتفائه ينتفي الضمان ضرورةً، وهكذا قوله في أي الغصب المستخرج من البحر كاللؤلؤ والعنبر : إنه لا خُمس فيه؛ لأنه لم يُوجف عليه المسلمون؛
الإمام محمد سے
فإن علة وجوب خُمس الغنيمة ليست إلا إيجاف المسلمين بالخيل، وهو منتف ههنا.
Chapter of Qiyas. Explanation of Istishab al-Hal. [Text] Not dropped due to a doubt, not being property, unlike hadd and qisas punishments which are averted by doubts, for they are never established by the testimony of women. Also, it is of a lower degree than property, evidenced by its being established through jest [i.e., marriage] which does not establish property. Since property is established by the testimony of women, then even more so marriage should be established by it. Except when the cause is specific, an exclusion from his saying: 'And like it is ta'lil bial-nafy', meaning: causation by negation is not accepted under any circumstance except when the cause is specific. For its absence prevents the existence of the ruling from another aspect, as there is no aspect for it. Like Muhammad's saying concerning an offspring of a usurped [object]: he is not liable because he did not usurp. If someone usurps a pregnant slave girl and she gives birth in his hand, then both perish, he is liable for the value of the slave girl but not the offspring, because the usurpation occurred only on the slave girl, not the offspring. So Muhammad here gave causation by negation: the cause of liability in this case is only usurpation; when it is absent, liability is necessarily absent. Similarly, his saying concerning anything taken from the sea like pearls and ambergris: there is no khums on it because the Muslims did not ride upon it [for conquest]. For the cause of the obligation of khums on spoils is only the riding of Muslims with horses, which is absent here.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul principle of 'ta'lil bi al-nafy' (causation by negation) as applied in Hanafi qiyas. The author first presents a context: marriage is established by the testimony of women because it is not a hadd or qisas punishment (which are averted by doubts) and it is of a lower degree than property, yet property itself is established by women's testimony, so marriage should be even more so. Then the focus shifts to the rule: causation by negation (i.e., proving a ruling by the absence of its cause) is not acceptable except when the cause is specific and known. If the cause is not specific, then the absence of one possible cause does not negate the ruling because there might be another cause. Two examples from Imam Muhammad's fiqh illustrate this: (1) In a case of usurpation of a pregnant slave girl, the usurper is liable for the slave but not the child, because the cause (usurpation) is specific to the slave; (2) In the case of items retrieved from the sea (like pearls), no khums is due because the specific cause of khums (military conquest with horses) is absent. These examples show that ta'lil bi al-nafy is valid only when the cause is uniquely identifiable.

Key Terms
التعليل بالنفي (al-ta'lil bi al-nafy): Causation by negation: deriving a ruling based on the absence of a specific cause; accepted only when the cause is uniquely identified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi example of the usurped slave girl's offspring, why is the usurper not liable for the child's value?
A) Because the child is not property
B) Because the cause of liability (usurpation) applies only to the mother, not the child
C) Because the child was born after the usurpation
D) Because the usurper did not intend to usurp the child

Key Takeaway
Ta'lil bi al-nafy is accepted in Hanafi qiyas only when the cause is specifically identified and is the only possible basis for the ruling.

Ta'arud al-Ashbah: Conflicting Similarities as an Invalid Proof
Explains why conflicting similarities are invalid as a legal proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to IDENTIFY the concept of ta'arud al-ashbah and APPLY the Hanafi rule that such conflicting similarities cannot serve as a valid legal proof.

Core Idea
Conflicting similarities cancel out and cannot establish a ruling; only a clear, non-contradictory illa is valid.

In this lesson, we examine a key usul principle: ta'arud al-ashbah (conflicting similarities) cannot be used as a proof for legal reasoning. The source text explains why and provides examples from shuf'a, inheritance of a missing person, and a slave's manumission. Understanding this principle helps us see the Hanafi commitment to certainty in causal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Define ta'arud al-ashbah
Identify the definition from the text: a conflict of two matters, each of which could potentially apply to the disputed case.
2
Identify the ruling on its validity
State that the Hanafi school considers it invalid as a proof for ta'lil (legal reasoning).
Literal: 'الاحتجاج بتعارض الأشباه في عدم صلاحيته للدليل'
3
Examine the example of the 'hand' (yad)
The hand is evidence of ownership; it can defend against a claim but cannot be used to aggressively claim pre-emption. This illustrates conflicting uses.
The same evidence cannot serve both defensive and offensive roles without clear preference.
4
Apply to the missing person case
Istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity) can only defend existing rights, not create new ones. Thus, the missing person's wealth is suspended.
Neither life nor death is certain, so conflicting similarities cancel out.
5
Distinguish from Shafi'i view
Shafi'i school allows istishab to obligate (e.g., slave case). Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
Hanafi: slave not freed; Shafi'i: slave freed.

Explanation of the invalidity of conflicting similarities for legal reasoning: in the case of the share to realize the disagreement of al-Shafi'i with him; since he does not hold pre-emption in [the neighborhood]. And arguing by conflicting similarities is attached to what came before, i.e., like the regularity condition, arguing by conflicting similarities is invalid as a proof. It is the conflict of two matters, each of which could potentially apply to the disputed case. Like the facilities (marafiq) suffice for repelling; the hand is evidence of ownership, so it repels with it the claim of another, and it [the hand] entitles pre-emption against the buyer. (Al-Qamar) 'And indeed the placing of the issue etc.' and what is in 'Maseer al-Da'ir': "And indeed he placed the issue regarding the share" as a precaution against the place of disagreement, because 'maseer' of pre-emption by neighborhood is not established according to him, so I cannot comprehend it. (Al-Qamar) 'And upon this' meaning that istishab al-hal is not a proof according to us. (Al-Qamar) 'And upon this we said etc.' He said in 'al-Tanwir': It is appropriate for deniers of istishab to say in this issue: the missing person is doubtful in his life and death, and neither is established; therefore the father does not inherit from him; because the condition for inheritance is the life of the heir after the death of the testator, and the life of the missing person is not established, as they say regarding a child who did not cry: that he does not inherit because his life is not established. Also, the missing person's relatives do not inherit from him; because the condition for inheritance is the death of the testator, and his death is not established either, so the condition for inheriting his property is not established. Therefore, the missing person's wealth becomes suspended until his death is established with certainty. This is a summary of what is in 'al-Tanwir'. (Al-Qamar) 'By istishab al-hal' i.e., his life is judged up to the known period by istishab of the past life for the present life. (Al-Qamar) 'Defender' i.e., against taking ownership of the missing person's wealth. (Al-Qamar) 'Not obligator' so that he would be an heir from his testator and owner of his wealth. (Al-Qamar) 'Many other issues' it is said from the controversial issues: when a man says to his slave: 'If you do not enter the house today, you are free.' The day passes and he does not know whether he entered or not. Then the master says: 'You entered the house,' and the slave says: 'I did not enter.' So the saying is the master's according to us, and the slave is not freed; because the slave adheres to istishab al-hal; because the original is non-entry, and it does not suffice as a proof to obligate the master. And according to al-Shafi'i, the saying is the slave's; because it suffices for obligation, so it is as if the slave established evidence of non-entry, so he becomes free. (Al-Qamar) 'Upon what came before' i.e., the statement of reasoning by negation. (Al-Qamar) 'And it is' i.e., the argument by conflicting similarities.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage introduces the usul principle that conflicting similarities (ta'arud al-ashbah) are not valid as a proof for legal reasoning (ta'lil). The text explains that ta'arud al-ashbah means two contradictory matters, each of which could potentially be analogous to the case in question, thus they cannot serve as a reliable basis for ruling. For example, the 'hand' (yad) as evidence of ownership: it can be used to repel a claim from someone else, but it cannot be used to aggressively establish pre-emption (shuf'a) against the buyer because that would be a conflicting application. The commentary by Qamar adds that this is why the Hanafi school holds that istishab al-hal is not a binding proof; it only works defensively. He then delves into the missing person case and the slave case as further examples where the conflict arises. The passage also includes a reference to 'al-Tanwir' which suggests that deniers of istishab (like Ibn al-Humam) would resolve the missing person issue by acknowledging that both life and death are unestablished, hence no inheritance flows either way—the wealth is suspended. This aligns with the principle that conflicting similarities cannot produce a definite ruling.

Key Terms
تعارض الأشباه (ta'arud al-ashbah): The conflict of two or more similar attributes or characteristics, each of which could potentially serve as the cause (illa) for a ruling, leading to uncertainty.
تعليل (ta'lil): Legal reasoning by identifying the cause (illa) for a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are conflicting similarities (ta'arud al-ashbah) not a valid proof for legal reasoning according to this passage?
A) Because they are based on weak analogies.
B) Because they cancel each other out and lack definitive force to establish a ruling.
C) Because they are only applicable in criminal law.
D) Because they are used exclusively in the Shafi'i school.

Key Takeaway
Ta'arud al-ashbah is invalid for legal reasoning because it leads to uncertainty, and only clear, non-contradictory proofs can establish rulings.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Why Conflicting Similarities Are Invalid as a Legal Cause
Argument explaining why conflict in similarities invalidates legal reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why conflicting similarities are invalid for legal reasoning under Hanafi usul, and distinguish between the two functions of legal proof: daf' (repelling) and ilzam (binding).

Core Idea
Conflicting similarities create doubt, and doubt cannot establish a ruling; only clear evidence suffices.

In this lesson, we examine a key Hanafi usul principle: conflicting similarities (ta'arud al-ashbah) cannot serve as a valid basis for legal reasoning. The passage argues that the apparent (zahir) is sufficient for both repelling claims and binding obligations, so there is no need to resort to conflicting similarities. We will explore two illustrative examples from fiqh: pre-emption (shuf'a) and the missing person (mafqud), and then see how the Hanafi school refutes arguments based on conflicting similarities, including those of Zufar and some Shafi'is.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
The author states that conflicting similarities are invalid for legal reasoning. Note that the 'zahir' (apparent evidence) serves both to repel claims (daf') and to bind obligations (ilzam). Write down this distinction.
Daf' repels a claim; ilzam imposes an obligation.
2
Analyze the pre-emption example
The passage uses the example of pre-emption (shuf'a) to show that the hand (yad) as evidence of ownership fulfills both functions. The neighbor's possession repels the seller's claim and binds the buyer to transfer ownership.
This demonstrates that a single clear evidence can do both jobs.
3
Understand the missing person example
Hanafis rule that a missing person is alive regarding his own property (so heirs cannot inherit from him) and dead regarding others' property (so he does not inherit from someone else). The reason is that istishab (presumption of continuity) only repels claims; it cannot bind.
Istishab is a weaker proof, only for daf'.
4
Critique Zufar's argument on ghayat
Zufar argued that since some end points (ghayat) are included in the limited and some are not, the elbows might be excluded from washing by analogy to fasting until night. The Hanafi response is that doubt does not establish anything; acting on doubt is acting without evidence.
The argument leads to an infinite regress or admission of ignorance.
5
Evaluate the comprehensive attribute problem
The passage also rejects arguments that use a comprehensive attribute without a distinguishing description in the branch. For example, comparing touching the penis to urine fails because the distinguishing description (being a source of impurity) is absent in the branch.
This shows that analogies based on conflicting similarities are invalid.

Statement of the invalidity of conflicting similarities for legal reasoning
Because the apparent (zahir) according to him is suitable for both repelling and binding; so he takes pre-emption from the buyer compulsorily, and the matter is placed on neighborhood. And on this basis we said regarding the missing person: He is alive regarding his own property so his wealth is not divided among his heirs, and dead regarding the property of others; so he does not inherit from the wealth of his testator; because his life is by istishab al-hal, and it is suitable for repelling his heirs not binding upon his testator. And of this type are many other issues mentioned in fiqh. Statement of the invalidity of conflicting similarities for legal reasoning] In the share to realize therein the disagreement of al-Shafi'i with him; since he does not say pre-emption in And arguing with conflicting similarities, conjunct to what precedes, i.e., like the habitual pattern, arguing with conflicting similarities in its invalidity as a proof, and it is the contradiction of two matters each of which can be attached to the disputed case. Like the elbows. It is suitable for repelling because the hand is evidence of ownership, so with it he repels the claim of another and deserves pre-emption from the buyer. (al-Qamar) 'And the matter is placed' etc. And what is in 'Maseer al-Da'ir': 'The matter is placed in the share' as a precaution from the place of disagreement, for 'the law of pre-emption by neighborhood is not established according to him, and that is something I do not comprehend.' (al-Qamar) 'And on this' i.e., that istishab al-hal is not a proof according to us. (al-Qamar) 'And on this we said' etc.: He said in 'al-Tanwir': 'It is incumbent on deniers of istishab to say in this issue: The missing person is doubtful in his life and death and neither is established, therefore the father does not inherit; because the condition of inheritance is the life of the heir after the death of the testator, and the life of the missing person is not established, just as they say regarding the newborn who has not cried: He does not inherit due to lack of establishment of his life. Also the relatives of the missing person do not inherit him; because the condition of inheritance is the death of the testator, and his death is also not established, so the condition of inheriting his wealth is not established, therefore the wealth of the missing person is suspended until his death is established with certainty.' This is the summary of what is in 'al-Tanwir'. (al-Qamar) 11 By istishab al-hal i.e., his life is judged up to the known period by continuing the past life to the present life. (al-Qamar) 'Repelling' i.e., from ownership of the missing person's wealth. (al-Qamar) 'Not binding' so that he would be an heir from his testator and owner of his wealth. (al-Qamar) 'Other issues' – it is said from the issues of disagreement: the case when a man says to his slave: 'If you do not enter the house today, you are free,' the day passes and it is not known whether he entered or not. Then the master says: 'You entered the house,' but the slave says: 'I did not enter.' According to us, the statement is the master's, and the slave is not freed; because the slave clings to istishab al-hal; because the original is non-entry, so it is not a valid proof for binding upon the master. According to al-Shafi'i, the statement is the slave's; because it is suitable for binding, so it is as if the slave established evidence of non-entry, so he is freed. (al-Qamar) 'Upon what precedes' i.e., the statement of legal reasoning by negation. (al-Qamar) 'And it is' i.e., the argument with conflicting similarities. (al-Qamar)

Chapter of Analogy
42
Statement of the invalidity of conflicting similarities for legal reasoning
Like the statement of Zufar to him regarding the non-obligation of washing the elbows: 'Among the end points are those that enter into the limited, like their saying: And in the ruling of the limited, you read the book from its beginning to its end. And among them are those that do not enter, like His statement: 'Then complete the fast until' – in the ruling of the limited – 'the night'; so the elbows do not enter into the obligation of washing the hand due to doubt; because doubt does not establish anything at all. (al-Baqarah: 187) And this is acting without evidence, i.e., this argument by which Zufar argued is acting without evidence, so it is invalid; because doubt is a contingent matter, so it must have evidence. If he says: 'Its evidence is conflicting similarities?' We say: Also a contingent matter, it must have evidence. If he says: 'Its evidence is the entry of some end points with the non-entry of some of them?' We say to him: 'Do you know to which category the disputed matter belongs?' If he says: 'I know,' then doubt has gone and knowledge has come. If he says: 'I do not know,' then he has admitted his ignorance and lack of evidence with him, and that is not a proof against us. And the argument with what does not stand alone except with a description by which the distinction occurs is conjunct to what precedes, i.e., like the habitual pattern in its invalidity as a proof: clinging to the comprehensive matter that does not stand by itself in establishing the ruling, except by the addition of a description by which the distinction occurs between the original and the branch where it is not present in the branch. Like his statement regarding touching the penis, i.e., the statement of the Shafi'is in making touching the penis a nullifier of ablution: The original (the analogized upon) the analogized (the description) 'until the night' so the night is not included in the fast. (al-Qamar) 'Due to doubt' i.e., the doubt that is established by conflicting similarities. (al-Qamar) 'Conflicting similarities' etc., i.e., the occurrence of the similarities of this end point conflicting in the ruling: that in some of them there is inclusion and in some non-inclusion, so this conflict necessitates the non-inclusion of the end point here in the limited. And the gist of his saying: 'What we said' is apparent. (al-Sanbali) 'The disputed matter' i.e., the elbows, from which category – i.e., from the category of the end point that enters or from the category of the end point that does not enter. (al-Qamar) 'Then he has admitted his ignorance' so it is said to him: 'Do not make your ignorance a proof against others.' (al-Qamar) 'Precedes' i.e., he said: legal reasoning by negation. (al-Qamar) 'Where it is not present' i.e., that added description in the branch, so the consideration of the description for obligating the ruling in the branch falls, so nothing remains after it except the comprehensive matter that does not stand by itself for establishing the ruling, and the ruling is not extended by it. (al-Qamar) 'Like his statement' etc.: It is indicated that this example is hypothetical, for the one who says: 'Touching the penis is an event nullifying ablution' does not say this, but has other evidence, and therefore the author said: 'Like their statement' and did not attribute this statement to a group, but in 'al-Kashf' that this is the statement of some of al-Shafi'i's companions who have not smelled the scent of fiqh. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul al-fiqh rule explaining why conflicting similarities (ta'arud al-ashbah) cannot serve as a valid basis for legal reasoning (ta'lil). The author begins by stating the principle: the apparent (zahir) is sufficient for both repelling (daf') a claim and binding (ilzam) someone, so there is no need to resort to conflicting similarities. He illustrates with two fiqh examples. First, in pre-emption (shuf'a), the neighbor's claim is based on apparent ownership (yad), which simultaneously repels the seller's claim and binds the buyer. Second, regarding a missing person (mafqud), Hanafis rule that he is considered alive for his own property (so his wealth is not divided among heirs) but dead regarding inheriting from someone else, because istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity) only repels heirs from claiming his property, not binds them to inherit. The gloss clarifies that this shows istishab is not a proof (hujja) in itself but only a repelling tool. The author then addresses specific counterarguments. The first is Zufar's analogy about ghayat (end points): he claimed that just as some end points (like 'to the end' of a book) are included while others (like 'until night' in fasting) are excluded, similarly the elbows might be excluded from washing the hand. The Hanafi response is that doubt (shakk) does not establish anything; acting on doubt is acting without evidence. Moreover, the doubt itself arises from conflicting similarities, which are also contingent and need evidence. The argument leads to an infinite regress or ignorance. Second, the passage critiques arguments that cling to a comprehensive attribute that only becomes valid with an additional distinguishing description (wasf) that is absent in the branch, making the analogy invalid. The example given is the Shafi'i claim that touching the penis nullifies ablution by analogy to urine, but the distinguishing description (being a source of ritual impurity) is not present in the branch. The author notes that this example is hypothetical and not actually held by sound Shafi'i jurists. Throughout, the passage maintains that conflicting similarities do not constitute a valid legal cause (illa) and that Hanafi reliance on apparent (zahir) and istishab is methodologically sound.

Key Terms
تعارض الأشباه (ta'arud al-ashbah): The conflict of two or more similarities (ashbah) that could each be used to attach a disputed case to a legal principle, but which contradict each other, thus providing no certain ruling.
الظاهر (al-zahir): The apparent evidence or prima facie indication that is sufficient for legal judgment, serving both to repel claims and to bind obligations.
الاستصحاب (istishab): Presumption of continuity of a previous state (e.g., life, ownership) until evidence changes it. In this passage, it is considered only repelling (daf') not binding (ilzam).
الدفع والإلزام (al-daf' wa al-ilzam): Two functions of legal proof: repelling a claim (daf') and binding someone to an obligation (ilzam). The zahir can serve both, but istishab only repels.
الغاية والمغيا (al-ghayah wa al-mughayya): The end point (ghayah) and the thing limited (mughayya). In legal interpretation, some end points are included in the ruling of the limited, others are excluded. Used in the example of fasting until night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle in this passage, why is istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity) not sufficient to make a missing person inherit from his testator?
A) Because istishab is only suitable for repelling (daf') claims, not for binding (ilzam) obligations.
B) Because istishab is not a proof at all according to any school.
C) Because the missing person's death is established with certainty.
D) Because inheritance is based on apparent ownership (zahir), not on presumption.

Key Takeaway
Conflicting similarities create doubt and cannot serve as a valid legal cause; Hanafi usul relies on clear evidence (zahir) and limits istishab to repelling claims only.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
Invalidity of a Disputed Description for Causal Reasoning
Explains why a disputed description cannot serve as the cause in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to EXPLAIN why a disputed description (wasf mukhtalaf fih) cannot serve as the cause (illah) in qiyas and APPLY the Hanafi principle of mu'aradah al-fasid bi al-fasid.

Core Idea
A cause must be undisputed; a contested description invalidates the analogy.

In usul al-fiqh, the validity of analogical reasoning depends on the suitability of the cause (illah). When the very description used as the cause is disputed—whether it actually produces the legal effect—the qiyas collapses. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi critique of a Shafi'i analogy regarding touching the private part and wudu, and extracts the broader principle that a disputed description cannot ground a valid qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i analogy
The Shafi'i argue that touching the private part (mas al-faraj) invalidates wudu by analogy to touching it while urinating, since both involve touching. The claimed illa is 'touching the private part'.
2
Analyze the logical flaw
The Hanafis point out that if the condition 'urine' is ignored, the analogy equates the thing to itself—touching is simply touching—which is circular. If the condition is considered, then a distinction (urine) exists between asl and far', making the analogy invalid.
This is a classic case of qiyas fasid.
3
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis counter using the Quranic verse (9:108) praising those who perform istinja' with water, which necessarily involves touching the private part. If touching were a hadath, Allah would not praise them. This is a mu'aradah al-fasid bi al-fasid—countering a corrupt analogy with another argument that highlights the flaw.
The Hanafi argument does not directly prove the non-invalidity, but exposes the weakness of the Shafi'i analogy.
4
Derive the general principle
From this, the Hanafi usul principle is established: a description whose causal status is contested (mukhtalaf fih) cannot serve as the illah in qiyas. The illah must be agreed upon or at least suitable.
5
Apply to a second example
The text applies the same principle to the case of kitaba al-hala (immediate payment contract). The Shafi'i attempt to analogize it to kitaba with wine is rejected because the disputed description 'lack of preventing kaffarah' is contested.
This reinforces that the principle extends beyond the wudu case.

Chapter of Analogy. Exposition on the unsuitability of the disputed description for causal reasoning: That touching the private part is an event (hadath) just as if one touches it while urinating. This is a corrupt analogy because if one does not consider the condition of urine in the analogized-upon (asl), it would be analogy of the thing on itself, which is impossible; and if one considers that condition, then there is a distinction between the original and the branch, since in the original the invalidator is urine, which is not present in the branch. The Hanafis countered this analogy with a corrupt vs. corrupt response, saying: Allah praised those who use water for istinja' in His saying: 'In it are men who love to purify themselves' (al-Tawba:108), and there is no doubt that there is touching of the private part in that, so if it were an event, He would not have praised them. And this is as you see. (Commentary: meaning touching the private part, etc.) (Then continuation about kitaba al-hala and further commentary.)
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule exposition on the unsuitability of a disputed description for causal reasoning. The text presents a Shafi'i analogy that claims touching the private part invalidates wudu by analogy to touching it while urinating. The Hanafis reject this as a corrupt qiyas because it either equates the thing with itself or introduces a distinguishing factor. They counter with a Quranic verse praising those who use water for istinja', implying that touching the private part during istinja' does not invalidate wudu, otherwise they would not be praised. The commentary further explains the concept of disputed description and applies it to the case of kitaba al-hala (immediate payment emancipation contract), where the Shafi'is analogize it to kitaba with wine. The Hanafis argue that the corrupt nature of the wine contract is due to wine itself, not the lack of preventing kaffarah, so the analogy fails. The key point is that a description whose causal status is contested cannot be used as the 'illah in a valid analogy.

Key Terms
وصف (wasf): A description or attribute used as the potential cause (illah) for a legal ruling in analogy.
قياس فاسد (qiyas fasid): A corrupt analogy that fails due to logical flaw or improper attribution.
تعليل (ta'lil): The process of identifying and applying the effective cause (illah) to derive a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Shafi'i used a Quranic verse incorrectly.
B) Because the analogy either equated the thing with itself or introduced a distinguishing factor (urine).
C) Because touching the private part is not considered a hadath in any case.
D) Because the Hanafis reject all analogies based on istihsan.

Key Takeaway
A description whose causal status is contested cannot be used as the effective cause (illah) in analogical reasoning; such a qiyas is fasid (corrupt).

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Why a Corrupt Description Cannot Be Used in Qiyas
Explaining the self-evident invalidity of a description used in analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a description that is undoubtedly corrupt in a qiyas argument and explain why it invalidates the analogy according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
An analogy built on a self-evidently corrupt description collapses immediately.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar explains a critical principle of Hanafi usul: a description (wasf) that is obviously invalid cannot serve as the cause (illah) in qiyas. The Hanafis illustrate this by critiquing the Shafi'i analogy regarding prayer with three verses. Understanding this principle sharpens your ability to evaluate the validity of analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Description (Wasf) Used as the Alleged Illah
Locate in the passage the specific attribute that the Shafi'is claim as the cause for the ruling. In this case, it is 'deficiency in number from seven' (ناقص العدد عن سبعة).
This is the description that the Hanafis will reject.
2
Determine Whether the Description Is Self-Evidently Corrupt
Check if the description has any established effect (athar) on the ruling in the original case. The Hanafis argue that deficiency from seven has no impact on the validity of prayer; therefore, it is a corrupt description.
A corrupt description is one that is intuitively irrelevant to the ruling.
3
Explain Why the Description Fails as a Cause
The true reason for the invalidity of a recitation less than a verse is that it is not considered Qur'anic recitation, not the number itself. Hence, using the number as a cause is invalid.
The Hanafi response exposes the logical gap in the Shafi'i analogy.
4
Recognize the Outcome: The Qiyas Is Invalid
Since the description is corrupt, the analogy is deemed 'qiyas badihi' (self-evidently invalid) and is rejected without detailed refutation.
This is a Hanafi tool to dismiss flawed reasoning quickly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

القياس بديهي
فإن هذا القياس إلخ : أي احتجت الشافعية في هذا القياس بوصف كون الكتابة غير مانع من التكفير على فساد الكتابة الحالة قياسًا لها على الكتابة بالخبر بجامع كون الكتابتين غير مانع من التكفير فيجب على الشافعية أن يثبتوا أن سبب جواز الكتابة المؤجّلة عند الحنفية هو كونها مانعة من التكفير ليلزم على ذلك فساد الكتابة الحالة لعدم وجود سبب جواز الكتابة فيها أي كونها مانعة؛ لأنها ليست بمانعة فافهم. (السنبلي)
آيات
Exposition on the unsuitability of the description that is undoubtedly corrupt for causal reasoning: And arguing by that which is undoubtedly corrupt is connected to what precedes, i.e., like consistency in invalidity. Arguing by a description that is undoubtedly corrupt, rather it is self-evident, like their saying (the Shafi'is) regarding the obligation and impermissibility of prayer with three verses: they are deficient in number from seven, i.e., from Surah al-Fatiha, so prayer is not performed with it just as less than a verse is not performed with it for that reason. This is corruption because the deficiency from seven has no effect on the invalidity of prayer; rather it was not permissible (the prayer) because the Fatiha is seven verses. The analogy is self-evident. Then commentary on the previous analogy about kitaba al-hala, etc.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage demonstrates the invalidity of using a description that is self-evidently corrupt as the cause for a ruling in analogy. The Shafi'i argument claims that praying with three verses is invalid because it is less than seven verses (the number of verses in Surah al-Fatiha), analogizing to the fact that less than a full verse is invalid. The Hanafis point out that the deficiency from seven has no bearing on the validity of prayer; rather, the validity depends on whether a complete verse of Qur'an is recited. The attribute 'less than seven' is not a valid cause. The commentary then ties this back to the previous discussion on kitaba al-hala, explaining that the Shafi'i use of the attribute 'not preventing kaffarah' as a cause for invalidity is similarly flawed because the corrupt nature of the wine contract is due to wine itself, not the lack of prevention. The key lesson is that a description whose corruption is obvious cannot serve as the illah.

Key Terms
وصف لا شك في فساده (wasf la shakka fi fasadihi): A description that is undoubtedly corrupt and self-evidently invalid as a cause for a ruling.
قياس بديهي (qiyas badihi): A self-evident analogy that is obviously invalid due to the corrupt nature of the description used.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because three verses are sufficient for prayer.
B) Because the description used has no bearing on the ruling.
C) Because the Hanafis forbid analogies in prayer.
D) Because the Shafi'is used a non-Qur'anic verse.

Key Takeaway
An analogy based on a description that is self-evidently corrupt cannot stand; the description must be a valid cause with a demonstrable effect on the ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
beginner
6 min
Invalidity of a Corrupt Description as an Illah in Qiyas
Critique of a Shafi'i qiyas using a clearly invalid description

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a corrupt description (wasf fāsid) in qiyas and explain why it fails as an illah, using the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on kitāba with wine.

Core Idea
A description that is clearly not the true cause invalidates the entire analogy.

The Hanafīs reject qiyas that relies on an attribute that is obviously not the effective cause. In this lesson, we examine a Shāfi‘ī argument that immediate writing (kitāba) is invalid by analogy with writing for wine because both fail to prevent expiation (takfīr). The Hanafī response shows that the real cause is wine's non-value, not failure to prevent expiation, and that writing never prevents expiation anyway. Thus the shared attribute is corrupt, breaking the analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shāfi‘ī qiyas
The Shāfi‘īs analogize immediate writing (far‘) to writing with wine (aṣl) claiming both do not prevent expiation. State the proposed illah: ‘not preventing expiation’.
Write clearly: aṣl = writing with wine, far‘ = immediate writing, illah = man‘ takfīr.
2
Analyze the true cause in the aṣl
According to Hanafīs, the invalidity of the wine contract is because wine is not valuable property (mutaqawwim), not because of expiation prevention. This refutes the shared attribute.
The text says: ‘فساد الكتابة بالخمر إنما هو لأجل الخمر، لا لعدم منعها التكفير’
3
Check the far‘ for the proposed illah
Hanafīs hold that writing (kitāba) never prevents expiation, whether immediate or deferred. So the far‘ lacks the illah altogether; there is no commonality.
The text says: ‘والكتابة عندنا لا تمنع من التكفير مطلقا’
4
Understand the burden of proof on the opponent
The Shāfi‘īs must prove that deferred writing does prevent expiation for the analogy to hold. Since they cannot, the description is corrupt and the qiyas invalid.
‘فلا بد للخصم من إقامة الدليل على أن الكتابة المؤجلة تمنع من التكفير’
5
Apply the general principle
An analogy using a description whose corruption is evident (badīhī) is automatically invalid. No further argument needed; it is like uniformity (itṭirād) in nullity.
The commentator says: ‘بل هو بديهي لا حاجة إلى ذكره’

لأنها سبع آيات
القياس بديهي
فإن هذا القياس إلخ : أي احتجت الشافعية في هذا القياس بوصف كون الكتابة غير مانع من التكفير على فساد الكتابة الحالة قياسًا لها على الكتابة بالخبر بجامع كون الكتابتين غير مانع من التكفير فيجب على الشافعية أن يثبتوا أن سبب جواز الكتابة المؤجّلة عند الحنفية هو كونها مانعة من التكفير ليلزم على ذلك فساد الكتابة الحالة لعدم وجود سبب جواز الكتابة فيها أي كونها مانعة؛ لأنها ليست بمانعة فافهم. (السنبلي) إنما هو لأجل الخمر لأن الخمر ليس بمال متقوّم عندنا. (القمر) لا تمنع أي قبل أداء شيء من بدل الكتابة، كذا في "الدر المختار". (القمر) من التكفير أي من إعتاق العبد المكاتب عن الكفارة. (القمر) على ما قبله أي قوله التعليل بالنفي. بل هو : أي لبطلان الاحتجاج بوصف لا شك في فساده بديهي لا حاجة إلى ذكره، وإنما ذكره للتنبيه على أن بعض استدلالات المخالف من هذا القبيل. (القمر) لأجل ذلك: أي لأجل النقصان من السبعة (القمر) إذ لا أثر للنقصان إلخ أي لا عندنا ولا عند الشافعي ليه أما عندنا فظاهر، وأما عند الشافعي ، فلأن قراءة الفاتحة فرض عنده ، وهي سبع آيات، أما لو قرأ سبع أخرى سوى الفاتحة بطل الصلاة عنده، فلا دخل لسبع الآيات في صحة الصلاة (القمر) وإنما لم تُجز إلخ: هذا دفع سؤال ظاهر يرد علينا من أنكم لم تقولون بعدم أجزاء الصلاة بقراءة ما دون الآية فيها؟ فقال محيبا لذلك: وإنما لم ،تجز أي وجه عدم أجزاء ما دون الآية ليس ذالك، بل هو غيره من كونه لا يسمى قرآنا. (السنبلي)
آيات

باب القياس
٤٥
بيان عدم صلاحية الوصف الذي....
بما دون الآية؛ لأنه لا يسمى قرآنًا في العرف وإن سمي به في اللغة. لوجود القراءة والاحتجاج بلا دليل عطف على ما قبله أي مثل الاطراد في البطلان الاحتجاج بلا دليل
لأجل النفي بأن يقول هذا الحكم غير ثابت؛ لأنه لا دليل عليه، فإن ادعى أنه غير ثابت في ذهن المستدلّ فلا شك في جوازه؛ لأن عدم وجدانه الدليل يقتضي عدم وجدانه أي المستدل الحكم في علمه، وإن ادعى أنه غير ثابت في نفس الأمر لعدم وجدان الدليل عليه
فاختلفوا فيه؛ فقيل: هو جائزة لقوله تعالى: ﴿قُلْ لا أَجِدُ فِي مَا أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ مُحَرَّمَا الآية، (الأنعام: ١٤٥) فإنه تعالى علم نبيه الاحتجاج بلا أجد دليلاً على عدم حرمته، وقيل: جائز في
الشرعيات دون العقليات؛ لأن مدّعي النفي والإثبات في العقليات مدعي حقيقة الوجود والعدم، فلا بد له من دليل، ولا يكفي عدم الدليل بخلاف الشرعيات؛ فإنها ليست كذلك، وعند الجمهور ليس بحجة أصلاً، لا في النفي ولا في الإثبات؛
اللغة: أي بالقرآن لوجود القراءة فيه أيضًا. (المحشي على ما قبله أي قوله: التعليل بالنفي (القمر) بأن يقول: أي المجتهد بعد البحث والتفتيش التام إذا لم يجد دليلًا لهذا الحكم إلخ. (القمر) وإن ادعى أنه غير إلخ أي يقول أو يعتقد أنه ليس من الله تعالى (القمر) فقيل: القائل بعض الشافعية، ومنهم القاضي البيضاوي، كذا قيل. (القمر) محرمًا: أي طعامًا محرمًا عَلَى طَاعِمٍ يَطْعَمُهُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَيْتَةً أَوْ دَماً مَسْفُو حالة (الأنعام: ١٤٥) الآية. (القمر) فإنه تعالى علم نبيه إلخ ونحن نقول: إن الاحتجاج بلا دليل من الشارع صحيح؛ لأن علمه محيط بالأدلة، وهو الشارع للأحكام والواضع للأدلة، فشهادته على عدم الدليل الموجب للحرمة دليل للقطع على عدم الدليل، فإن الشارع ليس ساهيًا ولا عاجزًا، بخلاف البشر فإن السهو والعجز كذا قال المصنف له في شرحه . (القمر) على عدم حرمته أي حرمة الطعام سوى المستثناة. (القمر)
يلازمهم، دون العقليات: أي يجب على النافي إقامة الدليل في العقليات دون الشرعيات. (القمر) ليست كذلك أي فإن الشرعيات ليست ،کالعقليات فمدارها على النقل. (القمر) وعند الجمهور أي من أصحابنا والشافعية ليس بحجة أصلاً، فإن عدم وجدان الدليل لا يوجب انتفاء الدليل في الواقع ولا انتفاء المدلول فيه فإذا لم يجد المجتهد بعد البحث التام دليلا على الحكم فيقول: إنه لا حكم عليه من الشارع لا بالنفي ولا بالإثبات لا أن يقول إن نفي هذا الحكم من الشارع، فإنه لا دليل عليه (القمر)
Chapter of Qiyas
44
Exposition of the invalidity of the description that...
For this analogy is incomplete; because the invalidity of the writing (kitāba) with wine is only due to the wine, not due to its not preventing expiation, and writing according to us does not prevent expiation at all, whether it is immediate or deferred. So the opponent must present evidence that deferred writing prevents expiation so that immediate writing becomes invalid due to the lack of prevention of expiation.
Exposition of the invalidity of a description whose corruption is not doubted for ta'līl] And arguing with that whose corruption is not doubted is conjuncted to the previous, i.e., like uniformity (itṭirād) in invalidity is arguing with a description whose corruption is not doubted, rather it is obvious, like their statement (i.e., the Shāfi‘īs) concerning the obligation and impermissibility of prayer with three verses: three, deficient in number from seven, i.e., from Sūrat al-Fātiḥa, so prayer is not performed with it, just as less than a verse is not performed with prayer for that reason. For this is corruption; since there is no effect of deficiency from seven in the corruption of prayer, and rather it is not permissible because al-Fātiḥa is seven verses. The analogy is obvious. "For this analogy etc.": i.e., the Shāfi‘īs argued in this analogy with the description of writing not preventing expiation to show the invalidity of immediate writing by analogy with writing with wine, based on the commonality that both writings do not prevent expiation. So the Shāfi‘īs must prove that the cause of permissibility of deferred writing according to the Ḥanafīs is that it prevents expiation, so that the invalidity of immediate writing follows due to the absence of the cause of permissibility of writing in it, i.e., its being preventive; because it is not preventive. (al-Sunbulī) It is only due to wine because wine is not a valuable property according to us. (al-Qamar) It does not prevent i.e., before paying anything of the writing's substitute, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtār. (al-Qamar) From expiation i.e., from emancipating the mukātab slave for expiation. (al-Qamar) On the previous i.e., his statement: ta'līl by negation. Rather it is: i.e., the invalidity of arguing with a description whose corruption is not doubted is obvious, no need to mention it; rather it is mentioned to alert that some arguments of the opponent are of this type. (al-Qamar) For that i.e., for the deficiency from seven (al-Qamar) Since there is no effect of deficiency etc. i.e., not according to us nor according to al-Shāfi‘ī? As for us, it is apparent; as for al-Shāfi‘ī, because recitation of al-Fātiḥa is obligatory according to him, and it is seven verses. But if he recites seven others besides al-Fātiḥa, prayer is invalid according to him, so the number seven has no bearing on the validity of prayer. (al-Qamar) "And rather it was not permissible etc.": This is a rebuttal of an apparent objection against us that why do you say that prayer with less than a verse is not valid? So he answers: the reason for the impermissibility of less than a verse is not that, but rather something else: that it is not called Qur'an. (al-Sunbulī)
Verses

[PAGE_046]
Chapter of Qiyas
45
Exposition of the invalidity of the description which...
With less than a verse; because it is not called Qur'an in custom even if it is called so in language. Due to the presence of recitation. And arguing without evidence is conjuncted to the previous, i.e., like uniformity in invalidity is arguing without evidence.
For the purpose of negation, by saying: this ruling is not established because there is no evidence for it. If he claims it is not established in the mind of the arguer, then there is no doubt about its permissibility; because his not finding evidence necessitates his not finding the ruling in his knowledge. And if he claims it is not established in reality due to not finding evidence for it, then they differed on it: It is said it is permissible based on His statement: {Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden...} (al-An‘ām 6:145) For He taught His Prophet arguing by 'I do not find' as evidence for its non-prohibition. And it is said it is permissible in shar‘ī matters but not in rational matters; because the claimant of negation and affirmation in rational matters claims the reality of existence and non-existence, so he must provide evidence, and lack of evidence is insufficient, contrary to shar‘ī matters; for they are not like that. And according to the majority (jumhūr), it is not a proof at all, neither in negation nor in affirmation.
Language: i.e., by the Qur'an because recitation is present in it as well. (al-Muḥashshī on the previous i.e., his statement: ta'līl by negation (al-Qamar) By saying: i.e., the mujtahid after complete research and investigation when he does not find evidence for this ruling etc. (al-Qamar) And if he claims it is not etc. i.e., he says or believes it is not from Allah. (al-Qamar) It is said: the one who says so is some of the Shāfi‘īs, among them al-Qāḍī al-Bayḍāwī, it is said. (al-Qamar) Forbidden: i.e., food forbidden to a person who eats it except if it is carrion or spilled blood... (al-An‘ām 6:145) the verse. (al-Qamar) For He taught His Prophet etc. And we say: arguing without evidence from the Lawgiver is valid; because His knowledge encompasses the evidences, and He is the Legislator of rulings and the Placer of evidences, so His testimony on the lack of evidence requiring prohibition is decisive proof of the lack of evidence, for the Lawgiver is neither forgetful nor incapable, unlike humans, for forgetfulness and incapacity exist in them. Thus said the author in his commentary. (al-Qamar) On its non-prohibition i.e., the prohibition of food other than the exceptions. (al-Qamar)
It is incumbent on them, not in rational matters: i.e., the claimant of negation must produce evidence in rational matters, but not in shar‘ī matters. (al-Qamar) They are not like that i.e., shar‘ī matters are not like rational matters; their basis is transmission. (al-Qamar) And according to the majority (jumhūr) i.e., from our scholars and the Shāfi‘īs, it is not a proof at all. For not finding evidence does not necessitate the non-existence of evidence in reality nor the non-existence of the indicated (madlūl) in it. So if the mujtahid after thorough research does not find evidence for a ruling, he says: there is no ruling from the Lawgiver regarding it, neither negation nor affirmation; he does not say that the negation of this ruling is from the Lawgiver, because there is no evidence for it. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Qiyas (analogy) addresses two types of flawed arguments in legal reasoning: (1) using a description that is evidently corrupt as a basis for analogy, and (2) arguing from the mere absence of evidence (iḥtijāj bi-lā dalīl). The author first critiques a Shāfi‘ī analogy regarding the validity of a slave's writing contract (kitāba) with wine. The Shāfi‘īs argued that immediate writing is invalid by analogy with writing for wine, claiming both writings do not prevent the master from expiating a vow (takfīr). The Hanafīs respond that the invalidity of the wine contract is due to wine not being valuable property, not because it does not prevent expiation. According to the Hanafī school, writing (whether immediate or deferred) does not prevent expiation at all before any payment. Thus, the Shāfi‘īs must prove that deferred writing prevents expiation to draw a valid analogy—something they cannot do. This shows that using a description that is clearly not the true cause (illah) makes the analogy invalid. The second topic concerns arguing without evidence, i.e., claiming a ruling is unestablished because no evidence is found. The text presents three views: some Shāfi‘īs (e.g., al-Qāḍī al-Bayḍāwī) allow it, citing the Prophet's use of 'I do not find' in the Qur'an (6:145) to argue against prohibition. Others restrict it to shar‘ī matters (where reliance on transmitted evidence is key), not rational matters. The majority (including both Hanafīs and Shāfi‘īs) hold it is not a proof at all—absence of evidence does not prove absence of ruling; the mujtahid can only say he has found no ruling, not that the ruling is negated by the Lawgiver. Throughout, the commentary clarifies that the Hanafī position on the kitāba issue is that both immediate and deferred writing do not prevent expiation (a ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah as per al-Durr al-Mukhtār). The discussion on arguing without evidence touches on key usul categories: the validity of negative claims (al-‘adam al-aṣlī) and the burden of proof.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in usul al-fiqh, used to extend a ruling from an original case (aṣl) to a new case (far‘) based on a shared effective cause (illah).
وصف فاسد (waṣf fāsid): A description or attribute that is clearly not the true effective cause (illah) in qiyas; using it invalidates the analogy.
مانع التكفير (māni‘ al-takfīr): Something that prevents the master from using the slave for expiation (takfīr). In the kitāba context, it refers to the slave's contract preventing the master from emancipating him as expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafī school, what is the actual cause of the invalidity of a writing contract made with wine?
A) The contract fails to prevent expiation (takfīr).
B) Wine is not considered valuable property (mutaqawwim).
C) Writing in exchange for wine is a form of gambling.
D) The contract is deferred, not immediate.

Key Takeaway
Using a description that is clearly not the true illah invalidates the entire qiyas; the Hanafī school demands that the illah be the actual effective cause in the original case.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
beginner
6 min
Arguing Without Evidence (al-Ihtijaj bi-la Dalil)
Discussion of the validity of arguing by absence of evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scholarly positions on ihtijaj bi-la dalil and identify the Hanafi (jumhur) position, explaining why absence of evidence does not prove absence of ruling.

Core Idea
Absence of evidence does not equal evidence of absence; the mujtahid can only say 'no evidence found', not 'ruling is negated'.

This lesson explores the controversial method of arguing that a ruling is unestablished simply because no evidence is found for it. The text presents three views: some Shāfi‘īs (including al-Qāḍī al-Bayḍāwī) permit it, citing the Prophet's use of 'I do not find' in the Qur’ān (6:145); others restrict it to shar‘ī matters; and the majority (jumhūr) of both Hanafīs and Shāfi‘īs reject it entirely. Understanding this debate clarifies the burden of proof in ijtihād and the limits of negative claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being debated
The claim is: A ruling is not established (non-existent) because no evidence for it is found. This is called iḥtijāj bi-lā dalīl.
The text says: 'بأن يقول هذا الحكم غير ثابت؛ لأنه لا دليل عليه'
2
Distinguish two interpretations
If the claimant says it is unestablished in his own knowledge (his mental finding), it is permissible because he can only speak from his research. If he claims it is unestablished in reality (from the Lawgiver), then disagreement arises.
The text distinguishes: 'إن ادعى أنه غير ثابت في ذهن المستدلّ' vs. 'وإن ادعى أنه غير ثابت في نفس الأمر'
3
Understand the first view: permissibility
Some (Shāfi‘īs like al-Bayḍāwī) argue it is permissible, citing Qur’ān 6:145 where the Prophet says 'I do not find...' to argue for permissibility. They analogize the mujtahid's lack of evidence to the Prophet's pronouncement.
The text says: 'فقيل: هو جائز لقوله تعالى: {قُلْ لا أَجِدُ...}'
4
Understand the second view: limited to shar‘ī matters
Others restrict it to shar‘ī matters because in rational matters, the burden of proof is heavier. In shar‘ī, the presumption is permissibility (al-aṣl al-ibāḥa), so absence of prohibition evidence may imply permissibility.
The text says: 'وقيل: جائز في الشرعيات دون العقليات'
5
Understand the third view (majority): not a proof
The jumhūr (Hanafīs and Shāfi‘īs) hold it is not a proof at all. Absence of evidence does not mean evidence is absent in reality. The mujtahid can only say he found no ruling, not that the Lawgiver has no ruling.
The text says: 'وعند الجمهور ليس بحجة أصلاً'

بيان عدم صلاحية الوصف الذي.
فإن هذا القياس غير تام؛ لأن فساد الكتابة بالخمر إنما هو لأجل الخمر، لا لعدم منعها التكفير، والكتابة عندنا لا تمنع من التكفير مطلقا، سواء كانت حالة أو مؤجلة، فلا بد للخصم من إقامة الدليل على أن الكتابة المؤجلة تمنع من التكفير حتى تكون الحالة فاسدة لأجل عدم المنع من التكفير.
بيان عدم صلاحية الوصف الذي لا شك في فساده للتعليل] والاحتجاج بما لا شك في فساده عطف على ما قبله أي مثل الاطراد في البطلان الاحتجاج بوصف لا يشك في فساده، بل هو بديهي كقولهم أي الشافعية في وجوب وعدم جواز الصلاة بثلاث آيات الثلاث ناقص العدد عن سبعة، أي عن سورة الفاتحة، فلا تتأدّى به الصلاة كما دون الآية لا يتأدّى به الصلاة لأجل ذلك، فإن هذا الفساد؛ إذ لا أثر للنقصان عن السبعة في فساد الصلاة، وإنما لم تجز

القياس بديهي
فإن هذا القياس إلخ : أي احتجت الشافعية في هذا القياس بوصف كون الكتابة غير مانع من التكفير على فساد الكتابة الحالة قياسًا لها على الكتابة بالخبر بجامع كون الكتابتين غير مانع من التكفير فيجب على الشافعية أن يثبتوا أن سبب جواز الكتابة المؤجّلة عند الحنفية هو كونها مانعة من التكفير ليلزم على ذلك فساد الكتابة الحالة لعدم وجود سبب جواز الكتابة فيها أي كونها مانعة؛ لأنها ليست بمانعة فافهم. (السنبلي) إنما هو لأجل الخمر لأن الخمر ليس بمال متقوّم عندنا. (القمر) لا تمنع أي قبل أداء شيء من بدل الكتابة، كذا في "الدر المختار". (القمر) من التكفير أي من إعتاق العبد المكاتب عن الكفارة. (القمر) على ما قبله أي قوله التعليل بالنفي. بل هو : أي لبطلان الاحتجاج بوصف لا شك في فساده بديهي لا حاجة إلى ذكره، وإنما ذكره للتنبيه على أن بعض استدلالات المخالف من هذا القبيل. (القمر) لأجل ذلك: أي لأجل النقصان من السبعة (القمر) إذ لا أثر للنقصان إلخ أي لا عندنا ولا عند الشافعي ليه أما عندنا فظاهر، وأما عند الشافعي ، فلأن قراءة الفاتحة فرض عنده ، وهي سبع آيات، أما لو قرأ سبع أخرى سوى الفاتحة بطل الصلاة عنده، فلا دخل لسبع الآيات في صحة الصلاة (القمر) وإنما لم تُجز إلخ: هذا دفع سؤال ظاهر يرد علينا من أنكم لم تقولون بعدم أجزاء الصلاة بقراءة ما دون الآية فيها؟ فقال محيبا لذلك: وإنما لم ،تجز أي وجه عدم أجزاء ما دون الآية ليس ذالك، بل هو غيره من كونه لا يسمى قرآنا. (السنبلي)

باب القياس
٤٥
بيان عدم صلاحية الوصف الذي....
بما دون الآية؛ لأنه لا يسمى قرآنًا في العرف وإن سمي به في اللغة. لوجود القراءة والاحتجاج بلا دليل عطف على ما قبله أي مثل الاطراد في البطلان الاحتجاج بلا دليل
لأجل النفي بأن يقول هذا الحكم غير ثابت؛ لأنه لا دليل عليه، فإن ادعى أنه غير ثابت في ذهن المستدلّ فلا شك في جوازه؛ لأن عدم وجدانه الدليل يقتضي عدم وجدانه أي المستدل الحكم في علمه، وإن ادعى أنه غير ثابت في نفس الأمر لعدم وجدان الدليل عليه
فاختلفوا فيه؛ فقيل: هو جائزة لقوله تعالى: ﴿قُلْ لا أَجِدُ فِي مَا أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ مُحَرَّمَا الآية، (الأنعام: ١٤٥) فإنه تعالى علم نبيه الاحتجاج بلا أجد دليلاً على عدم حرمته، وقيل: جائز في
الشرعيات دون العقليات؛ لأن مدّعي النفي والإثبات في العقليات مدعي حقيقة الوجود والعدم، فلا بد له من دليل، ولا يكفي عدم الدليل بخلاف الشرعيات؛ فإنها ليست كذلك، وعند الجمهور ليس بحجة أصلاً، لا في النفي ولا في الإثبات؛
اللغة: أي بالقرآن لوجود القراءة فيه أيضًا. (المحشي على ما قبله أي قوله: التعليل بالنفي (القمر) بأن يقول: أي المجتهد بعد البحث والتفتيش التام إذا لم يجد دليلًا لهذا الحكم إلخ. (القمر) وإن ادعى أنه غير إلخ أي يقول أو يعتقد أنه ليس من الله تعالى (القمر) فقيل: القائل بعض الشافعية، ومنهم القاضي البيضاوي، كذا قيل. (القمر) محرمًا: أي طعامًا محرمًا عَلَى طَاعِمٍ يَطْعَمُهُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَيْتَةً أَوْ دَماً مَسْفُو حالة (الأنعام: ١٤٥) الآية. (القمر) فإنه تعالى علم نبيه إلخ ونحن نقول: إن الاحتجاج بلا دليل من الشارع صحيح؛ لأن علمه محيط بالأدلة، وهو الشارع للأحكام والواضع للأدلة، فشهادته على عدم الدليل الموجب للحرمة دليل للقطع على عدم الدليل، فإن الشارع ليس ساهيًا ولا عاجزًا، بخلاف البشر فإن السهو والعجز كذا قال المصنف له في شرحه . (القمر) على عدم حرمته أي حرمة الطعام سوى المستثناة. (القمر)
يلازمهم، دون العقليات: أي يجب على النافي إقامة الدليل في العقليات دون الشرعيات. (القمر) ليست كذلك أي فإن الشرعيات ليست ،کالعقليات فمدارها على النقل. (القمر) وعند الجمهور أي من أصحابنا والشافعية ليس بحجة أصلاً، فإن عدم وجدان الدليل لا يوجب انتفاء الدليل في الواقع ولا انتفاء المدلول فيه فإذا لم يجد المجتهد بعد البحث التام دليلا على الحكم فيقول: إنه لا حكم عليه من الشارع لا بالنفي ولا بالإثبات لا أن يقول إن نفي هذا الحكم من الشارع، فإنه لا دليل عليه (القمر)
Chapter of Qiyas
44
Exposition of the invalidity of the description that...
For this analogy is incomplete; because the invalidity of the writing (kitāba) with wine is only due to the wine, not due to its not preventing expiation, and writing according to us does not prevent expiation at all, whether it is immediate or deferred. So the opponent must present evidence that deferred writing prevents expiation so that immediate writing becomes invalid due to the lack of prevention of expiation.
Exposition of the invalidity of a description whose corruption is not doubted for ta'līl] And arguing with that whose corruption is not doubted is conjuncted to the previous, i.e., like uniformity (itṭirād) in invalidity is arguing with a description whose corruption is not doubted, rather it is obvious, like their statement (i.e., the Shāfi‘īs) concerning the obligation and impermissibility of prayer with three verses: three, deficient in number from seven, i.e., from Sūrat al-Fātiḥa, so prayer is not performed with it, just as less than a verse is not performed with prayer for that reason. For this is corruption; since there is no effect of deficiency from seven in the corruption of prayer, and rather it is not permissible because al-Fātiḥa is seven verses. The analogy is obvious. "For this analogy etc.": i.e., the Shāfi‘īs argued in this analogy with the description of writing not preventing expiation to show the invalidity of immediate writing by analogy with writing with wine, based on the commonality that both writings do not prevent expiation. So the Shāfi‘īs must prove that the cause of permissibility of deferred writing according to the Ḥanafīs is that it prevents expiation, so that the invalidity of immediate writing follows due to the absence of the cause of permissibility of writing in it, i.e., its being preventive; because it is not preventive. (al-Sunbulī) It is only due to wine because wine is not a valuable property according to us. (al-Qamar) It does not prevent i.e., before paying anything of the writing's substitute, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtār. (al-Qamar) From expiation i.e., from emancipating the mukātab slave for expiation. (al-Qamar) On the previous i.e., his statement: ta'līl by negation. Rather it is: i.e., the invalidity of arguing with a description whose corruption is not doubted is obvious, no need to mention it; rather it is mentioned to alert that some arguments of the opponent are of this type. (al-Qamar) For that i.e., for the deficiency from seven (al-Qamar) Since there is no effect of deficiency etc. i.e., not according to us nor according to al-Shāfi‘ī? As for us, it is apparent; as for al-Shāfi‘ī, because recitation of al-Fātiḥa is obligatory according to him, and it is seven verses. But if he recites seven others besides al-Fātiḥa, prayer is invalid according to him, so the number seven has no bearing on the validity of prayer. (al-Qamar) "And rather it was not permissible etc.": This is a rebuttal of an apparent objection against us that why do you say that prayer with less than a verse is not valid? So he answers: the reason for the impermissibility of less than a verse is not that, but rather something else: that it is not called Qur'an. (al-Sunbulī)
Verses
